Shahadat — Testimony

6 min
Suspicion from Deficient Testimony
Maxim on suspicion from defective testimony components

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two components of testimony required for credibility and identify which deficiency creates legal suspicion.

Core Idea
A testimony lacking in number or integrity triggers legal suspicion.

In Islamic legal procedure, the credibility of testimony rests on two pillars: the number of witnesses and their moral integrity. This maxim encapsulates that if either pillar is defective, the testimony becomes suspect. Understanding this principle is key to evaluating evidence in a Hanafi court.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Maxim's Claim
The maxim states that suspicion (tuhma) is established by one of the two halves of testimony: number or integrity.
Suspicion does not automatically mean rejection, but requires further scrutiny.
2
Define the Two Components
Number (adad) refers to the required quantity of witnesses (e.g., two males or one male and two females in most cases). Integrity (adala) refers to the moral uprightness and reliability of the witness.
Both components are necessary for full credibility.
3
Apply to Examples
A single witness, even if upright, creates suspicion due to deficient number. A known liar, even if two are present, creates suspicion due to deficient integrity.
Each deficiency independently triggers suspicion.
4
Note the Legal Consequence
Suspicion prompts the court to seek corroboration or an oath; it does not automatically invalidate the testimony but raises a caution.
The burden may shift to the proponent to strengthen the evidence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
اَلتُهُمَةُ ثَبَتَتْ بَأَحَدِ شَطْرَى الشَّهَادَةِ إِمَّا الْعَدَدِ أَوِ الْعَدَالَةِ
Suspicion is established by one of the two halves of testimony: either number or integrity (uprightness).
Source pages p. 6

Commentary
This maxim relates to the law of evidence. For testimony to be credible, it must have both sufficient number (e.g., two male witnesses) and integrity (the witnesses must be upright, 'adl). If either is lacking, suspicion (tuhma) arises regarding the testimony's reliability. For example, a single witness creates suspicion due to insufficient number; a known liar creates suspicion due to lack of integrity.

Key Terms
التُّهُمَةُ (al-tuhma): Suspicion or doubt about the credibility of testimony.
شَطْرَى الشَّهَادَةِ (shaṭrā al-shahāda): The two essential components of testimony: number and integrity.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What are the two components of testimony mentioned in the maxim?
A) Age and gender
B) Number and integrity
C) Wealth and status
D) Memory and honesty

Key Takeaway
A testimony lacking in number or integrity raises legal suspicion, requiring further scrutiny before acceptance.

Shahadat — Testimony

6 min
Five Maxims on the Law of Testimony
List of five legal maxims on testimony and proof

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the five maxims on testimony and explain their application in judicial evidence.

Core Idea
Judgment is built on proof; testimony is not self-obligating; possession is the strongest evidence of ownership.

This lesson presents five foundational maxims from the Hanafi Book of Testimony. They underlie the entire law of evidence, guiding judges on proof, obligation to testify, and inference of ownership. Commit them to memory as legal anchors.

Guided Path
1
Identify each maxim
Locate each maxim by its number (61-65) and read the Arabic text. Note that the numbers are given in the passage.
2
Translate literally and explain meaning
For each maxim, understand the literal translation and then the legal implication. Example: Maxim 61 means every judgment must have a valid proof (ḥujjah).
3
Connect to practical scenarios
Think of a courtroom scenario where each maxim would apply. For maxim 65, a judge presumes ownership from possession.
4
Relate the maxims to each other
Note that maxim 61 is overarching; maxims 62 and 64 deal with similarity (one favor to another, one line to another); maxim 63 with obligation; maxim 65 with evidence of ownership.
5
Summarize the takeaway for each
For each maxim, articulate the key legal principle in one sentence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الشهادة (٦١) الْقَضَاءُ مَبْنَاهُ عَلَى الْحُجَّةِ (۶۲) إِنَّ النَّعْمَةَ تَشْبَهُ النَّعْمَةَ (۶۳) اَلشَّهَادَةُ غَيْرُ مُوْجِبَةٍ بِنَفْسِهَا (۶۴) الْخَطُّ يَشْبَهُ الْخَطَّ (۲۵) الْيَدُ أَقْصَى مَا يُسْتَدَلُّ بِهِ الْمِلْكُ
Book of testimony. (61) Judgment is built upon proof. (62) Indeed, a favor resembles a favor. (63) Testimony is not obligatory by itself. (64) The line resembles the line. (65) The hand (possession) is the maximum by which ownership is inferred.
Source pages p. 7

Commentary
This passage presents five maxims from the book of testimony. The first maxim asserts that all judicial decisions must be based on evidence (ḥujjah). The second maxim indicates that one favor (like a gift) can be compared to another favor for legal purposes. The third maxim means that giving testimony is not an individual obligation (fard 'ayn) in itself — it becomes obligatory only when one is called upon or when rights are at stake. The fourth maxim states that a signature or handwriting can be compared to another signature for identification purposes. The fifth maxim says that the strongest evidence of ownership is possession (yad) — being in control of an object is the primary indicator of ownership in disputes.

Key Terms
اليد أقصى ما يستدل به الملك (al-yadu aqṣā mā yustadallu bihi al-milk): Possession is the strongest indicator of ownership in legal inference
الشهادة غير موجبة بنفسها (al-shahādatu ghayru mūjibatin bi-nafsihā): Testimony does not create an obligation by itself — it requires a request or necessity

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to maxim (63), which of the following is true about testimony?
A) Testimony is always obligatory on every Muslim.
B) Testimony is not obligatory by itself — it becomes obligatory when needed.
C) Testimony is only obligatory for men.
D) Testimony is never obligatory.

Key Takeaway
These five maxims are the bedrock of Hanafi evidence law: judgment by proof, obligation of testimony only when needed, and possession as primary evidence of ownership.

Shahadat — Testimony

Six Maxims on Witness Acceptance
List of six maxims on acceptance and rejection of witnesses

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state and explain the six Hanafi maxims regarding the acceptance and rejection of testimony, and apply them to identify when testimony is admissible.

Core Idea
Testimony is rejected for self-benefit or strong suspicion, but not for heretical belief alone.

This lesson presents six foundational maxims (qawāʿid) that govern the Hanafi law of evidence. These maxims distill centuries of judicial practice into concise rules. Understanding them is essential for any student of fiqh because they appear repeatedly in discussions of witness qualification. The maxims cover self-interest, suspicion, belief-based misconduct, the legal enforceability of sin, confession, and procedural unity.

Guided Path
1
Identify each maxim's core condition
Read the six maxims one by one. For each, determine the condition that leads to acceptance or rejection of testimony. For example, maxim (26) says testimony is rejected when it benefits the witness himself.
The numbers (66–71) correspond to the given sequence; some may be misprinted.
2
Distinguish fisq in belief from fisq in action
Maxim (28) states that transgression in belief does not prevent acceptance. Contrast this with moral turpitude (fisq al-ʿamal), which does disqualify. Understand that the Hanafi school focuses on outward reliability, not theological correctness.
This is a major Hanafi principle: a witness's creed is not investigated unless it leads to dishonesty.
3
Contrast shahāda (testimony) with iqrār (confession)
Maxims (29) and (30) state that fisq (sin) is not subject to legal ruling, but confession is. This means a sinner's testimony may be accepted despite his sin, but a confession must be enforced by the court. Grasp the different legal consequences.
Fisq itself is not punishable unless it involves a ḥadd crime.
4
Apply maxim (31) on unified sitting
If witnesses testify in the same session, any later addition or correction attaches to the original testimony. This procedural maxim affects how evidence is recorded and evaluated.
The term 'mulḥaq' (annexation) refers to supplementary statements.
5
Apply the maxims to a hypothetical scenario
Given a fact pattern, determine which maxim(s) apply and whether testimony is accepted or rejected. Practice integrating multiple maxims.
For example, a witness who is a heretic but truthful in his testimony: maxim (28) says his belief does not disqualify.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب من يُقبل شهادته ومن لا يُقبل (٢٦) اَلشَّهَادَةُ إِذَا كَانَتْ لِنَفْسِهِ مِنْ وَجْهِ لَا تُقْبَلُ (۲۷) الشَّهَادَةُ إِذَا تَمَكَّنَتْ فِيْهَا التُهُمَةُ لَا تُقْبَلُ (۲۸) الْفِسْقُ مِنْ حَيْثُ الْإِعْتِقَادِ غَيْرُ مَانِعِ مِنْ قَبُولِ الشَّهَادَةِ (۲۹) الْفِسْقُ مِمَّا لَا يَدْخُلُ تَحْتَ الْحُكْمِ (۷۰) الْإِقْرَارُ مِمَّا يَدْخُلُ تَحْتَ الْحُكم (۱) الْمَجْلِسُ إِذَا اتَّحَدَ لَحِقَ الْمُلْحَقُ بِأَصْلِ الشَّهَادَةِ
Chapter of who is accepted and who is not accepted. (66) Testimony, when it is for himself from one perspective, is not accepted. (67) Testimony, when suspicion is firmly established in it, is not accepted. (68) Transgression from the standpoint of belief does not prevent acceptance of testimony. (69) Transgression is not subject to legal ruling. (70) Confession is subject to legal ruling. (71) The sitting, when it is unified, the annexation is attached to the original testimony.
Source pages p. 7

Commentary
This passage lists six maxims on witness qualification. The first maxim states that if a witness stands to benefit personally from the testimony, it is rejected. The second says that if strong suspicion of bias or enmity exists, testimony is rejected. The third clarifies that if a person's misconduct is a matter of belief (e.g., he belongs to a deviant sect but does not act immorally), that does not disqualify him. The fourth means that sinful behavior (fisq) as such is not itself subject to criminal punishment — it is a moral failing. The fifth says that a confession (iqrar) does come under the jurisdiction of the judge; the court can enforce it. The sixth means that if witnesses give testimony in the same session, any later addition or correction attaches to the original testimony.

Key Terms
الفسق من حيث الاعتقاد غير مانع (al-fisqu min ḥaythu al-i'tiqādi ghayru māni'in): Misconduct in belief (heresy) does not automatically disqualify a witness if he is truthful and upright in action
التهمة (al-tuhma): Strong suspicion of bias or enmity that taints testimony
المُلحَق (al-mulḥaq): Annexation; an addition or correction made to original testimony

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to maxim (66), when is testimony not accepted?
A) When the witness is a heretic.
B) When the testimony benefits the witness himself.
C) When the witness is a known liar.
D) When the testimony is about a confession.

Key Takeaway
The six Hanafi maxims on testimony provide a practical framework for assessing witness admissibility based on benefit, suspicion, belief, sin, confession, and procedural unity.

Maxim 72: Testimony Required for Inheritance
A ruling about required testimony for inheritance claims.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two conditions required for an heir to claim property based on testimony and apply them to a hypothetical scenario.

Core Idea
Ownership alone is not enough; witnesses must also testify to death and inheritance.

This maxim from the Hanafi fiqh clarifies when an heir can take property based on witness testimony. Simply proving that the deceased owned something is insufficient unless the witnesses also confirm the death and that the property was left as inheritance. This protects against premature claims.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two required testimonies
Read the maxim and list the two facts witnesses must testify to: ownership of the deceased and his death leaving it as inheritance.
2
Understand the legal rationale
Why is ownership alone insufficient? The maxim prevents property from being transferred without proof of death and inheritance, which could lead to disputes.
3
Apply the maxim to a scenario
Given a scenario where witnesses only testify to ownership, determine whether the heir can inherit and explain why.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب الاختلاف في الشهادة (۷۲) اَلْمِلْكُ مَتَى ثَبَتَتْ لِلْمُوْرِثِ لَا يُقْضَى لِلْوَارِثِ بِهِ حَتَّى شَهِدَ الشُّهُودُ أَنَّهُ فَاتَ وَتَرَكَهَا مِيرَانًا لَهُ (٧٣) اَلْجَهَالَةُ فِى الْمُقِرِّ بِهِ لَا تَمْنَعُ صِحَّةَ الْإِقْرَارِ
Chapter of disagreement in testimony. (72) Ownership, when established for the deceased, is not adjudged for the heir until the witnesses testify that he died and left it as inheritance for him. (73) Ignorance about the subject of confession does not prevent the validity of the confession.
Source pages p. 8

Commentary
This passage contains two maxims from the chapter on contradictory testimony. The first maxim addresses a scenario: if witnesses state that the deceased owned an item, the court cannot simply transfer it to the heir unless they also testify that the deceased died and left it as inheritance. This prevents heirs from claiming property based on testimony about ownership alone without proof of death and inheritance. The second maxim states that if a person confesses to something but is vague about what it is (e.g., he says 'I owe a debt' without specifying amount), the confession is still valid; the details can be clarified later.

Key Terms
الجهالة في المقر به لا تمنع صحة الإقرار (al-jahālatu fī al-muqarri bihi lā tamna'u ṣiḥḥata al-iqrār): Unclarity about the specific thing confessed does not invalidate the confession as long as the confession itself is clear

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to maxim (72), what must witnesses testify for an heir to inherit property?
A) That the deceased owned the property.
B) That the deceased died and left it as inheritance.
C) Both that the deceased owned it and that he died leaving it as inheritance.
D) That the heir is the only relative.

Key Takeaway
An heir cannot inherit based solely on ownership testimony; death and inheritance must also be proven.

Maxim 73: Confession Valid Despite Ignorance of the Subject
A ruling about the validity of a confession when the subject is unknown.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why a confession remains valid even if the specific object or amount is unknown, and identify an example.

Core Idea
Unclarity about the thing confessed does not invalidate the confession.

This maxim addresses cases where someone admits to a debt or right but does not specify the exact amount or object. According to Hanafi fiqh, the confession is still valid and binding, with details to be resolved later. This facilitates settlements and prevents people from avoiding liability through vagueness.

Guided Path
1
Recognize the maxim
Read the Arabic maxim and understand its literal meaning: ignorance about the subject of confession does not invalidate the confession.
2
Understand the legal rationale
The confession establishes liability or right. The specific object is a secondary detail that can be clarified later. This prevents a confessor from escaping liability by being vague.
Hanafis view the confession as binding when the intent to confess is clear.
3
Apply the maxim to a scenario
Consider someone saying 'I owe you money' without specifying the amount. Is the confession valid? Apply the maxim.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب الاختلاف في الشهادة (۷۲) اَلْمِلْكُ مَتَى ثَبَتَتْ لِلْمُوْرِثِ لَا يُقْضَى لِلْوَارِثِ بِهِ حَتَّى شَهِدَ الشُّهُودُ أَنَّهُ فَاتَ وَتَرَكَهَا مِيرَانًا لَهُ (٧٣) اَلْجَهَالَةُ فِى الْمُقِرِّ بِهِ لَا تَمْنَعُ صِحَّةَ الْإِقْرَارِ
Chapter of disagreement in testimony. (72) Ownership, when established for the deceased, is not adjudged for the heir until the witnesses testify that he died and left it as inheritance for him. (73) Ignorance about the subject of confession does not prevent the validity of the confession.
Source pages p. 8

Commentary
This passage contains two maxims from the chapter on contradictory testimony. The first maxim addresses a scenario: if witnesses state that the deceased owned an item, the court cannot simply transfer it to the heir unless they also testify that the deceased died and left it as inheritance. This prevents heirs from claiming property based on testimony about ownership alone without proof of death and inheritance. The second maxim states that if a person confesses to something but is vague about what it is (e.g., he says 'I owe a debt' without specifying amount), the confession is still valid; the details can be clarified later.

Key Terms
الجهالة في المقر به لا تمنع صحة الإقرار (al-jahālatu fī al-muqarri bihi lā tamna'u ṣiḥḥata al-iqrār): Unclarity about the specific thing confessed does not invalidate the confession as long as the confession itself is clear
إقرار (iqrār): A legal confession or acknowledgment of a right or liability.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to maxim (73), what is the effect of ignorance about the subject of confession?
A) It makes the confession void.
B) It delays the validity until clarification.
C) It does not prevent the validity of the confession.
D) It requires the confessor to repeat the confession.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, a confession is valid even if the specific subject is unknown; details can be clarified later.

Four Qawaid on Withdrawal from Testimonies and Repentance
Four maxims on retraction of testimony and repentance

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state and apply each of the four maxims on retraction of testimony and repentance, distinguishing the legal effects of each.

Core Idea
Contradiction does not undo a confession; repentance matches the wrong; retraction by some does not undo testimony; damages require equivalence.

This passage presents four concise legal maxims that serve as foundational principles in the Hanafi law of testimony and torts. They govern the effects of a witness or party contradicting themselves, the nature of repentance required for different sins, the persistence of testimony despite partial retraction, and the requirement of equivalence in compensation. Each maxim encapsulates a rule that guides judges and muftis in resolving cases with minimal ambiguity.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Context and Purpose
Recognize that these maxims appear in the Book of Withdrawal from Testimonies, dealing with situations where a person who has given testimony later retracts it. The maxims provide general principles to determine the legal effect of such retractions and related matters.
The chapter is distinct from the general law of evidence; it focuses on post-testimony changes.
2
Analyze Maxim 74: Contradiction and Confession
Understand that if a person makes a confession (iqrar) and later contradicts it (tanāqud), the original confession remains valid. The contradiction does not, by itself, nullify the earlier confession. This is because a clear, voluntary confession is a strong proof, and a mere contradictory statement does not automatically outweigh it.
This maxim applies specifically to confessions, not to other types of testimony.
3
Analyze Maxim 75: Repentance Proportional to Crime
Grasp that repentance must be tailored to the nature of the sin. For sins against Allah (huquq Allah), sincere remorse and a resolve not to return suffice. For sins that involve harm to others (huquq al-ibad), repentance requires making amends, such as returning stolen property or compensating for harm.
This maxim underscores the Hanafi principle that interpersonal rights are not waived by mere verbal repentance.
4
Analyze Maxim 76: Effect of Partial Retraction
When multiple witnesses testify and one or some retract, the testimony of those who remain stands; the retraction does not nullify the entire testimony. The court considers the number and credibility of the remaining witnesses.
The maximum number of retracting witnesses before the testimony collapses depends on the required threshold (e.g., two male witnesses for hudud).
5
Analyze Maxim 77: Liability Requires Equivalence
In cases of liability for damages (tadmeen), the compensation must be equivalent to the loss. If the lost item is fungible (mithli), compensation is in kind; if unique (qimi), compensation is monetary value.
This maxim is a cornerstone of Hanafi tort law and is derived from the Qur'anic principle of 'al-mithlu bil-mithl' (like for like).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الرجوع عن الشهادات (۷۴) اَلتَّناقُضُ لَا يَمْنَعُ صِحَّةَ الْإِقْرَارِ (۷۵) اَلتَّوْبَةُ عَلَى حَسَبِ الْجِنَايَةِ (۶) الْمُعْتَبَرُ فِى بَابِ الرُّجُوعِ بَقَاءُ مَنْ بَقِيَ لَا رُجُوعَ مَنْ رَجَعَ (۷۷) اَلتَّضْمِينُ يَسْتَدْعِى الْمُمَاثَلَةَ
Book of withdrawal from testimonies. (74) Contradiction does not prevent the validity of confession. (75) Repentance is according to the crime. (76) The consideration in the chapter of withdrawal is the remaining of those who remain, not the withdrawal of those who withdraw. (77) Liability (for damages) requires equivalence.
Source pages p. 8

Commentary
This passage lists four maxims on retraction of testimony. The first says that if a person makes a confession and later contradicts it, the initial confession remains valid; the contradiction does not nullify it. The second maxim states that the manner of repentance must match the nature of the sin — for example, if the crime involved harming others, repentance requires compensating them. The third maxim addresses a case where multiple witnesses testify and one retracts; the effect of the retraction does not destroy the testimony of those who persist, so judgment may still be passed based on the remaining witnesses. The fourth maxim means that when a person is liable for damages, the compensation must be equivalent to the loss in kind or value.

Key Terms
التوبة على حسب الجناية (al-tawbatu 'alā ḥasabi al-jināyah): Repentance must be proportionate to the crime; if the crime involves violation of others' rights, those must be rectified
التضمين يستدعي المماثلة (al-taḍmīnu yastad'ī al-mumāthalah): Liability for compensation requires equivalence in kind or value
التناقض لا يمنع صحة الإقرار (al-tanāquḍ lā yamna'u ṣiḥḥata al-iqrār): Contradiction does not prevent the validity of confession
المعتبر في باب الرجوع بقاء من بقي لا رجوع من رجع (al-mu'tabaru fī bābi al-rujū'i baqā'u man baqiya lā rujū'u man raja'a): The consideration in the chapter of withdrawal is the remaining of those who remain, not the withdrawal of those who withdraw

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to maxim (76), what is the guiding principle when some witnesses retract?
A) The retraction of some nullifies the entire testimony.
B) The withdrawal of those who withdraw is considered.
C) The remaining testimony of those who stay is considered, not the retraction of those who retract.
D) The case is dismissed if any witness retracts.

Key Takeaway
The four maxims collectively ensure that once a confession is made, it retains validity; repentance addresses both divine and human rights; testimony persists despite partial retraction; and damages must be equivalent to the loss.

Maxims on the Acceptance of Testimony (Shahadah)
Collection of maxims on testimony admissibility

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state and apply the Hanafi maxims governing when testimony is accepted or rejected.

Core Idea
Testimony is rejected when strong suspicion exists, but sinfulness in belief alone does not disqualify.

These maxims from Al-Hidayah lay the foundation for evaluating witness testimony. The key distinction between suspicion (tuhmah) and sinfulness (fisq) determines admissibility. Understanding these rules is essential for anyone studying Hanafi judicial procedure.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is giving testimony. Maxim 27 states it is not accepted when strong suspicion (tuhmah) is present. Maxim 28 adds that fisq in belief does not prevent acceptance. Maxim 29 clarifies that fisq that does not fall under the judge's ruling is not a bar.
Focus on the precise wording: 'tamakkanat' (firmly present) indicates a high threshold.
2
Understand the unification of session
Maxim (1) [likely 71] says that if the session is unified, any appended testimony is attached to the original. This means additions or clarifications given in the same session are considered part of the initial testimony.
This maxim prevents procedural splitting.
3
Apply the inheritance condition
Maxim 72: For an heir to claim property, witnesses must testify not only that the deceased owned it, but also that he died leaving it as inheritance. This establishes a clear chain of ownership.
Without proof of inheritance, the heir cannot automatically inherit the property.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
اصول ہدایہ ثالث
(۲۷) الشَّهَادَةُ إِذَا تَمَكَّنَتْ فِيْهَا التُهُمَةُ لَا تُقْبَلُ
(۲۸) الْفِسْقُ مِنْ حَيْثُ الْإِعْتِقَادِ غَيْرُ مَانِعِ مِنْ قَبُولِ الشَّهَادَةِ
(۲۹) الْفِسْقُ مِمَّا لَا يَدْخُلُ تَحْتَ الْحُكْمِ
(۷۰) الْإِقْرَارُ مِمَّا يَدْخُلُ تَحْتَ الْحُكم
(۱) الْمَجْلِسُ إِذَا اتَّحَدَ لَحِقَ الْمُلْحَقُ بِأَصْلِ الشَّهَادَةِ
باب الاختلاف في الشهادة
(۷۲) اَلْمِلْكُ مَتَى ثَبَتَتْ لِلْمُوْرِثِ لَا يُقْضَى لِلْوَارِثِ بِهِ حَتَّى شَهِدَ الشُّهُودُ أَنَّهُ فَاتَ وَتَرَكَهَا مِيرَانًا لَهُ
(٧٣) اَلْجَهَالَةُ فِى الْمُقِرِّ بِهِ لَا تَمْنَعُ صِحَّةَ الْإِقْرَارِ
كتاب الرجوع عن الشهادات
(۷۴) اَلتَّناقُضُ لَا يَمْنَعُ صِحَّةَ الْإِقْرَارِ
(۷۵) اَلتَّوْبَةُ عَلَى حَسَبِ الْجِنَايَةِ
(۶) الْمُعْتَبَرُ فِى بَابِ الرُّجُوعِ بَقَاءُ مَنْ بَقِيَ لَا رُجُوعَ مَنْ رَجَعَ
(۷۷) اَلتَّضْمِينُ يَسْتَدْعِى الْمُمَاثَلَةَ
كتاب الوكالة
(۷۸) كُلُّ عَقْدِ يُضِيْفُهُ الْوَكِيْلُ إِلَى نَفْسِهِ فَحُقُوقُهُ يَتَعَلَّقُ بِالْوَكِيْلِ وَمَا هُوَ عَلَى الْعَكْسِ فَحُقُوقُهُ تَتَعَلَّقُ بِالْمُؤَكّل
باب الوكالة بالبيع والشراء
(۷۹) اَلْحَهَالَةُ الْيَسِيْرَةُ تَتَحَمَّلُ فِي الْوَكَالَةِ
(۸۰) الْأَصْلُ فِي الْمُضَارَبَةِ الْعُمُومُ
باب عزل الوكيل
(۸۱) بَقَاءُ الْوَكَالَةِ يَعْتَمِدُ قِيَامَ الْأَمْرِ
(۸۲) اَلْعَزْلُ الْحُكْمِيَّ لَا يَتَوَقَّفُ عَلَى عِلْمِ الْوَكِيلِ
كتاب الدعوى
(۸۳) الْإِلْزَامُ فِي الْمَجْهُولِ لَا يَتَحَقَّقُ
(۸۴) الْإِعْلَامُ بِأَقْصَى مَا يُمْكِنُ شَرُطْ فِي صِحَّةِ الدَّعْوَى
(۸۵) الْقِسْمَةُ تُنَافِي الشَّرُكَةَ
باب اليمين
(٨٦) اَلْكَفَالَةُ بِالنَّفْسِ جَائِزَةٌ عِنْدَنَا لَا عِنْدَ الشَّافِعِي
(۸۷) الْبَيِّنَاتُ لِلْإِثْبَاتِ
باب التحالف
(۸۸) اَلتَّحَالُفُ يَعْتَمِدُ الْاِخْتِلَافَ فِي الْمَعْقُودِ عَلَيْهِ وَالْمَعْقُودِ بِهِ
(۸۹) الْقَوْلُ لِمُنْكِرِ الْعَوارض
(٩٠) هَلَالُ السِّلْعَةِ يَمْنَعُ التَّحَالُفَ عِندَ الشَّيْخَيْنِ رَحِمَهُمَا اللَّهُ
(۹۱) الْإِقَالَةُ فِي بَابِ السَّلَمِ لَا تَحْتَمِلُ النَّقْضَ
(۹۲) اَلْقَوْلُ فِي الدَّعَاوِي لِصَاحِبِ الْيَدِ
باب ما يدعيه الرجلان
(۹۳) يَجِبُ الْعَمَلُ بِالشَّهَادَتَيْنِ مَا أَمْكَنَ
Principles of Hidayah - Third Volume. (27) Testimony, when suspicion (tuhmah) becomes firmly present in it, is not accepted. (28) Fisq (sinfulness) from the perspective of belief does not prevent acceptance of testimony. (29) Fisq is among things that do not fall under the ruling (of the judge). (70) Confession (iqrar) is among things that fall under the ruling. (1) If the session (majlis) is unified, that which is annexed is attached to the original testimony. Chapter of Disagreement in Testimony: (72) When ownership is established for the testator, it is not adjudicated for the heir until the witnesses testify that he died and left it as inheritance for him. (73) Ignorance (jahalah) concerning that which is confessed does not prevent the validity of the confession. Book of Retraction of Testimonies: (74) Contradiction (tanaqud) does not prevent the validity of the confession. (75) Repentance (tawbah) is according to the crime. (76) Consideration in the chapter of retraction is the persistence of those who remain, not the retraction of those who retract. (77) Compensation (tadmeen) requires equivalence. Book of Agency: (78) Every contract that the agent (wakil) attributes to himself, its rights are attached to the agent; and what is the opposite, its rights are attached to the principal (muwakkil). Chapter of Agency in Selling and Buying: (79) Minor ignorance is tolerated in agency. (80) The principle in mudarabah is generality. Chapter of Dismissal of the Agent: (81) The continuation of agency depends on the continuation of the matter. (82) Constructive dismissal (al-azl al-hukmi) does not depend on the knowledge of the agent. Book of Claims: (83) Imposition (ilzam) concerning the unknown is not actualized. (84) Information to the fullest extent possible is a condition for the validity of the claim. (85) Division (qismah) contradicts partnership. Chapter of Oath: (86) Guarantee of the person (kafalah bi-nafs) is permissible according to us, not according to al-Shafi'i. (87) Evidences (bayyinat) are for proof. Chapter of Mutual Oath (tahaluf): (88) Mutual oath depends on disagreement concerning the subject matter and the price. (89) The saying is of the denier of defects. (90) Halal of the commodity prevents mutual oath according to the two Shaykhs (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf), may Allah have mercy on them. (91) Annulment (iqalah) in the chapter of salam does not allow revocation (naqd). (92) The saying in claims is for the possessor (sahib al-yad). Chapter of What Two Men Claim: (93) It is obligatory to act upon two testimonies as much as possible.
Source pages p. 8

Commentary
This passage is a compilation of legal maxims (qawa'id) from Al-Hidayah, organized by chapter. The maxims are concise principles that summarize key rulings in fiqh. The first set covers testimony (shahadah): testimony is rejected when there is strong suspicion (tuhmah), but fisq (sinfulness) in belief does not automatically bar testimony; however, fisq in action is a separate matter. Confession (iqrar) is subject to judicial ruling. The next chapter addresses disagreement in testimony: for inheritance, ownership must be proven through witnesses that the deceased owned the property and left it as inheritance. The Book of Retraction of Testimonies covers contradictions and repentance: repentance corresponds to the crime. Compensation requires equivalence. In Agency, contracts attributed to the agent bind the agent; those attributed to the principal bind the principal. Minor ignorance is tolerated in agency. Mudarabah applies generally. Agency continues as long as the task continues; constructive dismissal takes effect without the agent's knowledge. In Claims, unknown matters cannot be imposed; full information is required for a valid claim; division ends partnership. In Oaths, guaranty of the person is valid in the Hanafi school but not according to al-Shafi'i. Evidences are for proof. Mutual oath applies when there is disagreement on the subject or price; the say is with the denier of defects. Halal of the commodity prevents mutual oath according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf. Iqalah in salam cannot be reversed. The say in claims is for the possessor. It is obligatory to act on two testimonies as far as possible.

Key Terms
الشَّهَادَة (al-shahadah): Testimony given in court by witnesses
التُّهْمَة (al-tuhmah): Strong suspicion or accusation, especially of bias
الْفِسْق (al-fisq): Sinfulness, departure from obedience

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to maxim 27, what is the ruling on a testimony in which strong suspicion (tuhmah) is present?
A) It is accepted
B) It is not accepted
C) It is suspended pending investigation
D) It is accepted only if the witness repents

Key Takeaway
Testimony is rejected if strong suspicion exists, but sinfulness in personal belief does not automatically disqualify a witness.

Shahadat — Testimony
beginner
8 min
Maxims on Confession (Iqrar)
Collection of maxims on confession (iqrar)

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi maxims on confession and explain why ignorance of details does not invalidate it.

Core Idea
Confession is enforceable even if the matter confessed is unknown, and contradiction in confession does not invalidate it.

These maxims address the validity and effect of confession (iqrar) in Hanafi law. A confession is a powerful legal tool, and these rules ensure that it is not easily set aside. Ignorance of the exact subject matter and later contradictions do not necessarily destroy its binding force.

Guided Path
1
Identify the nature of confession
Maxim 70 states that confession falls under the ruling of the judge, meaning it is binding and actionable.
2
Understand the effect of ignorance
Maxim 73 says ignorance of the matter confessed does not prevent validity. If someone confesses to owing an unspecified debt, it is valid.
The details can be clarified later.
3
Analyze contradictions
Maxim 74 states that contradiction (tanaqud) does not prevent validity. A person can confess and later contradict themselves; the original confession still stands.
The burden of proof shifts to the confessor to repudiate.

الْجَھَالَة (al-jahalah): Ignorance or lack of knowledge about a matter
التَّنَاقُض (al-tanaqud): Contradiction, inconsistency in statements

Checkpoint
According to the maxims in this lesson, what is the effect of ignorance (jahalah) on the validity of a confession?
A) It renders the confession invalid
B) It does not prevent validity
C) It suspends the confession until details become known
D) It makes the confession conditional

Key Takeaway
A confession remains valid even if the details are unknown or if the confessor later contradicts himself.

Shahadat — Testimony
intermediate

Maxims on Retraction of Testimony (Ruju')
Collection of maxims on retraction of testimony

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi maxims on retraction of testimony and evaluate the principles of repentance and compensation.

Core Idea
Retraction of testimony is considered in light of those who persist, not those who retract, and repentance corresponds to the crime.

These maxims from the Book of Retraction of Testimonies establish how the law deals with witnesses who change their statements. The key principles are that the retraction of some does not erase the testimony of others, that repentance is proportional to the offense, and that compensation must match the loss caused.

Guided Path
1
Identify the principle of persistence
Maxim 76 states that in retraction, consideration is given to those who remain (persist in their testimony), not to those who retract.
This means if some witnesses retract while others stick, the case may proceed based on the remaining testimony.
2
Connect repentance to the crime
Maxim 75 says repentance is according to the crime. If the false testimony caused harm, repentance requires compensation.
3
Understand compensation equivalence
Maxim 77: Compensation (tadmeen) requires equivalence (mumathalah). The retracting witness must pay an amount equal to the loss caused.
This prevents arbitrary damages.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

(۱) الْمَجْلِسُ إِذَا اتَّحَدَ لَحِقَ الْمُلْحَقُ بِأَصْلِ الشَّهَادَةِ
باب الاختلاف في الشهادة
(۷۲) اَلْمِلْكُ مَتَى ثَبَتَتْ لِلْمُوْرِثِ لَا يُقْضَى لِلْوَارِثِ بِهِ حَتَّى شَهِدَ الشُّهُودُ أَنَّهُ فَاتَ وَتَرَكَهَا مِيرَانًا لَهُ
(٧٣) اَلْجَهَالَةُ فِى الْمُقِرِّ بِهِ لَا تَمْنَعُ صِحَّةَ الْإِقْرَارِ
كتاب الرجوع عن الشهادات
(۷۴) اَلتَّناقُضُ لَا يَمْنَعُ صِحَّةَ الْإِقْرَارِ
(۷۵) اَلتَّوْبَةُ عَلَى حَسَبِ الْجِنَايَةِ
(۶) الْمُعْتَبَرُ فِى بَابِ الرُّجُوعِ بَقَاءُ مَنْ بَقِيَ لَا رُجُوعَ مَنْ رَجَعَ
(۷۷) اَلتَّضْمِينُ يَسْتَدْعِى الْمُمَاثَلَةَ
كتاب الوكالة
(۷۸) كُلُّ عَقْدِ يُضِيْفُهُ الْوَكِيْلُ إِلَى نَفْسِهِ فَحُقُوقُهُ يَتَعَلَّقُ بِالْوَكِيْلِ وَمَا هُوَ عَلَى الْعَكْسِ فَحُقُوقُهُ تَتَعَلَّقُ بِالْمُؤَكّل
باب الوكالة بالبيع والشراء
(۷۹) اَلْحَهَالَةُ الْيَسِيْرَةُ تَتَحَمَّلُ فِي الْوَكَالَةِ
(۸۰) الْأَصْلُ فِي الْمُضَارَبَةِ الْعُمُومُ
باب عزل الوكيل
(۸۱) بَقَاءُ الْوَكَالَةِ يَعْتَمِدُ قِيَامَ الْأَمْرِ
(۸۲) اَلْعَزْلُ الْحُكْمِيَّ لَا يَتَوَقَّفُ عَلَى عِلْمِ الْوَكِيلِ
كتاب الدعوى
(۸۳) الْإِلْزَامُ فِي الْمَجْهُولِ لَا يَتَحَقَّقُ
(۸۴) الْإِعْلَامُ بِأَقْصَى مَا يُمْكِنُ شَرُطْ فِي صِحَّةِ الدَّعْوَى
(۸۵) الْقِسْمَةُ تُنَافِي الشَّرُكَةَ
باب اليمين
(٨٦) اَلْكَفَالَةُ بِالنَّفْسِ جَائِزَةٌ عِنْدَنَا لَا عِنْدَ الشَّافِعِي
(۸۷) الْبَيِّنَاتُ لِلْإِثْبَاتِ
باب التحالف
(۸۸) اَلتَّحَالُفُ يَعْتَمِدُ الْاِخْتِلَافَ فِي الْمَعْقُودِ عَلَيْهِ وَالْمَعْقُودِ بِهِ
(۸۹) الْقَوْلُ لِمُنْكِرِ الْعَوارض
(٩٠) هَلَالُ السِّلْعَةِ يَمْنَعُ التَّحَالُفَ عِندَ الشَّيْخَيْنِ رَحِمَهُمَا اللَّهُ
(۹۱) الْإِقَالَةُ فِي بَابِ السَّلَمِ لَا تَحْتَمِلُ النَّقْضَ
(۹۲) اَلْقَوْلُ فِي الدَّعَاوِي لِصَاحِبِ الْيَدِ
باب ما يدعيه الرجلان
(۹۳) يَجِبُ الْعَمَلُ بِالشَّهَادَتَيْنِ مَا أَمْكَنَ
Principles of Hidayah - Third Volume. (27) Testimony, when suspicion (tuhmah) becomes firmly present in it, is not accepted. (28) Fisq (sinfulness) from the perspective of belief does not prevent acceptance of testimony. (29) Fisq is among things that do not fall under the ruling (of the judge). (70) Confession (iqrar) is among things that fall under the ruling. (1) If the session (majlis) is unified, that which is annexed is attached to the original testimony. Chapter of Disagreement in Testimony: (72) When ownership is established for the testator, it is not adjudicated for the heir until the witnesses testify that he died and left it as inheritance for him. (73) Ignorance (jahalah) concerning that which is confessed does not prevent the validity of the confession. Book of Retraction of Testimonies: (74) Contradiction (tanaqud) does not prevent the validity of the confession. (75) Repentance (tawbah) is according to the crime. (76) Consideration in the chapter of retraction is the persistence of those who remain, not the retraction of those who retract. (77) Compensation (tadmeen) requires equivalence. Book of Agency: (78) Every contract that the agent (wakil) attributes to himself, its rights are attached to the agent; and what is the opposite, its rights are attached to the principal (muwakkil). Chapter of Agency in Selling and Buying: (79) Minor ignorance is tolerated in agency. (80) The principle in mudarabah is generality. Chapter of Dismissal of the Agent: (81) The continuation of agency depends on the continuation of the matter. (82) Constructive dismissal (al-azl al-hukmi) does not depend on the knowledge of the agent. Book of Claims: (83) Imposition (ilzam) concerning the unknown is not actualized. (84) Information to the fullest extent possible is a condition for the validity of the claim. (85) Division (qismah) contradicts partnership. Chapter of Oath: (86) Guarantee of the person (kafalah bi-nafs) is permissible according to us, not according to al-Shafi'i. (87) Evidences (bayyinat) are for proof. Chapter of Mutual Oath (tahaluf): (88) Mutual oath depends on disagreement concerning the subject matter and the price. (89) The saying is of the denier of defects. (90) Halal of the commodity prevents mutual oath according to the two Shaykhs (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf), may Allah have mercy on them. (91) Annulment (iqalah) in the chapter of salam does not allow revocation (naqd). (92) The saying in claims is for the possessor (sahib al-yad). Chapter of What Two Men Claim: (93) It is obligatory to act upon two testimonies as much as possible.
Source pages p. 8

Commentary
This passage is a compilation of legal maxims (qawa'id) from Al-Hidayah, organized by chapter. The maxims are concise principles that summarize key rulings in fiqh. The first set covers testimony (shahadah): testimony is rejected when there is strong suspicion (tuhmah), but fisq (sinfulness) in belief does not automatically bar testimony; however, fisq in action is a separate matter. Confession (iqrar) is subject to judicial ruling. The next chapter addresses disagreement in testimony: for inheritance, ownership must be proven through witnesses that the deceased owned the property and left it as inheritance. The Book of Retraction of Testimonies covers contradictions and repentance: repentance corresponds to the crime. Compensation requires equivalence. In Agency, contracts attributed to the agent bind the agent; those attributed to the principal bind the principal. Minor ignorance is tolerated in agency. Mudarabah applies generally. Agency continues as long as the task continues; constructive dismissal takes effect without the agent's knowledge. In Claims, unknown matters cannot be imposed; full information is required for a valid claim; division ends partnership. In Oaths, guaranty of the person is valid in the Hanafi school but not according to al-Shafi'i. Evidences are for proof. Mutual oath applies when there is disagreement on the subject or price; the say is with the denier of defects. Halal of the commodity prevents mutual oath according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf. Iqalah in salam cannot be reversed. The say in claims is for the possessor. It is obligatory to act on two testimonies as far as possible.

Key Terms
الرُّجُوع (al-ruju'): Retraction or withdrawal of previous testimony
التَّضْمِين (al-tadmeen): Compensation, liability for damages
الْمُمَاثَلَة (al-mumathalah): Equivalence, proportional compensation

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What does maxim 76 state regarding retraction of testimony?
A) Retraction cancels all testimony
B) Consideration is for those who remain, not those who retract
C) The retracting witness must be punished
D) The court must accept the retraction

Key Takeaway
Retraction of testimony does not erase the testimony of those who persist; retracting witnesses bear liability proportional to the harm.

Shahadat — Testimony
intermediate
12 min
Maxims on Agency (Wikalah)
Collection of maxims on agency (wikalah)

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi maxims on agency to determine rights and responsibilities of agents and principals.

Core Idea
Contracts attributed to the agent bind the agent; contracts attributed to the principal bind the principal.

These maxims from the Book of Agency clarify how rights and obligations are distributed in contractual agency. The key is how the agent attributes the contract: to himself or to the principal. Additional rules cover minor ignorance, the general nature of mudarabah, the duration of agency, and constructive dismissal.

Guided Path
1
Distinguish attribution of contracts
Maxim 78: If the agent attributes the contract to himself, rights attach to him; if to the principal, rights attach to the principal. This determines who bears liability and profit.
Example: agent buys goods saying 'I buy this for you' (principal liable) vs 'I buy this for myself' (agent liable).
2
Understand tolerance of minor ignorance
Maxim 79: Minor ignorance (jahalah yasirah) is tolerated in agency. The agent does not need complete details to act.
This facilitates practical delegation.
3
Apply the principle of generality in mudarabah
Maxim 80: The principle in mudarabah (profit-sharing partnership) is generality; the agent has broad authority unless restricted.
4
Know the conditions for termination
Maxim 81: Agency continues as long as the matter (task) continues; when the task ends, agency ends. Maxim 82: Constructive dismissal (azl hukmi) does not require the agent's knowledge.
Constructive dismissal occurs when the principal's capacity ends (e.g., death).

الوَكَالَة (al-wikalah): Agency: one appoints another to act on his behalf

العَزْل الحُكْمِي (al-azl al-hukmi): Constructive dismissal of an agent without explicit notice

When does the continuation of agency depend on?
A) The agent's willingness
B) The continuation of the task (matter)

Shahadat — Testimony

Maxims on Claims (Da'wa) and Oaths
Collection of maxims on claims and oaths

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi maxims on claims, oaths, and mutual oath to determine procedural rules in litigation.

Core Idea
The say is with the possessor; evidences are for proof; mutual oath arises from disagreement on the object or price.

These maxims from Al-Hidayah cover procedural aspects of claims and oaths. Topics include the necessity of specificity in claims, the role of the possessor, the purpose of evidence, and the conditions for mutual oath (tahaluf). Understanding these rules is essential for anyone studying Hanafi litigation procedure.

Guided Path
1
Understand the requirements for a valid claim
Maxim 83: Imposition (ilzam) cannot be on the unknown. Maxim 84: The claimant must provide information to the fullest extent possible. Maxim 85: Division (qismah) is incompatible with partnership.
Claims must be specific; vague claims are not actionable.
2
Know the rule of possession
Maxim 92: The say (qawl) in claims is for the possessor (sahib al-yad). The defendant (possessor) is favored with the benefit of the doubt.
3
Apply the rule of evidence
Maxim 87: Evidences (bayyinat) are for proof (ithbat). The purpose of evidence is to establish the truth.
4
Identify when mutual oath applies
Maxim 88: Mutual oath applies when there is disagreement on the subject matter (ma'qud alayh) or the price (ma'qud bihi). Maxim 89: The say is of the denier of defects. Maxim 90: The halal of the commodity prevents mutual oath according to the two Shaykhs. Maxim 91: In salam (advance payment), iqalah (annulment) cannot be reversed. Maxim 93: It is obligatory to act upon two testimonies as far as possible.
These govern disputes in sale contracts.

Principles of Hidayah - Third Volume. (27) Testimony, when suspicion (tuhmah) becomes firmly present in it, is not accepted. (28) Fisq (sinfulness) from the perspective of belief does not prevent acceptance of testimony. (29) Fisq is among things that do not fall under the ruling (of the judge). (70) Confession (iqrar) is among things that fall under the ruling. (1) If the session (majlis) is unified, that which is annexed is attached to the original testimony. Chapter of Disagreement in Testimony: (72) When ownership is established for the testator, it is not adjudicated for the heir until the witnesses testify that he died and left it as inheritance for him. (73) Ignorance (jahalah) concerning that which is confessed does not prevent the validity of the confession. Book of Retraction of Testimonies: (74) Contradiction (tanaqud) does not prevent the validity of the confession. (75) Repentance (tawbah) is according to the crime. (76) Consideration in the chapter of retraction is the persistence of those who remain, not the retraction of those who retract. (77) Compensation (tadmeen) requires equivalence. Book of Agency: (78) Every contract that the agent (wakil) attributes to himself, its rights are attached to the agent; and what is the opposite, its rights are attached to the principal (muwakkil). Chapter of Agency in Selling and Buying: (79) Minor ignorance is tolerated in agency. (80) The principle in mudarabah is generality. Chapter of Dismissal of the Agent: (81) The continuation of agency depends on the continuation of the matter. (82) Constructive dismissal (al-azl al-hukmi) does not depend on the knowledge of the agent. Book of Claims: (83) Imposition (ilzam) concerning the unknown is not actualized. (84) Information to the fullest extent possible is a condition for the validity of the claim. (85) Division (qismah) contradicts partnership. Chapter of Oath: (86) Guarantee of the person (kafalah bi-nafs) is permissible according to us, not according to al-Shafi'i. (87) Evidences (bayyinat) are for proof. Chapter of Mutual Oath (tahaluf): (88) Mutual oath depends on disagreement concerning the subject matter and the price. (89) The saying is of the denier of defects. (90) Halal of the commodity prevents mutual oath according to the two Shaykhs (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf), may Allah have mercy on them. (91) Annulment (iqalah) in the chapter of salam does not allow revocation (naqd). (92) The saying in claims is for the possessor (sahib al-yad). Chapter of What Two Men Claim: (93) It is obligatory to act upon two testimonies as much as possible.
Source pages p. 8

Commentary
This passage is a compilation of legal maxims (qawa'id) from Al-Hidayah, organized by chapter. The maxims are concise principles that summarize key rulings in fiqh. The first set covers testimony (shahadah): testimony is rejected when there is strong suspicion (tuhmah), but fisq (sinfulness) in belief does not automatically bar testimony; however, fisq in action is a separate matter. Confession (iqrar) is subject to judicial ruling. The next chapter addresses disagreement in testimony: for inheritance, ownership must be proven through witnesses that the deceased owned the property and left it as inheritance. The Book of Retraction of Testimonies covers contradictions and repentance: repentance corresponds to the crime. Compensation requires equivalence. In Agency, contracts attributed to the agent bind the agent; those attributed to the principal bind the principal. Minor ignorance is tolerated in agency. Mudarabah applies generally. Agency continues as long as the task continues; constructive dismissal takes effect without the agent's knowledge. In Claims, unknown matters cannot be imposed; full information is required for a valid claim; division ends partnership. In Oaths, guaranty of the person is valid in the Hanafi school but not according to al-Shafi'i. Evidences are for proof. Mutual oath applies when there is disagreement on the subject or price; the say is with the denier of defects. Halal of the commodity prevents mutual oath according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf. Iqalah in salam cannot be reversed. The say in claims is for the possessor. It is obligatory to act on two testimonies as far as possible.

Key Terms
الدَّعْوَى (al-da'wa): Legal claim or lawsuit
التَّحَالُف (al-tahaluf): Mutual oath taken by both parties in a dispute when evidence is lacking
الْقَوْل لِصَاحِب الْيَد (al-qawl li-sahib al-yad): The say (presumption) is for the possessor

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
Claims must be specific; mutual oath resolves pricing disputes; the possessor has procedural advantage.

Evidence is for Proof
States a maxim about evidence

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the meaning of the maxim 'al-bayyinat lil-ithbat' and apply it to identify when a claim is established in Hanafi fiqh.

Core Idea
Evidence is solely to prove claims; without evidence, a claim is unestablished.

This short maxim, found in the Hanafi legal maxims, establishes a fundamental principle of judicial proof. It tells us that the role of evidence (bayyina) is to prove a claim, not to create doubt or delay. Understanding this maxim is essential for grasping how cases are decided in Islamic law.

Guided Path
1
State the maxim
Read the maxim in Arabic and English. Recognize that it is a concise legal principle.
2
Identify the subject
'al-bayyinat' refers to evidence, especially testimony. Understand its scope.
In Hanafi school, bayyina typically means two male witnesses or one male and two females.
3
Identify the predicate
'lil-ithbat' means 'for proof' or 'for establishing'. Understand that the purpose is to establish the truth of a claim.
4
Apply the maxim
Given a scenario where someone makes a claim, determine whether providing evidence establishes the claim. If evidence is provided, the claim is proven; if not, the claim remains unproven.
5
Recognize implications
This maxim implies that the burden of proof is on the claimant. Without evidence, the defendant's denial is accepted on oath.
This is the basis for the rule 'al-bayyina 'ala man idda'a wa al-yamin 'ala man ankara'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(87) الْبَيِّنَاتُ لِلْإِثْبَاتِ
(87) Evidence is for proof.
Source pages p. 9

Commentary
This maxim states that evidence (baiyinat) in Islamic law is used to prove claims. If a claimant provides evidence, their claim is established.

Key Terms
الْبَيِّنَاتُ (al-bayyinat): Evidence, especially witness testimony or documents.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the maxim, what is the purpose of evidence?
A) To create uncertainty
B) To establish proof
C) To punish the defendant
D) To delay judgment

Key Takeaway
Evidence in Hanafi law is solely a tool to prove claims; without it, a claim is not established.

Establishment of Suspicion (Tuhma) by One Component of Testimony
Explaining the rule of tuhma with an example of implied dissolution of a sale

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on imprisonment based on incomplete testimony in hadd and qisas cases and explain how tuhma is established by either number or uprightness of witnesses.

Core Idea
Suspicion suffices for detention: one upright witness or two concealed ones trigger tuhma in serious crimes.

In Hanafi criminal procedure, the threshold for detaining an accused differs from the threshold for conviction. This lesson explores a key principle: the judge may order imprisonment based on suspicion (tuhma), which can be established by only one of the two components of full testimony—either the number of witnesses (two, even if their character is unknown) or the uprightness of a single witness. This nuanced rule balances the need to secure the accused with the protection of individual liberty, and it is distinct from the stricter requirements for property cases.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Ruling and Its Context
Locate the ruling: imprisonment in hadd (fixed penalty) and qisas (retaliation) cases. Note that it is permissive (mubah) for the judge, not obligatory.
The passage contrasts this with property cases where imprisonment requires complete proof.
2
Understand the Basis: Tuhma
Tuhma (suspicion) is the legal ground. According to the Hanafi school, tuhma is established by one of the two halves of testimony: either number (two witnesses) or uprightness (one just witness). The witness's moral status or the count alone can create sufficient suspicion.
The two halves are 'adad (number) and 'adalah (uprightness).
3
Examine the Supporting Example from Sales
The passage uses an analogy from sale law to illustrate implicit legal effects. If a sale is made for 1000 and then renewed for 1500, the first sale dissolves implicitly by the mere establishment of the second. This shows that a legal consequence can arise without explicit action, similar to how tuhma arises from partial testimony.
This example demonstrates the principle of 'al-istiqlal bi al-bay' (implied dissolution).
4
Distinguish from Property Cases
In property disputes, imprisonment is the ultimate penalty, so it requires complete proof (two upright witnesses). The lower threshold for hadd/qisas is justified by the gravity and the need to prevent evasion of justice.
The key phrase: 'because imprisonment here is due to suspicion, and suspicion is established by one of the two halves of testimony.'
5
Note the Cross-Madhhab Difference
The Shafi'i school does not accept tuhma as a sufficient basis for imprisonment and requires two upright witnesses even for detention. This difference affects practical outcomes in jurisdictions where multiple schools are applied.
Al-Marghinani in al-Hidayah presents the Hanafi position as the established one.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الكفالة. (٤٢) التهمة تثبت بأحد شطري الشهادة إما العدد أو العدالة. كما لو تبايعا بألف ثم جدداه بألف وخمسمائة فإن البيع الأول ينفسخ ضرورة ثبوت الثاني اقتضاء. تبيين الحقائق: كتاب الصرف، ج ٤ ص ١٤٠) والفسخ قد يثبت بطريق الاقتضاء هذا جواب أيضا عما يقال: إن العقد لو فسخ للمقاصة وجب قبض الدينار على البائع بحكم الإقالة، لأن للإقالة حكم الصرف، وتقرير الجواب: أن الفسخ ضمنى يثبت في ضمن المقاصة بطريق الاقتضاء، فجاز أن لا يثبت بعد هذا حكم البيع (كما إذا تبايعا بألف) يعنى عقدا بألف درهم ثم بألف وخمسمائة أى ثم تبايعا، فإن العقد الأول ينفسخ ضرورة بثبوت الثاني. (البناية: كتاب الصرف، ج٨ ص ٤٠٨) الهداية كتاب الكفالة، ج ٣ ص ١٢٢

فإن شهد عليه) أي على المدعى عليه (مستوران) أي غير معلوم فسادهما في حد أو قود حبس وكذا يحبس إن شهد عدل واحد) يعرفه القاضي بالعدالة لأن الحبس هنا للتهمة والتهمة تثبت بإحدى شطري الشهادة، وهو العدد في المستور أو العدالة في الواحد بخلاف الحبس في الأموال لأنه غاية عقوبة فيها فلا يثبت إلا بحجة كاملة. (مجمع الأنهر : كتاب الكفالة، ج ٢ ص ١٢٩) قال (ولا يحبس فيها حتى يشهد شاهدان إلخ لا يحبس الحاكم في الحدود
(Book of Surety) (42) Suspicion (tuhma) is established by one of the two halves of testimony: either number or uprightness. For example, if two parties transacted a sale for one thousand then renewed it for one thousand five hundred, then the first sale is dissolved necessarily due to the establishment of the second implicitly. (Tabyin al-Haqa'iq: Kitab al-Sarf, vol. 4 p. 140) And dissolution may occur by way of implicit indication. This is also a response to what is said: if the contract were dissolved for set-off, it would be necessary for the seller to take possession of the dinar by virtue of annulment, because annulment has the ruling of exchange. The clarification of the response: that the dissolution is implicit, established within the set-off by way of implicit indication, so it is permissible that the ruling of sale is not established after this. (As if they transacted for one thousand) meaning a contract for one thousand dirhams, then for one thousand five hundred, i.e., then they transacted, then the first contract is dissolved necessarily due to the establishment of the second. (al-Binaya: Kitab al-Sarf, vol. 8 p. 408) al-Hidayah, Kitab al-Kafala, vol. 3 p. 122. Then if two concealed persons (i.e., whose corruption is not known) testify against him (i.e., the defendant) in a hadd or retaliation case, he is imprisoned, and similarly he is imprisoned if one upright witness testifies whom the judge knows to be upright, because imprisonment here is due to suspicion (tuhma), and suspicion is established by one of the two halves of testimony: number in the case of the concealed, or uprightness in the case of the one. Unlike imprisonment in property cases, because it is the ultimate punishment in them, so it is not established except by a complete proof. (Majma' al-Anhur: Kitab al-Kafala, vol. 2 p. 129) He said: 'And he is not imprisoned in them until two witnesses testify, etc.' The judge does not imprison in the hadd...
Source pages p. 77

Commentary
This passage from Usool e Hidayah presents a key legal principle from the Hanafi school concerning the establishment of suspicion (tuhma) in the context of imprisonment (habs) for hadd (fixed penalties) and qisas (retaliation) cases. The core ruling, taken from al-Hidayah, states that tuhma is proven by one of the two components of testimony: either by the number of witnesses (two, even if their uprightness is unknown) or by the uprightness of a single witness. This is a relaxation of the normal requirement of complete testimony (two upright witnesses) because imprisonment here is not a final punishment but a precautionary measure based on suspicion.

The passage then provides an illustrative example from the law of sale (sarf) to explain the concept of implied dissolution (فسخ بطريق الاقتضاء). The example: if two parties agree on a sale for 1000, then before delivery of the price, they renew the contract for 1500, the first contract is automatically dissolved by implication because the same object cannot be subject to two different prices simultaneously. This demonstrates how a legal effect can occur implicitly—here, the dissolution of the first sale is necessitated by the establishment of the second. The commentaries from Tabyin al-Haqa'iq and al-Binaya elaborate on this point, showing that such implicit dissolution is valid and does not require explicit annulment.

Returning to the main topic, the text specifies that in hadd and qisas cases, the judge may imprison the defendant if two witnesses whose moral character is unknown (مستوران) testify, or if one upright witness (عدل واحد) whose justice the judge knows testifies. The reason is that the imprisonment is due to suspicion (tuhma), and suspicion is established by either the number of witnesses (in the case of the concealed) or the uprightness of a single witness. In contrast, for property cases, imprisonment is the ultimate penalty (غاية عقوبة), so it requires complete proof (حجة كاملة), i.e., two upright witnesses. This distinction highlights the practical wisdom of the Hanafi school: in serious criminal matters, a lower threshold suffices to detain the accused pending further investigation, whereas in property disputes, the final nature of imprisonment demands full evidentiary standards.

Key Terms
تہمت (tuhma): Suspicion or accusation that arises from testimony falling short of complete proof.
شطر الشہادہ (shathr al-shahadah): One of the two components of testimony: either the number of witnesses (at least two) or the uprightness of a single witness.
مستور (mastur): A person whose moral integrity (adala) is not known; his testimony is accepted for tuhma but not for complete proof.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, in which scenario can a judge imprison a defendant in a hadd or qisas case based on incomplete testimony?
A) Only if two upright witnesses testify
B) If two concealed witnesses or one upright witness testify
C) Only if the defendant confesses
D) Only in property cases

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, suspicion (tuhma) is established by either the number or the uprightness of witnesses, permitting imprisonment in serious crimes even without complete proof.

The Principle of Voice Similarity
States that voices can be similar, cautioning against sole reliance on voice identification.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the principle of voice similarity and explain its legal implication in Hanafi testimony law, specifically why voice alone is insufficient for identification.

Core Idea
Voices can be alike; alone they are not enough for identification.

This brief principle from Hanafi legal literature may appear simple, but it carries a significant procedural caution. In cases of testimony or oath, relying solely on voice recognition can lead to error. The Hanafi school teaches that additional corroboration is needed when identity is based on something as variable as the human voice.

Guided Path
1
Understand the literal meaning
Read the Arabic phrase: 'إِنَّ النَّغْمَةَ تَشْبَهُ النَّعْمَةَ'. Literally it says 'a melody resembles a blessing'. But in legal usage, 'naghmat' refers to the voice or tone, and the phrase conveys that voices can be similar.
The term 'naghmat' is key; it is not about musical melody but the spoken voice.
2
Grasp the underlying caution
The principle warns against overconfidence in voice identification. Since two people may have strikingly similar voices, a witness or judge might mistake one person for another. This principle is a reminder to seek additional evidence.
This is particularly relevant in shahadat (testimony) and qada (judgment).
3
Apply to a legal scenario
Imagine a witness claims to recognize a defendant by voice alone in a dark room. The Hanafi judge would not accept this as conclusive proof. The principle requires the judge to demand further corroboration, such as visual identification or other evidence.
This protects against wrongful convictions based on unreliable sensory evidence.
4
Memorize the maxim
Commit the Arabic to memory: 'إِنَّ النَّغْمَةَ تَشْبَهُ النَّعْمَةَ'. It is a concise legal maxim that encapsulates an important evidentiary rule.
Memorization anchors this principle for quick recall in discussions of evidence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
إِنَّ النَّغْمَةَ تَشْبَهُ النَّعْمَةَ.
Indeed, a melody resembles a blessing.
Source pages p. 102

Commentary
This is a ruling statement presenting a principle: voices can be similar. In Islamic legal procedure, this principle is invoked to caution that identification by voice alone is not reliable, as one person's voice may be mistaken for another's. Although the literal meaning mentions 'melody' and 'blessing', the Urdu explanation clarifies that it refers to voice similarity. This principle is relevant in cases of testimony or oath where voice recognition might be used as evidence.

Key Terms
النَّغْمَة (al-naghmatu): Voice or melody; used here to mean a person's spoken voice.

Key Terms from Source Passage

D) This principle is only about musical matters

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi principle 'إن النغمة تشبه النعمة' teaches that voice identification alone is insufficient for legal certainty and must be corroborated.

Voice Resemblance and Witness Investigation: An Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on witness investigation and rule on testimony by voice.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the judge's duty to investigate witnesses and apply the principle of voice resemblance to determine the validity of testimony based on hearing.

Core Idea
Voice resemblance prevents certain knowledge; testimony requires certainty. Judges must investigate witnesses in corrupt times.

This lesson examines two related legal principles from the Hanafi school. First, the rule that a voice heard from behind a curtain is insufficient for testimony because voices can resemble one another. Second, the intra-Hanafi disagreement between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) regarding the judge's duty to investigate the character of witnesses before accepting their testimony. The text shows how legal rulings can adapt to changing social conditions, with the fatwa shifting to the Sahibayn's view in corrupt times.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Principle of Voice Resemblance
Recognize the maxim 'النغمة تشبه النعمة' meaning one voice resembles another. Understand that this creates doubt about the identity of a speaker behind a curtain.
Testimony requires certain knowledge (ilm), so hearing alone is insufficient unless circumstances remove all doubt.
2
State the Ruling on Testimony by Voice
If a person hears a voice from behind a curtain saying 'I sold' or 'I bought', they cannot testify to that contract because the voice may belong to someone else. Exception: if they are certain the speaker is alone and it is his voice.
Certainty is negated by voice similarity.
3
Present the Two Hanafi Positions on Witness Investigation
Abu Hanifa holds that the judge may rely on the apparent uprightness of a Muslim witness and need not investigate unless the opponent challenges. The Sahibayn hold that the judge must inquire about witnesses secretly and openly in all rights.
This is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf.
4
Analyse the Proofs of Each Side
Abu Hanifa: Muslims are presumed upright. Sahibayn: judgment is based on proof (testimony of upright witnesses), so ascertaining uprightness is necessary to avoid nullity if witnesses turn out to be slaves or disbelievers.
Both are rational arguments (dalil aqli).
5
Determine the Tarjih and Thamarah al-Khilaf
The difference is attributed to change of times: Abu Hanifa's era was upright, Sahibayn's era was corrupt. The fatwa is on the Sahibayn's view in this era. Practical consequence: judges today must investigate witnesses.
Rulings can change based on social context (taghayyur al-ahkam bi taghayyur al-zaman).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
اصول ہدایہ ثالث ۱۰۲ لیے انہوں نے گواہوں کے ظاہری حال پر اکتفا کیا جبکہ صاحبین کے دور میں شر و فساد غالب تھا، بدگوئی اور دروغ گوئی عام تھی، اس لیے انہوں نے تزکیہ کو لازم قرار دیا، فتوی صاحبین کے قول پر ہے۔ (۲۲) إِنَّ النَّغْمَةَ تَشْبَهُ النَّعْمَةَ. ترجمہ: آواز کی مشابہ ہوتی ہے۔ تشریح: مذکورہ اصول کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ ایک کی آواز دوسرے کی آواز کے مشابہ ہوتی (قَوْلُهُ وَسَأَلَ عَنْ الشُّهُودِ سِرًّا وَعَلَنَا فِي سَائِرِ الْحُقُوقِ أَى وَسَأَلَ الْقَاضِي عَنْهُمُ فِي السِّرِّ وَالْعَلَانِيَةِ وَهُوَ قَوْلُ أَبِى يُوسُفَ وَمُحَمَّدٍ ، لأَنَّ الْقَضَاءَ مَبْنِيٌّ عَلَى الْحُجَّةِ وَهِيَ شَهَادَةُ الْعُدُولِ فَيَتَعَرَّفْ عَنْ الْعَدَالَةِ وَفِيهِ صَوْنُ قَضَائِهِ عَنِ الْبُطْلَانِ وَقَالَ أَبُو حَنِيفَةَ يَقْتَصِرُ الْحَاكِمُ عَلَى ظَاهِرِ الْعَدَالَةِ فِي الْمُسْلِمِ وَلَا يَسْأَلُ حَتَّى بِطَعْنِ الْخَصْمِ ... وَالْحَاصِلُ أَنَّهُ إِنْ طَعَنَ الْخَصْمُ سَأَلَ عَنْهُمْ فِي الْكُلِّ وَإِلَّا سَأَلَ فِي الْحُدُودِ وَالْقِصَاصِ وَفِي غَيْرِهَا مَحَلُّ الِاخْتِلَافِ وَقِيلَ هَذَا اخْتِلَافُ عَصْرٍ وَزَمَانٍ وَالْفَتْوَى عَلَى قَوْلِهِمَا فِى هَذَا الزَّمَانِ. (البحر الرائق: كتاب الشهادات، ج۷ ص ۶۳) وَقَالَ أَبُو يُوسُفَ وَمُحَمَّدٌ : لَا بُدَّ أَنْ يَسْأَلَ عَنْهُمْ فِي السِّرِّ وَالْعَلَانِيَةِ فِي جَمِيعِ الْحُقُوقِ، لِأَنَّ مَبْنَى الْقَضَاءِ عَلَى الْحُجَّةِ وَهِيَ شَهَادَةُ الْعُدُولِ فَلَا بُدَّ مِنْ التَّعَرُّفِ عَنْ الْعَدَالَةِ، وَفِي السُّؤَالِ صَوْنُ الْقَضَاءِ عَنْ الْبُطْلَانِ عَلَى تَقْدِيرِ ظُهُورِ الشُّهُودِ عَبِيدًا أَوْ كُفَّارًا وَقِيلَ هَذَا الاخْتِلافُ اخْتِلَافُ عَصْرٍ وَزَمَانٍ)، لِأَنَّ أَبَا حَنِيفَةَ أَجَابَ فِي زَمَانِهِ وَكَانَ الْغَالِبُ مِنْهُمُ عُدُولًا وَهُمَا أَجَابَا فِي زَمَانِهِمَا وَقَدْ تَغَيَّرَ النَّاسُ وَكَفُرَ الْفَسَادُ، وَلَوْ شَاهَدَ ذَلِكَ أَبُو حَنِيفَةَ لَقَالَ بِقَوْلِهِمَا، وَلِهَذَا قَالَ وَالْفَتْوَى عَلَى قَوْلِهِمَا فِي هَذَا الرَّمَانِ). (العناية كتاب الشهادة، ج۷ ص ۳۷۸، ۳۷۹) الهداية كتاب الشهادة، ج ۳ ص ۱۲۵ اصول ہدایہ ثالث ۱۰۳ ہے، لہذا محض آواز سن کر بغیر دیکھے گواہی دینا درست نہیں ہے۔ صاحب ہدایہ مذکورہ اصول ذکر کر کے یہ بتلا رہے ہیں کہ اگر کسی آدمی نے پردہ کے پیچھے سے آواز سنی ، مثلاً بِعْتُ “ اور ”اشْتَرَيْتُ “ کہتے ہوئے ، تو اب اس کے لئے جائز نہیں ہے کہ یہ گواہی دے کہ اس نے اس چیز کو فلاں پر فروخت کیا ہے، یا اس سے خریدا ہے، کیونکہ ایک آواز دوسری آواز کے ساتھ مشابہت رکھتی ہے، اور پردے کے پیچھے سے سنی ہوئی آواز اور بھی مشتبہ ہوتی ہے اور مشتبہ سے علم حاصل نہیں ہو پاتا، جبکہ ادائے شہادت کے لیے علم اور واقعیت شرط ہے، اس لیے پردے کے پیچھے سے سنی ہوئی بات پر شہادت دینا جائز نہیں ہے، الا یہ کہ یقینی طور پر معلوم ہو جائے کہ اس کمرے میں اس کے علاوہ کوئی اور شخص نہیں ہے، اور یہ اس کی آواز ہے تو گواہی دے سکتا ہے۔
Principles of Hidayah, volume 3, page 102. Therefore they were satisfied with the apparent condition of the witnesses, while in the era of the Sahibayn evil and corruption were prevalent, slander and lying were common, so they deemed verification necessary. The fatwa is according to their statement. (22) Indeed, the voice resembles the voice. Translation: The voice is similar. Explanation: The meaning of this principle is that one voice resembles another. (His statement: And he asked about the witnesses secretly and openly regarding all rights, meaning the judge asks about them in secret and open, and this is the statement of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, because judgment is based on proof, which is the testimony of upright witnesses, so he should ascertain their uprightness, and in this is the preservation of his judgment from nullity. And Abu Hanifa said: The judge restricts himself to the apparent uprightness of a Muslim and does not ask unless the opponent challenges. The summary: If the opponent challenges, he asks about them in all cases; otherwise, he asks in cases of hudud and qisas, and in other matters it is a point of disagreement. It is said this is a difference of era and time, and the fatwa is according to their statement in this time. (Al-Bahr al-Raiq: Kitab al-Shahadat, vol. 7 p. 63) And Abu Yusuf and Muhammad said: It is necessary to ask about them secretly and openly in all rights, because judgment is based on proof which is the testimony of upright witnesses, so ascertaining uprightness is necessary, and in the questioning is preservation of judgment from nullity on the assumption that the witnesses appear to be slaves or disbelievers. And it is said this difference is a difference of era and time, because Abu Hanifa answered in his time when most people were upright, and they answered in their time when people had changed and corruption increased, and had Abu Hanifa witnessed that, he would have said according to their statement, and therefore it is said the fatwa is according to their statement in this time. (Al-Inayah: Kitab al-Shahada, vol. 7 pp. 378-379) Al-Hidayah: Kitab al-Shahada, vol. 3 p. 125. Principles of Hidayah, volume 3, page 103. Therefore, merely hearing a voice without seeing is not valid for testimony. The author of Hidayah, by mentioning this principle, explains that if a person hears a voice from behind a curtain, for example saying 'I sold' and 'I bought', then it is not permissible for him to testify that he sold that item to so-and-so or bought it from him, because one voice resembles another, and a voice heard from behind a curtain is even more ambiguous, and from ambiguity certainty is not obtained, while for giving testimony, knowledge and certainty are conditions. Therefore, testifying based on something heard from behind a curtain is not permissible, unless it is known with certainty that there is no one else in that room besides that person and that it is his voice, then he may testify.
Source pages p. 102

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute with a ruling. It begins by stating the principle that voices resemble each other (النغمة تشبه النعمة), meaning that one person's voice can sound similar to another's. The author then explains the ruling: if a person hears a voice from behind a curtain stating 'I sold' and 'I bought', they cannot testify to that sale or purchase because the voice could belong to someone else. Testimony requires certain knowledge, and hearing from behind a curtain does not provide that certainty. The exception is if the hearer knows for certain that the speaker is alone in the room and it is his voice. The passage then discusses a related dispute about the judge's duty to investigate witnesses' character (tazkiyah). The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) hold that the judge must inquire about witnesses secretly and openly in all cases, because judgment is based on proof, and proof requires upright witnesses. Abu Hanifa held that the judge may rely on apparent uprightness and only needs to investigate if the opponent challenges the witnesses. However, this difference is attributed to the change of times: in Abu Hanifa's era, people were generally upright, but in the Sahibayn's era, corruption had spread. Therefore, the fatwa is according to the Sahibayn's view in modern times. This shows how rulings can change based on social context according to the Hanafi school.

Key Terms
النَّغْمَةَ (al-naghma): Voice or sound, specifically the tone of a person's speech.
شَهَادَةُ (shahada): Testimony, giving evidence in court.
عَدَالَةِ (adala): Uprightness, moral character; a condition for witness acceptability.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) Because the Sahibayn were more knowledgeable than Abu Hanifa.
B) Because corruption spread after Abu Hanifa's time, making investigation necessary.
C) Because the Sahibayn's view is easier to implement.
D) Because all later scholars rejected Abu Hanifa's view.

Key Takeaway
Testimony requires certain knowledge; voice similarity prevents certainty. In corrupt times, the judge must thoroughly investigate witnesses to ensure the validity of judgments.

Shahadat — Testimony
