Testimony Is Not Binding by Itself
States a principle about testimony not being binding by itself.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the meaning of the Hanafi principle 'al-shahadah ghayr mujibatun bi-nafsiha' and explain why testimony heard from behind a curtain is not accepted due to uncertainty.

Core Idea
Testimony is evidence, not a verdict; it does not automatically create legal effects.

This lesson introduces a foundational principle in the law of evidence: testimony (shahadah) is not by itself binding. The judge must evaluate it, and mere presentation does not guarantee acceptance. We will apply this principle to the scenario of hearing a transaction from behind a curtain, where uncertainty about identity prevents the testimony from being accepted.

Guided Path
1
Identify the legal principle
The statement 'الشهادة غير موجبة بنفسها' is a principle about the nature of testimony. It means that testimony does not automatically prove a claim or create an obligation.
2
Understand the meaning
Testimony is a report that requires judicial assessment. It is a proof (hujja) but not a direct cause of legal effect. The judge must evaluate its reliability and certainty.
3
Apply to the curtain scenario
If a witness hears a transaction from behind a curtain, they cannot be certain of the speaker's identity because voice resembles voice. Their testimony lacks the required certainty (yaqin) and is therefore inadmissible.
4
Note the evidentiary implication
The principle reinforces that testimony must be based on certain knowledge. Speculation or doubt invalidates it.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۶۳) اَلشَّهَادَةُ غَيْرُ مُوجِبَةٍ بِنَفْسِهَا. ترجمہ: شہادت بذات خود کسی چیز کو واجب کرنے والی نہیں ہے۔ تشریح: مذکورہ اصول کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ شہادت از خود دعوی کو ثابت نہیں کر سکتی اور نہ ہی اُس سے کوئی چیز لازم ہوسکتی ہے۔ صاحب ہدایہ مذکورہ اصول ذکر کر کے یہ بتلارہے ہیں کہ شہادت کی ایک قسم شہادت وَلَوْ سَمِعَ مِنْ وَرَاءِ الْحِجَابِ لَا يَسَعُهُ أَنْ يَشْهَدَ لِاحْتِمَالِ أَنْ يَكُونَ غَيْرُهُ إِذِ النَّعْمَةُ تُشْبِهُ النَّعْمَةَ إِلَّا إِذَا كَانَ فِى الدَّاخِلِ وَحْدَهُ وَعَلِمَ الشَّاهِدُ أَنَّهُ لَيْسَ فِيهِ غَيْرُهُ. تبيين الحقائق كتاب الشهادة، ج ۴ ص (۲۱۴) ولو سمع من وراء الحجاب أى قول :واحد بعت وقول آخر: اشتريت (لا يجوز له أن يشهد ولو فسر للقاضي بأن قال : أشهد بالسماع من رواء الحجاب (لا يقبله لأن النغمة تشبه النغمة، فلم يحصل العلم). (البناية: كتاب الشهادة، ج ۹ ص ۱۲۳) الهداية كتاب الشهادة، ج ۳ ص ۱۶۵
(63) Testimony is not by itself binding. Translation: Testimony by itself does not make anything obligatory. Explanation: The meaning of this principle is that testimony cannot by itself prove a claim nor can anything become necessary from it. The author of Hidayah, by mentioning this principle, explains that one kind of testimony: 'And if he hears from behind a curtain, it is not permissible for him to testify due to the possibility that it might be someone else, because voice resembles voice, except if the person inside is alone and the witness knows that there is no one else with him.' (Tabyin al-Haqa'iq: Kitab al-Shahada, vol. 4 p. 214) 'And if he hears from behind a curtain, meaning one person saying 'I sold' and another saying 'I bought', it is not permissible for him to testify even if he explains to the judge by saying 'I testify based on hearing from behind the curtain', the judge does not accept it because voice resembles voice, so knowledge is not obtained.' (Al-Binayah: Kitab al-Shahada, vol. 9 p. 123) Al-Hidayah: Kitab al-Shahada, vol. 3 p. 165.
Source pages p. 103

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling statement: 'Testimony is not binding by itself' (الشهادة غير موجبة بنفسها). The author explains that testimony does not automatically prove a claim or create an obligation; it merely presents evidence. The judge must evaluate it. The passage then references the previous principle about hearing from behind a curtain, reiterating that such testimony is invalid due to voice similarity. The author cites Tabyin al-Haqa'iq and Al-Binayah to reinforce that even if the witness explains to the judge that they heard from behind a curtain, the testimony is not accepted because certainty (ilm) is not achieved. This principle underscores that testimony is a means of proof, not the proof itself.

Key Terms
غَيْرُ مُوجِبَةٍ (ghayr mujiba): Not causing obligation; testimony does not by itself make a claim binding.
مُوجِبَةٍ (mujiba): That which makes something obligatory or binding.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
Testimony is evidence, not a verdict; it requires judicial evaluation and cannot alone create legal obligations.

Shahadat — Testimony

Testimony Based on Voice from Behind a Curtain
Ruling on impermissibility of testifying solely by hearing a voice from behind a curtain

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on testimony based on hearing a voice from behind a curtain and identify the condition that makes it permissible.

Core Idea
Testimony requires certainty; a voice behind a curtain is uncertain because voices resemble each other.

The Hanafi school places a high standard on testimony: the witness must have certain knowledge (ilm) of what they attest. In this passage from al-Hidayah and its commentaries, we examine a scenario where a person hears a transaction from behind a curtain. The school rules that such testimony is not permissible, as the voice alone cannot guarantee identity. However, an exception exists when the witness is absolutely certain the room contained only one person. This ruling illustrates the school's careful approach to preserving legal rights through stringent evidentiary requirements.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine what action is being judged. The act is giving testimony (shahadah) based on hearing a voice from behind a curtain. The ruling is that it is not permissible (la yajuuz), i.e., haram.
The text uses 'لا يجوز' which indicates prohibition.
2
Locate the dalil
Find the proof or reasoning (dalil) for the ruling. The text states: 'النغمة تشبه النغمة' (one tone resembles another). This is the core argument that voices can be similar, leading to uncertainty.
The proof is a rational principle (talil) based on experience.
3
Analyze the wajh al-dalalah
Understand how the proof leads to the ruling. Because voices can be identical, hearing a voice does not produce certain knowledge (ilm) of the speaker's identity. Since testimony requires certainty (علم) and exact reality (واقعیت), the evidence is insufficient.
The Hanafi school holds that ilm is a condition for testimony.
4
Identify the exception (istithna)
The text allows testimony if the witness knows with certainty that no other person was present (الا یہ کہ یقینی طور پر معلوم ہو جائے کہ اس کمرے میں اس کے علاوہ کوئی اور شخص نہیں ہے). This exception preserves the possibility of valid testimony when certainty is attained.
The exception is narrow: absolute certainty of the speaker's identity.
5
Note the ikhtilaf
Other schools may permit testimony based on voice alone if the witness is confident. The Hanafi position is stricter and represents the zahir al-riwayah (relied-upon transmission).
The cross-madhhab dispute is acknowledged but the Hanafi ruling is mufta bihi.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ہے، لہذا محض آواز سن کر بغیر دیکھے گواہی دینا درست نہیں ہے۔ صاحب ہدایہ مذکورہ اصول ذکر کر کے یہ بتلا رہے ہیں کہ اگر کسی آدمی نے پردہ کے پیچھے سے آواز سنی ، مثلاً بِعْتُ “ اور ”اشْتَرَيْتُ “ کہتے ہوئے ، تو اب اس کے لئے جائز نہیں ہے کہ یہ گواہی دے کہ اس نے اس چیز کو فلاں پر فروخت کیا ہے، یا اس سے خریدا ہے، کیونکہ ایک آواز دوسری آواز کے ساتھ مشابہت رکھتی ہے، اور پردے کے پیچھے سے سنی ہوئی آواز اور بھی مشتبہ ہوتی ہے اور مشتبہ سے علم حاصل نہیں ہو پاتا، جبکہ ادائے شہادت کے لیے علم اور واقعیت شرط ہے، اس لیے پردے کے پیچھے سے سنی ہوئی بات پر شہادت دینا جائز نہیں ہے، الا یہ کہ یقینی طور پر معلوم ہو جائے کہ اس کمرے میں اس کے علاوہ کوئی اور شخص نہیں ہے، اور یہ اس کی آواز ہے تو گواہی دے سکتا ہے۔ تبيين الحقائق كتاب الشهادة، ج ۴ ص (۲۱۴) ولو سمع من وراء الحجاب أى قول :واحد بعت وقول آخر: اشتريت (لا يجوز له أن يشهد ولو فسر للقاضي بأن قال : أشهد بالسماع من رواء الحجاب (لا يقبله لأن النغمة تشبه النغمة، فلم يحصل العلم). (البناية: كتاب الشهادة، ج ۹ ص ۱۲۳) الهداية كتاب الشهادة، ج ۳ ص ۱۶۵
So, merely hearing a voice without seeing is not correct for giving testimony. The author of al-Hidayah, after mentioning this principle, states that if a person hears a voice from behind a curtain, for example hearing 'I sold' and 'I bought', then it is not permissible for him to testify that he sold such and such to so-and-so or bought from him, because one voice resembles another, and a voice heard from behind a curtain is even more ambiguous, and from ambiguous [evidence] certainty is not attained, while for testimony knowledge and exact reality are conditions. Therefore, testifying based on something heard from behind a curtain is not permissible, unless it is known with certainty that there is no other person in that room and that it is his voice; then he may testify. Tabyin al-Haqa'iq, Book of Testimony, vol. 4, p. 214: 'If he hears from behind the curtain, i.e., one person saying "I sold" and another saying "I bought", it is not permissible for him to testify even if he explains to the judge by saying "I testify by hearing from behind the curtain". It is not accepted because one tone resembles another, so certainty is not attained.' (al-Binaya, Book of Testimony, vol. 9, p. 123) al-Hidayah, Book of Testimony, vol. 3, p. 165.
Source pages p. 103

Commentary
This passage is a ruling from the Hanafi school on the validity of testimony based solely on hearing a voice from behind a curtain. The author explains that testifying in such a case is not permissible because certainty of identity cannot be established. The principle is that one voice resembles another (النغمة تشبه النغمة), so there is a possibility of mistake. Since testimony requires certainty (علم) and exact knowledge (واقعیت), ambiguous evidence is insufficient. The exception is if the witness knows that the room contains only one person and that it is indeed that person's voice. The passage quotes from Tabyin al-Haqa'iq and al-Binaya confirming this ruling, and the reference to al-Hidayah indicates this is the relied-upon position.

Key Terms
شهادة (shahādah): Testimony in court, giving evidence about a right or transaction.
نغمة (نعمة) (naghmatun/ni'mah): Tone of voice or timbre; in this context, the sound quality of a person's voice.
حجاب (hijāb): A curtain or barrier that prevents seeing the speaker.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is testimony based solely on hearing a voice from behind a curtain not permissible according to Hanafi fiqh?
A) Because the person may not have been seen
B) Because one voice can resemble another, causing uncertainty
C) Because it is not allowed to testify without seeing the transaction
D) Because the witness must be present in the court

Key Takeaway
Testimony requires certain knowledge; a voice behind a curtain is insufficient because voices can be similar, unless absolute certainty of identity exists.

The Condition of Deputyship for Witness-upon-Witness
Ruling on the requirement of deputyship for witness-upon-witness

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi condition for the validity of shahada 'ala al-shahada and explain the legal basis for requiring deputyship.

Core Idea
Testimony is not self-obligating — it only becomes effective when transmitted to the judge's court.

This passage introduces a key procedural principle in Hanafi testimony law: testimony does not create a binding right by itself. It only acquires legal force when presented before a judge. This principle governs the validity of 'shahada 'ala al-shahada' (witness-upon-witness). Understanding this principle helps you avoid a common misunderstanding—that hearing an original witness suffices to become a branch witness.

Guided Path
1
Identify the legal principle
Locate the statement 'al-shahada ghayr mujiba bi nafsiha' (testimony is not self-obligating). This is the core maxim that drives the entire ruling.
This principle is stated in the first line of the passage.
2
Understand the application to witness-upon-witness
The passage explains that because testimony is not self-obligating, shahada 'ala al-shahada (branch testimony) is only valid if the original witness deputizes the branch witness and transfers the testimony to the judge's court.
Deputyship (inaba) and transfer (naql) are essential.
3
Identify the required conditions
Note the two conditions: (1) the original witness must appoint the branch witness as his deputy (inaba), and (2) the testimony must be transferred to the judge's court (naql). The branch witness must also undertake to bear the testimony (tahmil).
These conditions are derived from the principle that testimony is not self-obligating.
4
Apply the rule to a scenario
Imagine person A testifies in court. Person B hears that testimony. Can B later testify in a different court about what A said? According to Hanafi, no—unless A deputized B and the testimony was transferred to the judge's court.
This application clarifies the practical effect of the principle.
5
Recognize the cross-madhhab difference
The passage notes that some schools do not require explicit deputyship if the branch witness hears the original testimony directly. This is a point of valid ikhtilaf.
Understanding the difference helps in comparative fiqh.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۶۳) اَلشَّهَادَةُ غَيْرُ مُوجِبَةٍ بِنَفْسِهَا. ترجمہ: شہادت بذات خود کسی چیز کو واجب کرنے والی نہیں ہے۔ تشریح: مذکورہ اصول کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ شہادت از خود دعوی کو ثابت نہیں کر سکتی اور نہ ہی اُس سے کوئی چیز لازم ہوسکتی ہے۔ صاحب ہدایہ مذکورہ اصول ذکر کر کے یہ بتلارہے ہیں کہ شہادت کی ایک قسم شہادت علی الشہادت ہے، یعنی گواہی پر گواہی دینا، جب تک اصل گواہ اپنی گواہی پر کسی کو نائب نہیں بنائے گا اور اُسے مجلس قضاء میں نیابت نہیں سونے گا اس وقت تک مذکورہ نائب کے لیے اصلی گواہ کی شہادت کو سن کر شہادت دینا جائز نہیں ہو گا۔ اس لیے کہ اصل کی شہادت بذاتِ خود کسی حکم کی موجب نہیں ہے بلکہ یہ شہادت قاضی کی مجلس میں ادا کرنے سے موجب ہوگی، چنانچہ جب اصل شاہد قاضی کی مجلس میں اپنی شہادت ادا کر کے اسے دوسری کی طرف منتقل کرے گا اور دوسرے کو دو تکمیل شہادت کا نائب بنائے گا اس وقت شہادت موجب حکم ہوگی، اور دوسرے کے لیے اس شہادت کے ذریعے حق دلوانا درست اور جائز ہوگا۔ قوله ومنه ما لا يثبت حكمه بنفسه مثل الشهادة على الشهادة) فإذا سمع شاهدا يشهد بشيء لم يجز له أن يشهد على شهادته إلا أن يشهده لأن الشهادة غیر موجبة بنفسها وإنما تصير موجبة بالنقل إلى مجلس القضاء فلا بد فيها من الإنابة والتحميل ولم يوجد . (الجوهرة النيرة كتاب الشهادة، ج ۲ ص ۲۲۸) فإذا سمع شاهدا يشهد بشيء لم يجز له أن يشهد على شهادته إلا أن يشهده عليه) بضم الباقى يشهد لأنه مجهول (لأن الشهادة أى شهادة الأصول (غير موجبة بنفسها وفى بعض النسخ غير مثبتة بنفسها وإنما تصير) أى الشهادة موجبة بالنقل إلى مجلس القضاء، فلا بد من الإنابة والتحميل) أى لا بد من الإنابة بتحمل الشهادة في الفرع حتى ينقلها الفرع إلى مجلس القاضي ...... ( ولم يوجد) أى كل واحد من الإنابة والتحميل. (البناية: كتاب الشهادة، ج ۹ ص ۱۲۴) الهداية كتاب الشهادة، ج ۳ ص ۱۶۵
(63) Testimony is not a cause of obligation by itself. Translation: Testimony by itself does not make anything obligatory. Explanation: The meaning of the aforementioned principle is that testimony cannot prove a claim by itself, nor can anything become obligatory from it. The author of al-Hidayah, after mentioning this principle, explains that one type of testimony is shahada ‘ala al-shahada, i.e., witness upon witness. As long as the original witness does not appoint someone as his deputy for his testimony and entrust him with deputyship in the judge’s court, it is not permissible for that deputy to testify by hearing the original witness’s testimony. Because the original testimony is not a cause of obligation by itself; rather, it becomes a cause only by being transmitted to the judge’s court. Therefore, when the original witness performs his testimony in the judge’s court and then transfers it to another and makes that other his deputy for completing the testimony, then the testimony becomes a cause of ruling, and it is valid for the other to establish the right through that testimony. His saying: ‘And from it is that which does not establish its ruling by itself, like testimony upon testimony.’ If he hears a witness testifying about something, it is not permissible for him to testify upon his testimony unless he makes him a witness, because testimony is not a cause by itself; rather, it becomes a cause by transmission to the judge’s court. Therefore, deputyship and bearing (of testimony) are necessary, and they were not found. (al-Jawhara al-Nayyira, Book of Testimony, vol. 2, p. 228) ‘If he hears a witness testifying about something, it is not permissible for him to testify upon his testimony unless he makes him a witness concerning it’ – with a damma on the remaining ‘yashhad’ because it is passive – ‘because testimony, i.e., the testimony of the original witnesses, is not a cause by itself, and in some copies it says it does not establish by itself; rather it becomes a cause by transmission to the judge’s court. Therefore, deputyship and bearing are necessary, i.e., it is necessary that the branch witness undertakes the bearing of testimony so that he may transmit it to the judge’s court... and they were not found, i.e., each of the two: deputyship and bearing.’ (al-Binaya, Book of Testimony, vol. 9, p. 124) al-Hidayah, Book of Testimony, vol. 3, p. 165.
Source pages p. 103

Commentary
This passage presents the Hanafi principle that testimony (shahada) does not obligate anything by itself. It only becomes effective when performed in the judge's court (bi al-naql ila majlis al-qada). This principle is particularly relevant for shahada ‘ala al-shahada (witness upon witness), where a branch witness (fir’) wishes to testify based on the original witness's (asl) testimony. The author explains that the original witness must have explicitly deputized (inaba) the branch witness and transferred the testimony to the court. Without such deputyship, the branch witness cannot testify, because the original testimony is not inherently binding; it is the act of presenting it before the judge that gives it legal effect. The text quotes from al-Jawhara al-Nayyira and al-Binaya to support this, emphasizing that both deputyship (inaba) and bearing (tahammul) are necessary. This is the relied-upon position in the Hanafi school.

Key Terms
شهادة على الشهادة (shahādah ʻalā al-shahādah): Testimony upon testimony; a branch witness testifying based on the testimony of an original witness.
إنابة (inābah): Deputyship; the original witness appointing the branch witness as his representative to transmit the testimony.
تحميل (taḥmīl): Bearing (of testimony); the branch witness undertaking to transmit the testimony.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
Shahada 'ala al-shahada is only valid when the original witness deputizes the branch witness and the testimony is transferred to the judge's court, because testimony is not self-obligating.

The Principle that Handwriting Resembles Handwriting
Maxim on handwriting in testimony

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi principle 'al-khattu yushbihu al-khatta' and explain its application in legal testimony.

Core Idea
Handwriting resemblance cannot serve as conclusive proof — ambiguity in likeness bars certainty.

In Hanafi testimony law, certainty is paramount. The maxim 'al-khattu yushbihu al-khatta' warns that because one person's handwriting can resemble another's, a judge cannot base a ruling solely on handwriting similarity. This lesson explores the principle and its practical implication for shahadat.

Guided Path
1
State the maxim in Arabic
Recite the Arabic text: الخط يشبه الخط
Memorize it verbatim.
2
Translate the maxim
Provide the literal meaning: 'Handwriting resembles handwriting.'
3
Explain the legal implication
Understand that this maxim cautions against relying on handwriting alone for evidence due to the possibility of imitation.
Certainty cannot be built on mere resemblance.
4
Apply to a testimony scenario
Consider a case where a document's handwriting is similar to the defendant's. Explain why the judge cannot accept it as proof without corroboration.
The maxim bars sole reliance on handwriting.

Commentary
This passage introduces the Hanafi legal maxim 'al-khattu yushbihu al-khatta' (handwriting resembles handwriting). This maxim is used as a cautionary principle in testimony and documentation: because handwriting can be imitated or similar, one cannot rely solely on the appearance of handwriting for certainty. For example, a judge cannot base a ruling purely on the similarity of handwriting without additional evidence. This maxim complements the earlier principles regarding voice and testimony, emphasizing that ambiguous evidence based on resemblance is insufficient for legal decisions.

Key Terms

The Maxim 'Writing Resembles Writing' and Its Effect on Testimony
Definition and application of the maxim 'al-khattu yushbihu al-khatt' in testimony

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi maxim 'al-khattu yushbihu al-khatt' and apply it to determine when testimony based on one's handwriting is valid.

Core Idea
Writing resembles writing, so certainty is lacking; testimony requires recollection, not mere handwriting recognition.

This lesson examines a key Hanafi evidentiary maxim that distinguishes between recognizing one's handwriting and knowing the content of the testimony. The Hanafi school requires actual memory of the event for valid testimony; seeing one's handwriting is insufficient due to the resemblance of scripts. The passage also draws an analogy to testimony upon testimony, emphasizing that testimony becomes effective only when performed before the qadi.

Guided Path
1
Identify the maxim and its literal meaning
The maxim is 'al-khattu yushbihu al-khatt' (الْخَطُّ يَشْبَهُ الْخَطَّ), meaning 'writing resembles writing'. Understand that this is a legal principle used to argue that handwriting alone does not provide certain knowledge of its content.
The maxim is straightforward but has significant implications for evidence law.
2
Understand the legal context of testimony
Testimony (shahada) in Hanafi fiqh requires absolute certainty (yaqin) about the matter. This is because testimony can determine rights and obligations. The passage distinguishes between 'tahammul' (bearing the testimony) and 'ada' (performing it in court).
Testimony upon testimony (shahada 'ala al-shahada) also requires proper delegation in court.
3
Apply the maxim to the scenario of seeing one's own handwriting
Consider a witness who sees his own handwriting on a document but has no memory of the event. The maxim says that because one's writing can resemble another's, seeing it does not produce certainty. Therefore, he cannot testify unless he actually remembers the testimony.
The same ruling applies even if the handwriting is uniquely his, because resemblance is possible.
4
Note the Hanafi consensus on this ruling
The passage states that this is the position of Imam Abu Hanifa and the two disciples (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad). It is the relied-upon (mufta bihi) ruling in the Hanafi school.
This unanimity within the school strengthens the authority of the position.
5
Recognize the cross-madhhab difference
Some other schools may allow testimony based on reliable handwriting, but the Hanafis insist on actual memory. Understand that the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf) affects how evidence is evaluated in court.
This is a legitimate area of scholarly difference (ikhtilaf).

( ولم يوجد) أى كل واحد من الإنابة والتحميل. (البناية: كتاب الشهادة، ج ۹ ص ۱۲۴) الهداية كتاب الشهادة، ج ۳ ص ۱۶۵ اصول ہدایہ ثالث ہوتا ہے، لہذا محض خط دیکھ کر گواہی دینا درست نہیں ہے۔ ۱۰۵ صاحب ہدایہ مذکورہ اصول ذکر کر کے یہ انکار ہے ہیں کہ گواہ کے لئے یہ جائز نہیں ہے کہ وہ محض اپنے محلے کو جس پر گواہی لکھی ہوئی ہے دیکھ کر گواہی دے، جب تک اس کو وہ مقدمہ اور معاملہ یاد نہ آئے ، یعنی محض سابقہ تحریر دیکھ کر گواہی نہیں دے سکتے ، جب تک اسے معاملہ یاد نہ آجائے کہ یہ فلاں معاملہ اور مقدمہ تھا، اس لیے کہ ایک تحریر دوسری کے مشابہ ہوتی ہے اور جب تک مقدمہ یاد نہیں آئے گا اس وقت تک گواہ کو کسی بھی مقدمے کا قطعی طور پر علم حاصل نہیں ہو گا اور علم کے بغیر گواہی دینا درست نہیں ہے، اس لیے محض تحریر دیکھ کر گواہی نہیں دے سکتے۔ ولا يحل للشاهد إذا رأى خطه أن يشهد إلا أن يذكر الشهادة، لأن الخط يشبه الخط، فلم يحصل العلم، وهذا قول الإمام، وعليه مشى الأئمة الملتزمون للتصحيح اللباب) في شرح الكتاب: كتاب الشهادة، ج۴ ص ۵۹) (قَوْلُهُ وَلَا يَحِلُّ لِلشَّاهِدِ إِذَا رَأَى خَطَّهُ أَنْ يَشْهَدَ إِلَّا أَنْ يَتَذَكَّرَ الشَّهَادَةَ لِأَنَّ الْخَطَّ يُشْبِهُ الْخَطَّ فَلَمْ يَحْضُلُ لَهُ الْعِلْمُ بِهِ بِيَقِينِ وَهَذَا قَوْلُهُمَا. The rule: testimony upon testimony, i.e., giving testimony on testimony, is not permissible until the original witness appoints a deputy for his testimony and delegates him in the court of qada. At that time, it is not permissible for the mentioned deputy to give testimony upon hearing the original witness's testimony, because the original testimony by itself does not necessitate any ruling; it necessitates the ruling only by being performed in the court of the qadi. Thus, when the original witness, having performed his testimony in the qadi's court, transfers it to another and makes that other his deputy for completing the testimony, then the testimony becomes effective, and it is valid for the other to claim the right through this testimony. (64) al-khattu yushbihu al-khatt. Translation: One writing resembles another writing. Explanation: The meaning of this principle is that one person's handwriting resembles another's. The statement: 'and from it is that which does not establish its ruling by itself, like testimony upon testimony.' So if he hears a witness testifying about something, it is not permissible for him to testify on his testimony unless he makes him a witness because testimony does not necessitate by itself; it only becomes necessitating by transfer to the court of qada. Thus, delegation and burden (tahammul) are necessary. And they do not exist. ... It is not permissible for a witness, when he sees his own handwriting, to testify unless he remembers the testimony, because writing resembles writing, so certainty is not obtained. This is the saying of Imam (Abu Hanifa), and upon this the scholars committed to correction have proceeded. His saying: 'and it is not permissible for the witness when he sees his handwriting to testify unless he remembers the testimony because writing resembles writing, so he does not obtain certain knowledge by it, and this is the saying of the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad).'
Source pages p. 104

Commentary
This passage defines and explains the Hanafi legal maxim 'al-khattu yushbihu al-khatt' (writing resembles writing) in the context of shahada (testimony). The passage opens with a discussion of shahada 'ala al-shahada (testimony on testimony), emphasizing that a deputy witness cannot testify until the original witness has formally presented his testimony in the qadi's court and appointed a deputy. The reason is that testimony does not create a legal effect by itself; it only becomes effective when performed before the qadi. Then the passage introduces the maxim at hand: writings can be similar, so merely seeing one's own handwriting does not provide certain knowledge of the content. Therefore, a witness cannot testify based solely on seeing his writing; he must actually remember the event. The passage cites two sources: Al-Jawhara al-Nayyira and Al-Binaya, and notes that both Imam Abu Hanifa and the two disciples (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) agree on this ruling. The key point is that certainty of knowledge is required for valid testimony, and writing alone does not guarantee that.

Key Terms
الخَطّ (al-khatt): Handwriting; the written script of a person
الشهادة (al-shahada): Testimony in court; giving evidence
النيابة (al-niyaba): Deputyship; a person appointed to perform testimony on behalf of another

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the reason behind the Hanafi ruling that a witness cannot testify based solely on seeing his own handwriting?
A) Because writing can be forged
B) Because writing resembles writing and certainty is not achieved
C) Because the witness must be present in court
D) Because testimony requires two witnesses

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi maxim 'al-khattu yushbihu al-khatt' establishes that testimony requires certain knowledge; handwriting recognition without memory is insufficient.

The Maxim: Possession is the Strongest Proof of Ownership
Definition and explanation of a legal maxim

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi maxim 'al-yadu aqsa ma yustadallu bihi al-milk' and apply it to determine the evidentiary weight of possession in ownership disputes.

Core Idea
Possession is the strongest evidence of ownership, but it is rebuttable by superior proof.

In Hanafi property law, when two parties dispute ownership of an object, the person in physical possession holds a critical advantage. This lesson unpacks the maxim that possession is the strongest proof of ownership. We will explore what this means for evidence in court and why it is not an absolute claim.

Guided Path
1
Identify the maxim's components
Break down the Arabic phrase 'al-yadu aqsa ma yustadallu bihi al-milk'. al-yad refers to possession, aqsa means strongest or farthest reaching, ma yustadallu bihi means that by which inference is made, al-milk is ownership. Understand each term's legal weight.
This is a definitional step; the maxim itself is concise.
2
Understand the legal effect
The maxim establishes that possession is prima facie evidence of ownership. In a dispute, the possessor is presumed the owner unless the opponent brings stronger evidence. This is a rule of evidence, not a substantive right.
The burden of proof shifts to the challenger.
3
Distinguish from absolute proof
The word 'aqsa' indicates highest degree among proofs, not absolute proof. Possession can be overcome by clear documentary evidence, witnesses, or admissions. Recognize that the maxim is rebuttable.
This avoids the common misunderstanding that possession equals ownership.
4
Apply to a simple scenario
Imagine A is holding a book; B claims it is his. According to the maxim, A's possession supports A's ownership. B must provide stronger evidence (e.g., receipt, witnesses) to rebut. Work through the inference step by step.
This is a foundational application for beginners.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۲۵) الْيَدُ أَقْصَى مَا يُسْتَدَلُّ بِهِ الْمِلْكُ .. ترجمہ: قبضہ ان دلائل میں سے اعلی دلیل ہے جن سے ملکیت پر استدلال کیا جاتا ہے۔ تشریح : مذکورہ اصول کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ جو چیز کسی کے قبضے میں ہو تو اس کا یہ قبضہ ملکیت پر استدلال کئے جانے والے دلائل میں سے اعلیٰ درجہ ہے، یعنی قبضہ سے ملکیت پر استدلال کیا جاسکتا ہے۔ صاحب ہدایہ مذکورہ اصول ذکر کر کے یہ بتلارہے ہیں کہ اگر کسی آدمی نے دوسرے

Explanation: The meaning of this principle is that if a thing is in someone's possession, then this possession is the highest degree among proofs used to infer ownership, i.e., ownership can be inferred from possession. The author of Al-Hidayah mentions this principle and states that if a person...

Commentary
This passage introduces the Hanafi legal maxim 'al-yadu aqsa ma yustadallu bihi al-milk' (possession is the strongest proof of ownership). The Urdu commentary explains that when an object is in a person's physical possession (yad), that possession serves as the primary and strongest evidence of ownership. The author of Al-Hidayah is cited as using this principle to argue that possession is a valid basis for inferring ownership. Although the text is cut off, the core idea is clear: in legal disputes, the person in possession is presumed to be the owner unless there is strong contrary evidence. This principle is fundamental in Hanafi property law and judicial proceedings.

Key Terms
اليد (al-yad): Possession; physical control or custody of an object
الملك (al-milk): Ownership; the legal right of exclusive possession and use of property
أقصى ما يستدل به (aqsa ma yustadallu bihi): The highest or strongest proof by which inference is made

Testimony Based on Handwriting Requires Remembering the Case
Explaining the ruling on testifying using one's own handwriting

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on testifying based on handwriting and explain why certain knowledge is required.

Core Idea
Testimony requires certainty; handwriting alone cannot provide it.

In this lesson, we examine a specific ruling from al-Hidayah: a witness cannot testify simply by recognizing his own handwriting on a document. The reason is fundamental to Hanafi law – certainty ('ilm) is a prerequisite for shahada. Understanding this reinforces the importance of knowledge over assumption in Islamic evidence law.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is testifying based on seeing one's own handwriting without independently remembering the case. The ruling is haram (not permissible).
The text uses 'لا يحل' which indicates a prohibition.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is: 'because handwriting resembles handwriting (al-khatt yushbihu al-khatt), so certainty is not attained.'
This is a rational proof (dalil aqli) based on the similarity of lines.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The similarity of handwriting means that seeing one's own writing does not produce certain knowledge that the specific case is remembered. Certainty is a condition for testimony, so without it the testimony is invalid.
This connects the proof to the ruling via the requirement of 'ilm.
4
Note the within-school attribution
The text attributes the ruling both to Imam Abu Hanifa (قول الإمام) and to the Sahibayn (قولهما). This shows that the ruling is unanimously accepted in the Hanafi school, despite the different transmissions.
There is no substantive disagreement; the thamarah al-khilaf is none.
5
Evaluate the tarjih
Since all major authorities agree, the ruling is mufta bihi and well-established.
The author of al-Hidayah and later commentators affirm this ruling.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
صاحب ہدایہ مذکورہ اصول ذکر کر کے یہ انکار ہے ہیں کہ گواہ کے لئے یہ جائز نہیں ہے کہ وہ محض اپنے محلے کو جس پر گواہی لکھی ہوئی ہے دیکھ کر گواہی دے، جب تک اس کو وہ مقدمہ اور معاملہ یاد نہ آئے ، یعنی محض سابقہ تحریر دیکھ کر گواہی نہیں دے سکتے ، جب تک اسے معاملہ یاد نہ آجائے کہ یہ فلاں معاملہ اور مقدمہ تھا، اس لیے کہ ایک تحریر دوسری کے مشابہ ہوتی ہے اور جب تک مقدمہ یاد نہیں آئے گا اس وقت تک گواہ کو کسی بھی مقدمے کا قطعی طور پر علم حاصل نہیں ہو گا اور علم کے بغیر گواہی دینا درست نہیں ہے، اس لیے محض تحریر دیکھ کر گواہی نہیں دے سکتے۔ (ولا يحل للشاهد إذا رأى خطه أن يشهد إلا أن يذكر الشهادة)، لأن الخط يشبه الخط، فلم يحصل العلم، وهذا قول الإمام، وعليه مشى الأئمة الملتزمون للتصحيح اللباب) في شرح الكتاب: كتاب الشهادة، ج۴ ص ۵۹) (قَوْلُهُ وَلَا يَحِلُّ لِلشَّاهِدِ إِذَا رَأَى خَطَّهُ أَنْ يَشْهَدَ إِلَّا أَنْ يَتَذَكَّرَ الشَّهَادَةَ لِأَنَّ الْخَطَّ يُشْبِهُ الْخَطَّ فَلَمْ يَحْضُلْ لَهُ الْعِلْمُ بِهِ بِيَقِينِ وَهَذَا قَوْلُهُمَا. (الجوهرة النيرة: كتاب الشهادة، ج ۲ ص ۲۲۸) الهداية كتاب الشهادة، ج ۳ ص ١٦٦
The author of Hidayah mentions this principle and denies that it is permissible for a witness to testify just by looking at his own paper on which the testimony is written, until he remembers the case. That is, he cannot testify solely by looking at the previous writing until he remembers the case that this is that particular case. Because one writing resembles another, and as long as the case is not remembered, the witness will not have certain knowledge of any case, and testifying without knowledge is not correct. So he cannot testify merely by looking at the writing. (And it is not permissible for the witness, when he sees his own handwriting, to testify unless he remembers the testimony), because handwriting resembles handwriting, so knowledge is not attained. This is the saying of Imam [Abu Hanifa], and the scholars committed to correction acted upon it (al-Lubab). In Sharh al-Kitab: Kitab al-Shahada, vol.4 p.59. (His saying: 'And it is not permissible for the witness when he sees his own handwriting to testify unless he remembers the testimony, because handwriting resembles handwriting, so he does not attain certain knowledge by it, and this is the saying of the two [Abu Yusuf and Muhammad].' (al-Jawhara al-Nira: Kitab al-Shahada, vol.2 p.228) al-Hidayah Kitab al-Shahada, vol.3 p.166.
Source pages p. 105

Commentary
This passage is an expansion of the Hidayah's ruling on a witness testifying on the basis of his own written record. The author explains that a witness cannot rely solely on seeing his own handwriting in a document to testify; he must actually recall the specific case. The reason provided is that one line of handwriting can closely resemble another, so looking at the writing does not produce the certain knowledge ('ilm) required for valid testimony. The text then cites two versions of the same ruling from different sources: one attributing it to Imam Abu Hanifa (قول الإمام) and another attributing it to the Sahibayn (قولهما), Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani. Both affirm the same prohibition. This illustrates that within the Hanafi school, there is no practical disagreement on this point; the ruling is well-established. The reliance on rational proof (that lines can resemble each other) demonstrates the Hanafi method of istidlal (deduction) in legal reasoning.

Key Terms
شاهد (shahid): A person who gives testimony in a legal case.
خط (khatt): Handwriting or script of the witness.
شهادة (shahada): Testimony or bearing witness in court.
علم ('ilm): Certain knowledge, as opposed to conjecture or suspicion.

Key Terms from Source Passage

D) Because the testimony would be considered hearsay.

Key Takeaway
A Hanafi witness cannot rely on his own handwriting to testify; he must independently remember the case to satisfy the condition of certain knowledge.

Possession as Proof of Ownership in Testimony
Explaining that possession is the primary indicator of ownership for testimony

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule that possession is the strongest evidence of ownership and apply it to determine the validity of testimony based on observed possession, including the exception for slaves.

Core Idea
Possession is the highest proof of ownership — testimony can be based on observed possession except for slaves.

This lesson examines the legal principle 'al-yad aqsa ma yustadallu bihi al-milk', which establishes physical possession as the primary indicator of ownership. The passage from al-Hidayah and its commentaries explains that a witness who sees someone in possession of an item (other than slaves) may testify that it belongs to that person. This ruling is grounded in customary practice and rational inference, making possession the central reference point for inferring ownership in all modes of acquisition.

Guided Path
1
Identify the legal principle and its scope
The principle 'al-yad aqsa ma yustadallu bihi al-milk' establishes possession as the highest proof of ownership. It applies to all property except slaves.
The term 'aqsa' means 'the highest', not 'the only'.
2
Examine the ruling for testimony
The passage states that a witness who sees property (other than slaves) in someone's possession may testify that it belongs to that person.
This is based on the principle that possession is sufficient evidence.
3
Understand the proof (dalil)
The proof is rational: possession is the reference point (marji' al-dalalah) in all causes of ownership (gift, inheritance, charity, etc.), so it suffices as evidence.
This is a dalil aqli (rational proof), not a direct scriptural text.
4
Note the exception for slaves
Slaves are excluded because of their special status; their ownership may require additional proof beyond mere possession.
The text explicitly excepts al-raqiq (slaves/slave-girls).
5
Apply the rule to a scenario
For example, if a witness sees a watch in Zaid's hand, then later sees it in Bakr's hand, the witness may testify for Zaid based on Zaid's prior possession.
This scenario is directly from the passage in al-Inayah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

(البحر الرائق: كتاب الشهادة، ج۷ ص ۷۵) رَجُلٌ رَأَى عَيْنًا فِي يَدِ آخَرَ ثُمَّ رَآهَا فِي يَدِ غَيْرِهِ وَالْأَوَّلُ يَدَّعِي عَلَيْهِ الْمِلْكَ وَسِعَهُ أَنْ يَشْهَدَ بِأَنَّهُ لِلْمُدَّعِى، لأنَّ الْيَدَ أَقْصَى مَا يُسْتَدَلُّ بِهِ عَلَى الْمِلْكِ إِذْ هِيَ مَرْجِعُ الدَّلَالَةِ فِي الْأَسْبَابِ كُلِّهَا. (العناية: كتاب الشهادة، ج۷ ص ۳۹۳) الهداية كتاب الشهادة، باب من يقبل شهادته ومن لا يقبل، ج ۳ ص ١٦٨
(25) Possession is the highest of the proofs by which ownership is deduced. Translation: Possession is among the strongest proofs for inferring ownership. Explanation: The meaning of this principle is that if something is in someone's possession, then this possession is of the highest degree among the proofs used to infer ownership; that is, ownership can be inferred from possession. The author of Hidayah mentions this principle and states that if a person sees in another's possession something other than a slave or slave-girl, for example cloth, a watch, etc., then it is permissible for him to testify that this thing belongs to that person, because possession is the strongest proof for inferring ownership. So when a witness sees it in his possession, this possession is evidence that it is his property. Possession itself is the point of reference for indication in all causes of ownership, and on its basis the ownership of the possessor over the possessed item is recognized. Thus, in gifts, inheritance, charity, etc., ownership is inferred from the possessor and his possession. Therefore, upon seeing someone in possession of something, one can testify that the possessed item is his property. (His saying: 'And whoever has in his hand something other than a slave, you may testify that it is his') because possession is the highest proof for ownership, as it is the reference point for indication in all causes, so it suffices. (al-Bahr al-Ra'iq: Kitab al-Shahada, vol.7 p.75) A man saw an article in the hand of another, then he saw it in the hand of someone else, and the first claims ownership against him; he is allowed to testify that it belongs to the claimant, because possession is the highest proof for ownership, as it is the reference point for indication in all causes. (al-Inayah: Kitab al-Shahada, vol.7 p.393) al-Hidayah Kitab al-Shahada, Bab man yuqbal shahadatuhu wa man la yuqbal, vol.3 p.168.
Source pages p. 105

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof regarding the evidentiary value of possession (yad) in matters of ownership. The principle 'al-yad aqsa ma yustadallu bihi al-milk' establishes that physical possession is the strongest indicator of ownership. The author explains that if a witness sees property (other than slaves, as slaves have a distinct rule) in someone's possession, he may testify that the property belongs to that person. This is because possession serves as the foundational evidence (marji' al-dalalah) in all causes of ownership, such as gift, inheritance, and charity. The text cites two additional Arabic texts from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq and al-Inayah that confirm this rule, including a scenario where the same item is seen in two different hands, and the witness may testify for the original claimant based on prior possession. This ruling is based on rational deduction (istidlal) from customary practice and legal reasoning, not on a direct scriptural text. The exception for slaves indicates that possession alone may not suffice for slaves because of other considerations.

Key Terms
يد (yad): Physical possession or control over an item, used as evidence of ownership.
ملك (milk): Ownership or proprietorship of property.
قابض (qabid): The person who has physical possession of an item.
مرجع الدلالة (marji' al-dalalah): The point of reference or foundation for legal indication. Here, it means that possession is the primary basis for inferring ownership in all causes of acquisition.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
Possession (yad) is the strongest evidence of ownership, allowing testimony based solely on observed possession, with the exception of slaves.

Testimony with Self-Interest Is Not Accepted
Stating the rule that testimony benefiting the witness is rejected

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the rule that a witness with any personal interest is disqualified and apply it to new scenarios.

Core Idea
Any witness with personal benefit is rejected due to tuhma.

This lesson introduces a foundational principle in Hanafi testimony law: a witness must be free from any personal interest in the case. The rule is stated concisely and is meant to be memorized. We will break down the key terms and explore its application.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the ruling
The act is giving testimony (shahada). The ruling is 'la tuqbal' (not accepted). This is a categorical prohibition.
The testimony is invalid (batil) if any self-interest exists.
2
Understand the scope of 'min wajh'
The phrase 'min wajh' (in any way) covers all forms of personal benefit—direct financial gain, family ties, enmity, etc.
This is broader than just monetary interest.
3
Recognize the underlying cause: tuhma
The reason for rejection is tuhma (suspicion of bias). The law presumes that self-interest may lead to false testimony.
Tuhma is a key concept in Hanafi law for disqualifying witnesses.
4
Apply to examples
Consider a partner testifying in a case involving the partnership, or a parent testifying for a child in a custody case. Both are disqualified.
The interest need not be certain; the mere possibility suffices.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب من يُقبل شهادته ومن لا يُقبل (٢٦) اَلشَّهَادَةُ إِذَا كَانَتْ لِنَفْسِهِ مِنْ وَجُهِ لَا تُقْبَلُ . ترجمہ: گواہی میں اگر گواہ کا من وجہ فائدہ ہو تو گواہی قبول نہیں ہوگی۔ تشریح: مذکورہ اصول کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ ہر ایسی گواہی جس میں من وجہ گواہ کا فائدہ ہو تو وہ گواہی مستر د ہوگی قبول نہیں ہوگی، کیونکہ ایسی گواہی میں تہمت ہے۔
Chapter: Who is accepted as a witness and who is not. (26) Testimony, if it benefits the witness himself in any way, is not accepted. Translation: In testimony, if the witness has a benefit (of any kind), the testimony will not be accepted. Explanation: The meaning of this principle is that any testimony in which the witness has any kind of personal benefit will be rejected and not accepted, because such testimony involves suspicion (tuhma).
Source pages p. 106

Commentary
This is a ruling statement from a chapter on accepted and rejected witnesses. The principle is concise: if a witness has any personal interest in the case, his testimony is inadmissible. The reason given is the presence of suspicion (tuhma) that the witness might be biased. In Hanafi law, this rule applies to various scenarios, such as a partner testifying for the partnership, a parent for a child (in certain cases), or a person testifying for his own debtor. The goal is to ensure impartiality and integrity of testimony. No proof is provided in this excerpt; it is a foundational rule memorized by students.

Key Terms
شهادة (shahada): Testimony in court.
من وجه (min wajh): In some way or from some aspect. It indicates that even an indirect or partial benefit disqualifies the testimony.
تہمت (tuhma): Suspicion or accusation of bias. The presence of tuhma makes the testimony unacceptable.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is a witness's testimony rejected if he has a personal interest in the case?
A) Because the witness is not reliable due to suspicion of bias.
B) Because the witness needs to be a neutral party.
C) Because the interest makes the testimony hearsay.
D) Because the court requires at least two witnesses without interest.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi rule is clear: any testimony with personal benefit, even indirect, is invalid due to the presumption of bias (tuhma).

Testimony Based on Possession (Yad) Indicates Ownership
Ruling on testifying ownership based on possession (yad) with proof

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on testifying ownership based on possession (yad) and apply the legal maxim 'al-yadu aqsa ma yustadallu bihi ala al-milk' to determine when such testimony is permissible.

Core Idea
Possession (yad) is the strongest evidence of ownership; you may testify based solely on seeing an item in someone's hand, unless the item is a slave.

In Hanafi law, testimony is a powerful tool for establishing rights. But how certain must a witness be? This passage from al-Hidayah addresses a common scenario: you see someone holding an item. Can you swear in court that the item belongs to that person? The Hanafi school gives a clear answer based on the maxim that possession is the ultimate indicator of ownership.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Item and the Ruling
The passage states that if you see an item (other than a slave) in someone's possession, it is permissible (ja'iz) for you to testify that it belongs to that person.
The item must be physical and movable; slaves are excluded.
2
Understand the Legal Maxim
The proof cited: 'al-yadu aqsa ma yustadallu bihi ala al-milk' – the hand (possession) is the strongest evidence used to indicate ownership. It is the reference point for all causes of ownership (gifts, inheritance, charity).
This is a qawl sahabi or legal principle, not a direct Quranic or hadith text.
3
Apply the Maxim to the Scenario
Because possession is the ultimate indicator, the witness's observation of possession is sufficient to form a legal basis for testimony. No additional evidence like a receipt is required.
The maxim applies to all items except slaves due to their special legal status.
4
Note the Exception for Slaves
Slaves (al-raqiq) are excluded from this ruling. For slaves, possession alone is not enough; more evidence is needed to prove ownership.
This exception highlights that the ruling does not apply to humans with legal personality.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
اصول ہدایہ ثالث
کے قبضہ میں غلام اور باندی کے علاوہ کوئی اور چیز دیکھی ، مثلاً کپڑا ، گھڑی وغیرہ ، تو اس کے لئے یہ جائز ہے کہ وہ اس بات کی گواہی دے کہ یہ چیز فلاں کی ہے، کیونکہ قبضہ ملکیت پر استدلال کئے جانے والے دلائل میں اعلیٰ دلیل ہے، لہذا جب گواہ نے اس کے قبضے میں دیکھی تو یہ قبضہ اس بات کی دلیل ہے کہ یہ اس کی ملکیت ہے۔ قبضہ ہی جملہ اسباب ملک میں مرجع دلالت ہے اور اس کی بنیاد پر شے مقبوضہ پر قابض کی ملکیت تسلیم کی جاتی ہے، چنانچہ هبه، وراثت اور صدقہ وغیرہ میں بھی قابض اور اس کے قبضہ سے ہی شے مقبوضہ پر اس کی ملکیت کا استدلال کیا جاتا ہے، لہذا کسی کو کسی چیز پر قابض دیکھ کر شے مقبوضہ پر اس کی ملکیت کی شہادت دی جاسکتی ہے۔
(قَوْلُهُ وَمَنْ فِي يَدِهِ شَيْءٌ سِوَى الرَّقِيقِ لَك أَنْ تَشْهَدَ أَنَّهُ لَهُ) لِأَنَّ الْيَدَ أَقْصَى مَا يُسْتَدَلُّ بِهِ عَلَى الْمِلْكِ إِذْ هِيَ مَرْجِعُ الدَّلَالَةِ فِي الْأَسْبَابِ كُلِّهَا فَيُكْتَفَى بِهَا.
(البحر الرائق: كتاب الشهادة، ج۷ ص ۷۵) رَجُلٌ رَأَى عَيْنًا فِي يَدِ آخَرَ ثُمَّ رَآهَا فِي يَدِ غَيْرِهِ وَالْأَوَّلُ يَدَّعِي عَلَيْهِ الْمِلْكَ وَسِعَهُ أَنْ يَشْهَدَ بِأَنَّهُ لِلْمُدَّعِى، لأنَّ الْيَدَ أَقْصَى مَا يُسْتَدَلُّ بِهِ عَلَى الْمِلْكِ إِذْ هِيَ مَرْجِعُ الدَّلَالَةِ فِي الْأَسْبَابِ كُلِّهَا. (العناية: كتاب الشهادة، ج۷ ص ۳۹۳) الهداية كتاب الشهادة، باب من يقبل شهادته ومن لا يقبل، ج ۳ ص ١٦٨
Principles of Hidayah, third volume. If someone sees in the possession of another a thing other than a male or female slave, e.g., a cloth, a watch, etc., then it is permissible for him to testify that this thing belongs to so-and-so, because possession is the strongest evidence used to indicate ownership. So when the witness saw it in his possession, this possession is evidence that it is his ownership. Possession is the focal point of indication in all causes of ownership, and on its basis the owner's ownership of the possessed item is acknowledged. Hence, in gifts, inheritance, charity, etc., the owner and his possession are used to infer his ownership of the possessed item. Therefore, seeing someone in possession of something, one can testify to his ownership of that possessed item. (His statement: "And whoever has in his hand something other than slaves, you may testify that it is his.") Because the hand is the utmost thing used as evidence for ownership, as it is the reference point of indication in all causes, so it is sufficient. (Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq: Kitab al-Shahada, vol. 7 p. 75) A man saw an item in the hand of another, then saw it in the hand of someone else, and the first claims ownership against him; it is permissible for him to testify that it belongs to the claimant, because the hand is the utmost used as evidence for ownership, as it is the reference point of indication in all causes. (Al-‘Inaya: Kitab al-Shahada, vol. 7 p. 393) Al-Hidaya, Kitab al-Shahada, chapter on who is accepted and who is not accepted, vol. 3 p. 168.
Source pages p. 106

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof from the Hanafi school on testifying based on possession. The author explains that if someone sees an item (other than a slave) in another's possession, he may testify that the item belongs to that person, because possession (yad) is the strongest indicator of ownership. The legal maxim 'al-yadu aqsa ma yustadallu bihi 'ala al-milk' is cited: possession is the ultimate evidence for ownership, as it is the reference point for all causes of ownership (hibah, inheritance, charity). The passage quotes al-Bahr al-Ra'iq and al-‘Inayah to reinforce this principle: if a man sees an item in A's hand, then later in B's hand, and A claims it, a witness can testify for A based on the initial possession. This ruling applies to all items except slaves (raqiq), likely due to special rules regarding slave ownership. The authority weight is from Zahir al-Riwayah as it is in al-Hidayah.

Key Terms
اليَد (al-yad): Possession or physical control of an item; used as a legal indicator of ownership.
الرَّقِيق (al-raqīq): Slaves, both male and female; excluded from the ruling that possession alone suffices for testimony.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Yes, because possession is the strongest evidence of ownership for items other than slaves.
B) No, possession is never sufficient for testimony.
C) Only if the watch is a slave.
D) Yes, only for items of great value.

Key Takeaway
Possession (yad) is the ultimate indicator of ownership; you may testify based on it, except for slaves.

Shahadat — Testimony

Testimony Rejected Due to Personal Benefit or Suspicion
Ruling that testimony is rejected if witness gains benefit or suspicion exists

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify and apply the Hanafi rules that testimony is rejected when the witness has personal benefit or suspicion of bias, and explain the reasoning based on connected benefits.

Core Idea
Testimony is rejected if the witness gains any indirect benefit because it becomes self-testimony.

The Hanafi school sets strict impartiality requirements for witnesses. This passage from al-Hidayah presents two foundational principles: testimony is inadmissible if the witness has a personal stake, or if there is suspicion of bias. The author illustrates these with clear examples of close relationships where benefits are shared, such as father-son, spouses, and master-slave. The reasoning relies on the concept of connected benefits (manafi' muttasilah), which makes the testimony equivalent to self-testimony.

Guided Path
1
State the two principles
Read the Arabic and translation to identify the two ruling statements: (26) testimony is not accepted if it is for oneself in some respect, (27) testimony is not accepted if suspicion is present.
These are general rules; the rest of the passage provides examples and reasoning.
2
List the examples given
Identify the specific relationships: father for son and grandson, son for father and grandfather, wife for husband, slave for master, and vice versa.
The examples show that the benefit can be indirect through shared family or ownership ties.
3
Understand the reasoning: connected benefits
The text explains that the benefits (manafi') between these parties are connected (muttasilah), so testifying for the other is like testifying for oneself in some respect. This is the core legal cause (illah) for rejection.
The parallel with zakat (cannot pay zakat to each other) reinforces the idea of intertwined interests.
4
Recognize the role of suspicion (tuhmah)
The second principle states that any testimony where suspicion enters is not accepted. Suspicion naturally arises when benefits are shared, but the rule is broader.
Tuhmah can apply even without direct financial benefit; e.g., close friendship might also create suspicion.
5
Apply the principles to new scenarios
Practice by considering cases like a brother testifying for a brother, or a business partner testifying for a partner. Determine if shared benefits exist.
The Hanafi school extends the principle beyond the listed examples by analogy (qiyas).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب من يُقبل شهادته ومن لا يُقبل
(٢٦) اَلشَّهَادَةُ إِذَا كَانَتْ لِنَفْسِهِ مِنْ وَجُهِ لَا تُقْبَلُ . ترجمہ: گواہی میں اگر گواہ کا من وجہ فائدہ ہو تو گواہی قبول نہیں ہوگی۔ تشریح: مذکورہ اصول کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ ہر ایسی گواہی جس میں من وجہ گواہ کا فائدہ ہو تو وہ گواہی مستر د ہوگی قبول نہیں ہوگی، کیونکہ ایسی گواہی میں تہمت ہے۔
صاحب ہدایہ مذکورہ اصول ذکر کر کے یہ بتلا رہے ہیں کہ باپ کی گواہی بیٹے کے حق میں اور پوتے کے حق میں قبول نہیں ہوگی، اسی طرح بیٹے کی گواہی باپ کی حق میں اور دادا کے حق میں قبول نہیں ہوگی ، اسی طرح بیوی کی گواہی شوہر کے حق میں ، غلام کی گواہی آقا کے حق میں قبول نہیں ہوگی، کیونکہ مذکورہ اشخاص کے حق میں گواہی میں گواہ من وجہ اپنے لئے گواہی دیتا ہے اور ہر ایسی گواہی جس میں گواہ کا اپنا نفع ہوتو وہ قبول نہیں ہوتی۔ یہ مذکورہ بالا تمام وہ افراد ہیں جن کے منافع مشترک ہیں، اور ایک دوسرے کے منافع سے فائدے اٹھاتے ہیں، اس لیے یہ من وجہ اپنی ذات کے لیے گواہی ہے، اور اس میں یہ تہمت بھی ہے کہ فلاں نے اپنے فائدے کے لیے اپنے والد یا بیٹے کے حق میں گواہی دی ہے اور نہ تو اپنی ذات کے لیے انسان کی شہادت مقبول ہوتی ہے اور نہ ہی اپنے نفع اور فائدے کے لیے مقبول ہوتی ہے، اسی طرح ان میں سے کوئی دوسرے کوزکوۃ ادا کرے تو بھی جائز نہیں۔ (۲۷) اَلشَّهَادَةُ إِذَا تَمَكَّنَتْ فِيْهَا التُّهمَةُ لَا تُقْبَلُ . ترجمہ: گواہی میں جب تہمت آ جائے تو قبول نہ ہوگی۔ تشریح : مذکورہ اصول کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ ہر ایسی گواہی جس میں گواہ پر تہمت آتی ہو . وَالْوَلَدِ لَا بَوَيْهِ وَجَدَّيْهِ وَعَكْسِهِ وَأَحَدِ الزَّوْجَيْنِ لِلْآخَرِ، وَالسَّيِّدِ لِعَبْدِهِ وَمُكَاتَبِهِ..... وَلَانَّ الْمَنَافِعَ بَيْنَ هَؤُلَاءِ مُتَّصِلَةٌ وَلِهَذَا لَا يَجُوزُ أَدَاءُ بَعْضِهِمُ الزَّكَاةَ إِلَى بَعْضٍ فَتَكُونُ شَهَادَةً لِنَفْسِهِ مِنْ وَجْهِ فَلَا تُقْبَلُ . (تبيين الحقائق: كتاب الشهادة، باب من تقبل شهادته ومن لا تقبل، ج۴ ص ۲۱۹) لِأَنَّ مَنَافِعَ الْأَمْلَاكِ بَيْنَ الْأَبِ وَبَيْنَ الِابْنِ مُتَّصِلَةٌ، فَكَانَتِ الشَّهَادَةُ لِلْأَبِ شَهَادَةً لِنَفْسِهِ مِنْ وَجْهٍ، وَشَهَادَةُ الْإِنْسَانِ لِنَفْسِهِ لَا تُقْبَلُ (المحيط البرهاني كتاب الشهادات الفصل الثالث، ج ۸ ص ۳۲۵) (الهداية: كتاب الشهادة، باب من يقبل شهادته ومن لا يقبل، ج ٣ ص ١٦٩)
Chapter: Who is accepted as a witness and who is not. (26) Testimony, if it is for himself in some respect, is not accepted. Translation: If the witness has some benefit in the testimony, the testimony will not be accepted. Explanation: The meaning of this principle is that every testimony in which the witness has some benefit is rejected, not accepted, because there is suspicion in such testimony. The author of Hidayah, after mentioning this principle, explains that the testimony of a father for his son and grandson is not accepted; similarly, the testimony of a son for his father and grandfather is not accepted; similarly, the testimony of a wife for her husband, and the testimony of a slave for his master are not accepted, because in testifying for these persons, the witness is in some sense testifying for himself, and every testimony in which the witness has his own benefit is not accepted. These are all persons whose benefits are shared, and they derive benefit from each other's benefits. Therefore, this is in a sense testimony for one's own self, and there is also the suspicion that so-and-so testified for his father or son for his own benefit. And a person's testimony for himself is not accepted, nor for his own benefit and advantage. Similarly, if any of them pays zakat to another, it is not permissible. (27) Testimony in which suspicion has taken hold is not accepted. Translation: When suspicion enters the testimony, it will not be accepted. Explanation: The meaning of this principle is that every testimony in which there is suspicion against the witness... And the child's testimony for his parents and grandparents, and vice versa, and one spouse for the other, and the master for his slave and his mukatab... And because the benefits between these persons are connected, for this reason it is not permissible for any of them to pay zakat to another, so it becomes testimony for himself in some respect and is not accepted. (Tabyin al-Haqa'iq: Kitab al-Shahada, chapter on who is accepted and who is not, vol. 4 p. 219) Because the benefits of properties between father and son are connected, so the testimony for the father is testimony for himself in some respect, and a person's testimony for himself is not accepted. (al-Muhit al-Burhani, Kitab al-Shahadat, third chapter, vol. 8 p. 325) (al-Hidayah: Kitab al-Shahada, chapter on who is accepted and who is not, vol. 3 p. 169).
Source pages p. 106

Commentary
This passage presents two principles from the Hanafi school regarding the admissibility of testimony. The first principle (26) states that testimony is not accepted if the witness has a personal benefit (manfa'ah) in the outcome, even if indirect. The author explains that this includes cases where benefits are shared, such as between father and son, spouses, or master and slave. The reason is that such testimony is considered testimony for oneself in some respect, and testimony for oneself is never accepted. Additionally, there is suspicion (tuhmah) of bias. The passage adds that these relationships also prevent the parties from paying zakat to each other, because their benefits are connected. The second principle (27) generalizes: any testimony in which suspicion is present is not accepted. The Arabic quotes from Tabyin al-Haqa'iq and al-Muhit al-Burhani reinforce the reasoning: the connected benefits make testimony equivalent to self-testimony. The authority weight of these rulings is from Zahir al-Riwayah as they appear in al-Hidayah.

Key Terms
الشَّهَادَة (al-shahādah): Testimony given in court to establish a right; the text discusses when it is admissible.
التُّهمَة (al-tuhmah): Suspicion of bias or self-interest that renders testimony inadmissible.
مَنَافِع (manāfi‘): Benefits or interests that are shared between parties, such as between father and son, making testimony suspect.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, why is a father's testimony for his son not accepted?
A) Because the father is not a reliable witness.
B) Because their benefits are connected, so father is testifying for himself in some sense.
C) Because the son is a minor.
D) Because testimony must always be given by unrelated parties.

Key Takeaway
Testimony is rejected if the witness has any personal benefit or suspicion, because benefits between parties are connected, making it self-testimony.

Shahadat — Testimony
intermediate
10 min
Testimony with Suspicion of Self-Benefit is Rejected
Establishes and illustrates a legal maxim

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi principle that testimony with inherent suspicion of self-benefit is rejected, and apply it to identify which testimonies are invalid in specific relationships.

Core Idea
Testimony that benefits the witness himself is void — even indirect benefit through close relatives or partners.

This passage establishes a foundational principle in Hanafi testimony law: any testimony tainted by suspicion (tuhmah) that the witness may gain personal benefit is automatically rejected. The author of Hidayah illustrates the principle through specific relationships where such suspicion is inherent due to shared interests. Understanding this principle helps us navigate complex cases where personal benefit may be hidden.

Guided Path
1
State the principle
Extract the core maxim from the passage: 'Testimony when suspicion is possible in it is not accepted.' This is the foundational rule.
2
List the relationships covered
Identify the specific relationships mentioned: father-son (including grandfather-grandson), husband-wife, master-slave (including mukatab), and business partners.
These are relationships with connected benefits (manafi' muttasilah).
3
Understand the rationale
Analyze the reasoning: connected benefits mean testifying for the other is like testifying for oneself in one aspect (shahadah li nafsih min wajh). The analogy to zakah (not giving to close relatives) reinforces this.
The proof is rational (dalil 'aqli) based on the connection of benefits.
4
Apply the distinction for partners
Note that a partner's testimony is invalid only if it concerns partnership property; if it is about a matter outside the partnership, there is no suspicion, so it is accepted.
This shows the principle is not simply about the relationship but about the presence of personal benefit.

صاحب ہدایہ مذکورہ اصول ذکر کر کے یہ بتلا رہے ہیں کہ باپ کی گواہی بیٹے کے حق میں اور پوتے کے حق میں قبول نہیں ہوگی، اسی طرح بیٹے کی گواہی باپ کی حق میں اور دادا کے حق میں قبول نہیں ہوگی ، اسی طرح بیوی کی گواہی شوہر کے حق میں ، غلام کی گواہی آقا کے حق میں قبول نہیں ہوگی، کیونکہ مذکورہ اشخاص کے حق میں گواہی میں گواہ من وجہ اپنے لئے گواہی دیتا ہے اور ہر ایسی گواہی جس میں گواہ کا اپنا نفع ہوتو وہ قبول نہیں ہوتی۔ یہ مذکورہ بالا تمام وہ افراد ہیں جن کے منافع مشترک ہیں، اور ایک دوسرے کے منافع سے فائدے اٹھاتے ہیں، اس لیے یہ من وجہ اپنی ذات کے لیے گواہی ہے، اور اس میں یہ تہمت بھی ہے کہ فلاں نے اپنے فائدے کے لیے اپنے والد یا بیٹے کے حق میں گواہی دی ہے اور نہ تو اپنی ذات کے لیے انسان کی شہادت مقبول ہوتی ہے اور نہ ہی اپنے نفع اور فائدے کے لیے مقبول ہوتی ہے، اسی طرح ان میں سے کوئی دوسرے کوزکوۃ ادا کرے تو بھی جائز نہیں۔ (۲۷) اَلشَّهَادَةُ إِذَا تَمَكَّنَتْ فِيْهَا التُّهمَةُ لَا تُقْبَلُ . ترجمہ: گواہی میں جب تہمت آ جائے تو قبول نہ ہوگی۔ تشریح : مذکورہ اصول کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ ہر ایسی گواہی جس میں گواہ پر تہمت آتی ہو وَالْوَلَدِ لا بَوَيْهِ وَجَدَّيْهِ وَعَكْسِهِ وَأَحَدِ الزَّوْجَيْنِ لِلْآخَرِ، وَالسَّيِّدِ لِعَبْدِهِ وَمُكَاتَبِهِ..... وَلَانَّ الْمَنَافِعَ بَيْنَ هَؤُلَاءِ مُتَّصِلَةٌ وَلِهَذَا لَا يَجُوزُ أَدَاءُ بَعْضِهِمُ الزَّكَاةَ إِلَى بَعْضٍ فَتَكُونُ شَهَادَةً لِنَفْسِهِ مِنْ وَجْهِ فَلَا تُقْبَلُ . (تبيين الحقائق: كتاب الشهادة، باب من تقبل شهادته ومن لا تقبل، ج۴ ص ۲۱۹) لأن منافع الأملاك بين الأب وبين الابن متصلة، فكانت الشهادة للأب شهادة لنفسه من وجه، وشهادة الإنسان لنفسه لا تقبل. المحيط البرهاني كتاب الشهادات الفصل الثالث، ج ۸ ص ۳۲۵ الهداية: كتاب الشهادة، باب من يقبل شهادته ومن لا يقبل، ج ٣ ص ١٦٩ مثلا گواہ کا اس میں فائدہ ہو تو ایسی گواہی قبول نہیں کی جائے گی بلکہ مستر دہوگی۔ صاحب ہدایہ مذکورہ اصول ذکر کر کے یہ بتلارہے ہیں کہ ایک شریک کی گواہی دوسرے شریک کے حق میں شے مشترکہ میں قبول نہ ہوگی، کیونکہ اس میں تہمت ہے، اور ہر وہ گواہی جس میں تہمت ہو قبول نہیں ہوتی ، قبول نہ ہونے کی وجہ یہ ہے کہ اپنے نفع کے لیے گواہی ہے، اس میں شریک کے ساتھ ساتھ اس کا بھی نفع ہے اور ہر وہ گواہی جس میں ذاتی نفع ہو وہ قبول نہیں کی جاتی ہے، جب اس کے اپنے حصہ میں گواہی باطل ہے تو شریک کے حصے میں بھی باطل ہوگی، اس لیے کہ شہادت واحدہ میں تجزی نہیں ہوتی ہے۔ اور اگر ایسی چیز میں گواہی دی جس میں وہ شریک نہیں ہے تو گواہی قبول ہوگی، اس لیے کہ اس صورت میں تہمت نہیں ہے اور شہادت لنفسہ کا شبہ نہیں ہے، اس لیے یہ شہادت مقبول ہے۔
The author of Hidayah, after mentioning the principle, explains that a father's testimony for his son and grandson is not accepted, likewise a son's testimony for his father and grandfather, similarly a wife's testimony for her husband, a slave's testimony for his master, because in testifying for these persons, the witness in one aspect testifies for himself, and every testimony in which the witness has his own benefit is not accepted. These are all persons whose interests are shared, and they benefit from each other's interests, so it is in one aspect testimony for oneself, and there is also suspicion that so-and-so testified for his father or son for his own benefit, and neither a person's testimony for himself is accepted nor for his own benefit. Similarly, none of them may pay zakah to another. (27) 'Testimony when suspicion is possible in it is not accepted.' Translation: When suspicion arises in testimony, it will not be accepted. Explanation: The meaning of the aforementioned principle is that every testimony in which there is suspicion on the witness... and the child for his parents and grandparents and vice versa, and one spouse for the other, and the master for his slave and mukatab... and because the benefits between these are connected, therefore it is not permissible for some of them to pay zakah to others, so it becomes testimony for oneself in one aspect, so it is not accepted. (Tabyin al-Haqa'iq: Kitab al-Shahadah, Bab man tuqbal shahadatuhu wa man la tuqbal, vol. 4 p. 219) Because the benefits of properties between father and son are connected, so the testimony for the father is testimony for himself in one aspect, and a person's testimony for himself is not accepted. (Al-Muhit al-Burhani, Kitab al-Shahadat, al-Fasl al-Thalith, vol. 8 p. 325) (Al-Hidayah: Kitab al-Shahadah, Bab man yuqbal shahadatuhu wa man la yuqbal, vol. 3 p. 169) For example, if the witness has benefit in it, such testimony will not be accepted but will be rejected. The author of Hidayah, after mentioning the principle, explains that a partner's testimony for his partner in what is part of their partnership is not accepted, because there is suspicion in it, and every testimony in which there is suspicion is not accepted; the reason for not being accepted is that it is testimony for his own benefit, along with the partner he also has benefit, and every testimony in which there is personal benefit is not accepted. When the testimony is invalid in his own share, it is also invalid in his partner's share, because it is a single testimony and is not divisible. And if he testifies for him in something that is not part of their partnership, it will be accepted, because in that case there is no suspicion and no semblance of testimony for oneself, so this testimony is accepted.
Source pages p. 107

Commentary
This passage presents a fundamental principle of Hanafi testimony law: any testimony tainted by suspicion (tuhmah) that the witness is testifying for his own benefit is rejected. The author first lists specific relationships where such suspicion is inherent: father and child (including grandfather/grandson), husband and wife, master and slave (including mukatab). The underlying rationale is that these parties share connected benefits (manafi' muttasilah) – for example, a father and son often have common financial interests. Therefore, testifying for such a relative is, in essence, testifying for oneself in that respect. The text draws an analogy to zakah: just as one cannot give zakah to close relatives in certain cases, testimony between such parties is also invalid. The principle is then applied to business partners: a partner cannot testify for his co-partner regarding partnership property because it involves his own share; but if the testimony concerns property outside the partnership, it is acceptable. This highlights that the prohibition is based on the nexus of benefits, not merely the relationship. The sources cited (Tabyin, Hidayah, Muhit) confirm this is the established Hanafi position from Zahir al-Riwayah.

Key Terms
التهمة (al-tuhmah): Suspicion or accusation that the witness may be biased or have a personal interest in the outcome of the testimony.
شهادة لنفسه (shahadah li nafsih): Testimony that ultimately benefits the witness himself, rendering it invalid.
شريك (sharik): A business partner with shared ownership and mutual financial interests.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the principle, a partner's testimony for his co-partner is rejected in which case?
A) When the testimony concerns any matter between them.
B) When the testimony concerns the partnership property.
C) When the testimony concerns a third party's debt.
D) When the testimony is about personal property of the partner.

Key Takeaway
Testimony that carries suspicion of self-benefit, whether through close relationships or shared interests, is invalid in Hanafi law.

Fisq in Belief Does Not Bar Testimony
States that fisq in belief does not bar testimony.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi principle that fisq in belief alone does not disqualify a witness and apply it to determine the admissibility of testimony.

Core Idea
Only outward fisq (sinful action) disqualifies a witness; belief alone does not.

This principle draws a sharp line between a witness's creed and his conduct. In Hanafi law, the admissibility of testimony hinges on the witness's outward reliability and justice ('adalah), not on the orthodoxy of his beliefs. A person may hold heretical or innovative views (fisq in belief) yet still be considered upright if his actions are righteous and he is truthful. This leniency reflects the school's focus on practical trustworthiness rather than theological correctness.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the type of fisq
The act under consideration is giving testimony (shahadah). Fisq is divided into two categories: fisq in belief (e.g., holding heretical doctrines) and fisq in action (committing major sins).
The principle only applies when the fisq is limited to belief; if the belief leads to sinful actions, the ruling may differ.
2
State the ruling
The Hanafi ruling: testimony from a person whose fisq is solely in belief is accepted (maqbul). Outward justice is sufficient.
This is the mufta bihi (relied-upon) position.
3
Understand the rationale
The disqualifying effect of fisq is tied to a lack of reliability in testimony. A person with corrupt beliefs but upright actions can still be trusted to testify truthfully, as his outward conduct demonstrates integrity.
The school gives weight to observable behavior rather than internal convictions.
4
Note the cross-madhhab ikhtilaf
Some other schools require the witness to be free from fisq in both belief and action, so they would not accept testimony from a heretic even if righteous in deeds.
This is a mukhtalaf fih issue – a legitimate area of scholarly difference.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۲۸) الْفِسْقُ مِنْ حَيْثُ الْاعْتِقَادِ غَيْرُ مَانِعٍ مِنْ قَبُولِ الشَّهَادَةِ. ترجمہ: وہ فسق جو اعتقاد ہو گواہی کی قبولیت کے لئے مانع نہیں ہے۔
(28) Fisq from the aspect of belief is not a preventer of acceptance of testimony. Translation: That fisq which is in belief is not a barrier for the acceptance of testimony.
Source pages p. 108

Commentary
This short passage introduces a second key principle regarding witness qualification in Hanafi law. The ruling distinguishes between fisq (transgression) in action versus fisq in belief (i.e., heretical or deviant creed without accompanying sinful deeds). According to this principle, a person who holds corrupt beliefs (such as a heretic or innovator) but is righteous in his actions may still have his testimony accepted. The underlying rationale is that the disqualifying effect of fisq is based on the lack of reliability in testimony, which is tied to outward actions and justice ('adalah). Mere deviation in belief, without outward sinful acts, does not necessarily make a person unreliable in giving testimony. However, note that this principle is subject to other conditions; for example, if the belief leads to practical consequences that affect credibility, the ruling may differ. The Hanafi school generally adopts a lenient approach, focusing on the witness's outward justice and reliability rather than delving into theological correctness.

Key Terms
فسق (fisq): Transgression or disobedience; here distinguished between fisq in belief (heresy/innovation) and fisq in action (sinful deeds).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling on the testimony of a person who is a fasiq in belief (e.g., an innovator) but righteous in action?
A) Not accepted.
B) Accepted.
C) Accepted only if he repents.
D) Not accepted unless he is reliable in action.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school accepts testimony from a witness whose fisq is limited to belief, focusing on outward justice rather than theological correctness.

Shahadat — Testimony
beginner
