Ignorance in the Confessed Matter Does Not Invalidate Confession
Explanation that ignorance of the thing confessed does not harm validity

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi principle that jahalah fi al-muqarr bihi does not invalidate iqrar and apply it to cases of ambiguous confessions, including the requirement to clarify.

Core Idea
Ignorance of the thing confessed does not void the confession — the confessor must clarify later.

When someone confesses to a debt but does not specify the item, is the confession valid? The Hanafi school says yes, as long as the confession itself is clear about the obligation; the ambiguity in the object does not invalidate it. This principle from al-Hidayah is a cornerstone in the law of iqrar, balancing the strength of confession with the need for eventual clarity.

Guided Path
1
Read the Principle
Start by reading the Arabic and translation of the principle. Note that it is a concise rule from al-Hidayah: 'Al-jahalah fi al-muqarr bihi la tamna' sihhat al-iqrar.'
Memorize this statement.
2
Define Key Terms
Identify the two critical terms: muqarr bihi (the thing confessed to) and jahalah (ignorance/specification). Understand that jahalah here refers to lack of detail about the object, not about the confession itself.
The confession (iqrar) is a distinct act; its validity depends on the clarity of the obligation, not the precise identity of the object.
3
Apply to the Example
Work through the house possession case: A claims possession of a house without specifying type; defendant confesses. Even if the nature of possession is unknown (jahalah in muqarr bihi), the confession is valid and the house is returned to A.
The confession is accepted because the act of confessing possession is clear, even though the exact type of possession is not specified.
4
Note the Clarification Requirement
The confessor (muqirr) is compelled to provide details (bayan) about the muqarr bihi. This preserves the integrity of the confession while upholding its validity.
The court will enforce this obligation if the confessor does not voluntarily clarify.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۷۳) الْجَهَالَةُ فِى الْمُقِرِّ بِهِ لَا تَمْنَعُ صِحَّةَ الْإِقْرَارِ . .
ترجمہ: مقربہ کی جہالت صحت اقرار کے لئے مانع نہیں ہے۔
تشریح: مذکورہ اصول کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ مقر جس چیز کا اقرار کرتا ہے اگر وہ مجہول ہو تو اقرار درست ہوگا ، مثلاً مقریہ کے لِغُلانِ عَلَيَّ شَيْءٌ “ کہ مجھ پر فلاں کے لیے کچھ ہے،
اصول ہدایہ ثالث
مگر مقر کو تفصیل پر مجبور کیا جائے گا۔
صاحب ہدایہ مذکورہ اصول ذکر کر کے یہ بتلارہے ہیں کہ اگر کسی نے کسی شخص پر مکان پر قبضہ کرنے کا دعوی کیا اور کس قسم کا قبضہ تھا اس کی وضاحت نہ کی ہو، اور مدعلی علیہ ( قابض ) نے اقرار بھی کر لیا کہ یہ مکان واقعی مدعی کے قبضہ میں تھا، تو یہ مکان مدعی کے قبضہ میں واپس دے دیا جائے گا، کیونکہ جس مکان کا اقرار کیا گیا وہ اگر چہ مجہول ہے، مگر یہ جہالت مقربہ میں ہے اور مقربہ کی جہالت اقرار کی صحت سے مانع نہیں ہے، اس لیے مدعلی علیہ کے اقرار کے مطابق مکان واپس مدعی کو دے دیا جائے ، البتہ مقر کو اس کی وضاحت پر پابند کیا جائے گا۔ اسی طرح اگر دو گواہان یہ گواہی دے دیں کہ مدعیٰ علیہ نے یہ اقرار کیا تھا کہ اس کے قبضہ میں موجود مکان مدعی کے ہاتھ میں ہے اور قابض (مدعی علیہ ) کے قبضہ کی نوعیت کی وضاحت بھی نہیں کی تب بھی اس مکان کا فیصلہ مدعی کے حق میں ہوگا۔
Ignorance in the thing confessed does not prevent the validity of confession. Translation: Ignorance of the thing confessed is not a barrier to the validity of confession. Explanation: The meaning of this principle is that if the thing a person confesses to is unknown, then the confession is valid, for example, if someone says 'I owe something to so-and-so.' The author of al-Hidayah mentions this principle and explains: if someone claims possession of a house from another without specifying the type of possession, and the defendant (the possessor) confesses that the house was indeed in the plaintiff's possession, then the house will be returned to the plaintiff's possession, because even though the house confessed to is unknown, this ignorance is in the thing confessed and does not prevent the validity of confession. Therefore, according to the defendant's confession, the house will be returned to the plaintiff, but the confessor will be compelled to detail it. Similarly, if two witnesses testify that the defendant made such a confession, then the house will also be decided in favor of the plaintiff.
Source pages p. 114

Commentary
This passage presents a fundamental Hanafi principle on confessions (iqrar). The passage type is a ruling statement with commentary. The principle states that ignorance (jahalah) regarding the object of confession (al-muqarr bihi) does not invalidate the confession. The author explains this with an example: if someone confesses to owing something unspecified, the confession is valid, but the confessor must later specify what it is. The commentary then applies this to a case where a person claims a house that the defendant possesses, and the defendant confesses the house was in the claimant's possession. Even if the exact nature of possession is unknown, the confession is accepted and the house is returned. The author emphasizes that the confessor will be compelled to detail. This ruling reflects the Hanafi school's practical approach: confessions are taken seriously and are not easily invalidated due to ambiguity, but the confessor is held accountable to clarify. The authority of this ruling is from the Zahir al-Riwayah as found in al-Hidayah.

Key Terms
مقر به (muqarr bihi): The thing or object that is confessed to. In this principle, it refers to the item that the confessor acknowledges is owed or belongs to another.
جهالة (jahalah): Lack of knowledge or specificity regarding the muqarr bihi.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi principle discussed, a person confesses 'I owe something to Zaid' but does not specify what. What is the ruling?
A) The confession is invalid due to ignorance.
B) The confession is valid and the confessor must specify.
C) The confession is valid only if the amount is known.
D) The confession is considered a promise, not a confession.

Key Takeaway
Ignorance of the thing confessed does not invalidate confession, but the confessor must specify the details.

Contradiction Does Not Invalidate Confession
Explanation that a contradictory confession remains valid

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi principle that contradiction does not invalidate a confession and apply it to a simple case.

Core Idea
A contradictory confession remains valid; the confessor must explain the contradiction.

In Hanafi law, a confession (iqrar) is given significant weight. Even if the confessor's statement contains a contradiction, the confession is not automatically rejected. This lesson explains the principle from Al-Hidayah and shows how it works in practice.

Guided Path
1
State the Principle
Read the headline: 'Contradiction does not prevent the validity of a confession.' Memorise this as a key rule.
2
Understand the Example
The example given: if the defendant says 'This house was in the plaintiff's hand,' the house is given to the plaintiff. Even if the defendant's words contradict some other fact, the confession stands.
The reason cited: ignorance (jahalah) in the object of confession does not invalidate the confession.
3
Identify the Obligation
Although the confession is valid, the confessor must still explain the contradiction. This is consistent with the rule that if someone confesses to 'something', they must clarify what it is.
4
Apply the Ruling
Consider a similar scenario: a defendant says 'I owe Zayd 100 dirhams' but later says 'I owe him 50.' Under this principle, the confession to 100 is valid and Zayd is entitled to 100, unless the defendant explains the contradiction.

كتاب الرجوع عن الشهادات
(۷۲) التَّنَاقُضُ لَا يَمْنَعُ صِحَّةَ الْإِقْرَارِ .
يَعْنِي إِذَا قَالَ الْمُدَّعَى عَلَيْهِ هَذِهِ الدَّارُ كَانَتْ فِي يَدِ هَذَا الْمُدَّعِي دُفِعَتْ إِلَيْهِ، لِأَنَّ الْجَهَالَةَ فِى الْمُقَرِّ بِهِ لَا تَمْنَعُ صِحَّةَ الْإِقْرَارِ وَكَذَا إِذَا شَهِدَ شَاهِدَانِ بِإِقْرَارِ الْمُدَّعَى عَلَيْهِ بِذَلِكَ دُفِعَتْ إِلَيْهِ. (العناية: كتاب الشهادة، باب الاختلاف في الشهادة، فصل في الشهادة على الإرث، ج ص ۴۲۰
(وإن أقر بذلك المدعى عليه أى أقر بأن الدار في يد المدعى دفعت إلى المدعى، لأن الجهالة فى المقر به لا تمنع صحة الإقرار) بل يجب عليه بيانه كما لو أقر لفلان بشيء يجب عليه بيانه البناية: كتاب الشهادة، باب الاختلاف في الشهادة، فصل في الشهادة على الإرث، ج ۹ ص ۱۸۴)
الهداية: كتاب الرجوع عن الشهادات، ج ۳ ص ۱۸۱
Book of Retraction from Testimonies. (72) Contradiction does not prevent the validity of confession. Meaning, if the defendant says: 'This house was in the hand of this plaintiff' it is given to him, because ignorance in the thing confessed does not prevent the validity of confession. Similarly, if two witnesses testify to the defendant's confession of that, it is given to him. (From al-Inayah: Book of Testimony, Chapter of Disagreement in Testimony, Section on Testimony on Inheritance, volume? page 420) (And if the defendant confesses that, i.e., confesses that the house is in the plaintiff's hand, it is given to the plaintiff, because ignorance in the thing confessed does not prevent the validity of confession. Rather, it is obligatory upon him to explain it, just as if he confessed to something for someone, it is obligatory upon him to explain it. Al-Binayah: Book of Testimony, Chapter of Disagreement in Testimony, Section on Testimony on Inheritance, volume 9 page 184) Al-Hidayah: Book of Retraction from Testimonies, volume 3 page 181.

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement from the Book of Retraction from Testimonies (Kitab al-Ruju' 'an al-Shahadat) in al-Hidayah. The principle is: Contradiction (tanaqud) does not prevent the validity of a confession. The commentary explains that if the defendant makes a confession that contains a contradiction (e.g., saying 'This house was in the plaintiff's hand' while also making another inconsistent claim), the confession is still valid and the house will be handed over to the plaintiff. The reason given is the previous principle: ignorance in the thing confessed does not prevent validity. The defendant is still obliged to clarify the contradiction. This is consistent with the Hanafi approach that confessions are given weight; they are not easily dismissed due to inconsistency. The ruling is from the Zahir al-Riwayah.

Key Terms
التناقض (al-tanaqud): Contradiction in the confession, such as the defendant saying the house was in the plaintiff's hand while also implying something else.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) The confession is rejected because of contradiction.
B) The confession is valid and the house is given to the plaintiff.
C) The defendant must be cross-examined.
D) The case is dismissed.

Key Takeaway
A contradictory confession is valid; the confessor must explain the inconsistency.

Ignorance of the Subject Does Not Prevent Iqrar
Explaining that jahala does not invalidate iqrar

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that a confession (iqrar) is valid even when the subject is unspecified, and explain the rationale based on the principle that jahala in the muqarr bihi does not invalidate the iqrar.

Core Idea
A confession is valid even if the thing confessed is unknown — ignorance in the subject does not invalidate the iqrar.

This lesson focuses on a key Hanafi principle in the law of evidence: the validity of a confession (iqrar) does not require full specification of its subject. The passage from al-Hidayah illustrates this through a case where a defendant admits a house is in the plaintiff's possession without detailing the nature of that possession. The ruling is that the confession is valid and the house is returned, though the confessor is compelled to clarify. Understanding this principle helps you appreciate the Hanafi approach to iqrar as a strong form of proof.

Guided Path
1
Identify the case and the issue
Consider the scenario: plaintiff claims defendant has possession of a house but does not specify the type of possession (e.g., usurpation, lease). Defendant confesses that the house is in plaintiff's possession. What is the legal effect of the defendant's confession?
The issue is whether ignorance (jahala) about the nature of possession invalidates the confession.
2
State the Hanafi rule
The text states: 'al-jahalah fi al-muqarr bihi la tamna' sihhat al-iqrar' — ignorance about the thing confessed does not prevent the validity of the confession. This is the core principle. The confession is valid (sahih) despite the lack of specification.
This rule applies as long as the subject is identifiable; absolute impossibility is not considered here.
3
Apply the consequence
Because the confession is valid, the house is returned to the plaintiff. However, the confessor (defendant) is compelled to provide the details (e.g., type of possession). The same ruling applies if two witnesses testify to the confession without specifying the nature.
The judge enforces the confession but requires clarification from the confessor.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مگر مقر کو تفصیل پر مجبور کیا جائے گا۔
صاحب ہدایہ مذکورہ اصول ذکر کر کے یہ بتلارہے ہیں کہ اگر کسی نے کسی شخص پر مکان پر قبضہ کرنے کا دعوی کیا اور کس قسم کا قبضہ تھا اس کی وضاحت نہ کی ہو، اور مدعلی علیہ ( قابض ) نے اقرار بھی کر لیا کہ یہ مکان واقعی مدعی کے قبضہ میں تھا، تو یہ مکان مدعی کے قبضہ میں واپس دے دیا جائے گا، کیونکہ جس مکان کا اقرار کیا گیا وہ اگر چہ مجہول ہے، مگر یہ جہالت مقربہ میں ہے اور مقربہ کی جہالت اقرار کی صحت سے مانع نہیں ہے، اس لیے مدعلی علیہ کے اقرار کے مطابق مکان واپس مدعی کو دے دیا جائے ، البتہ مقر کو اس کی وضاحت پر پابند کیا جائے گا۔ اسی طرح اگر دو گواہان یہ گواہی دے دیں کہ مدعیٰ علیہ نے یہ اقرار کیا تھا کہ اس کے قبضہ میں موجود مکان مدعی کے ہاتھ میں ہے اور قابض (مدعی علیہ ) کے قبضہ کی نوعیت کی وضاحت بھی نہیں کی تب بھی اس مکان کا فیصلہ مدعی کے حق میں ہوگا۔

يَعْنِي إِذَا قَالَ الْمُدَّعَى عَلَيْهِ هَذِهِ الدَّارُ كَانَتْ فِي يَدِ هَذَا الْمُدَّعِي دُفِعَتْ إِلَيْهِ، لِأَنَّ الْجَهَالَةَ فِى الْمُقَرِّ بِهِ لَا تَمْنَعُ صِحَّةَ الْإِقْرَارِ وَكَذَا إِذَا شَهِدَ شَاهِدَانِ بِإِقْرَارِ الْمُدَّعَى عَلَيْهِ بِذَلِكَ دُفِعَتْ إِلَيْهِ. (العناية: كتاب الشهادة، باب الاختلاف في الشهادة، فصل في الشهادة على الإرث، ج ص ۴۲۰)
(وإن أقر بذلك المدعى عليه أى أقر بأن الدار في يد المدعى دفعت إلى المدعى، لأن الجهالة فى المقر به لا تمنع صحة الإقرار) بل يجب عليه بيانه كما لو أقر لفلان بشيء يجب عليه بيانه البناية: كتاب الشهادة، باب الاختلاف في الشهادة، فصل في الشهادة على الإرث، ج ۹ ص ۱۸۴)
But the confessor will be compelled to provide detail. The author of al-Hidayah, after mentioning the aforementioned principle, is explaining that if someone claims that another person took possession of a house but does not specify the type of possession, and the defendant (the possessor) confesses that the house was indeed in the plaintiff's possession, then the house will be returned to the plaintiff's possession. Because the house that was confessed to, although unknown, this ignorance is in the matter of possession (muqarrabah) and ignorance in muqarrabah does not prevent the validity of the confession. Therefore, according to the defendant's confession, the house will be given back to the plaintiff. However, the confessor will be bound to clarify it. Similarly, if two witnesses testify that the defendant had confessed that the house in his possession is in the plaintiff's hand, and they do not clarify the nature of the possessor's possession, even then the judgment for the house will be in favor of the plaintiff. Meaning, when the defendant says, 'This house was in the hand of this plaintiff,' it is given to him. Because ignorance about the thing confessed does not prevent the validity of the confession. And likewise, if two witnesses testify to the defendant's confession of that, it is given to him. (Al-'Inayah: Kitab al-Shahada, Bab al-Ikhtilaf fi al-Shahada, Fasl fi al-Shahada 'ala al-Irth, vol. 9, p. 420) And if the defendant confesses that, i.e., he confesses that the house is in the plaintiff's hand, it is given to the plaintiff, because ignorance about the thing confessed does not prevent the validity of the confession; rather, he must explain it, just as if he confessed to someone for something, he must explain it. (Al-Binayah: Kitab al-Shahada, Bab al-Ikhtilaf fi al-Shahada, Fasl fi al-Shahada 'ala al-Irth, vol. 9, p. 184)
Source pages p. 115

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement from the Hanafi school concerning the validity of an iqrar (confession) when the subject of the confession is not fully known. The author of al-Hidayah explains that if a plaintiff claims that the defendant is in possession of a house but does not specify the nature of that possession (e.g., usurpation, lease, etc.), and the defendant simply admits that the house is in the plaintiff's possession, the house is returned to the plaintiff. The reason given is that ignorance (jahala) about the thing confessed (muqarr bihi) does not prevent the validity of the iqrar. The jahala here is in the attribute (muqarrabah), not in the essence. The confessor is, however, compelled to clarify the details. The same ruling applies if two witnesses testify to the defendant's confession without specifying the nature of possession. This principle is grounded in the Hanafi view that iqrar is a form of testimony against oneself, and certainty in the subject is not a condition for validity; rather, it is sufficient that the subject is identifiable. The text cites al-'Inayah and al-Binayah as sources, both of which are standard commentaries on al-Hidayah.

Key Terms
الجَهَالَة (al-jahalah): Ignorance or lack of specification about the subject of confession (muqarr bihi).
المُقَرّ بِه (al-muqarr bihi): The thing or right that is confessed (iqrar is made about it).
الإِقْرَار (al-iqrar): A legal declaration or confession by a person against themselves, creating a binding obligation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school as explained in this passage, if a defendant confesses that a house is in the plaintiff's possession but does not specify the type of possession, what happens?
A) The confession is invalid because the subject is unknown.
B) The confession is valid and the house is returned, but the defendant must specify the type of possession.
C) The confession is valid only if two witnesses testify.
D) The house is not returned until the type of possession is clarified.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, a confession is valid even if the subject is unspecified; ignorance in the muqarr bihi does not invalidate iqrar.

Contradiction Does Not Prevent Validity of Iqrar
Stating that contradictory statements in iqrar do not invalidate it

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi principle that contradiction does not invalidate an iqrar, and apply it to determine the liability of witnesses who retract after a judgment.

Core Idea
Contradiction does not void a confession; a retraction itself may be a confession of liability.

In this passage from al-Hidayah, Imam al-Marghinani establishes a key principle of Hanafi fiqh: contradiction in a statement does not nullify the legal effect of an iqrar (confession). Although intuitive objections arise—if a statement is contradictory, how can it have legal force?—the principle is defended through a powerful qiyas (analogy). By the end of this lesson, you will understand why a witness who contradicts himself can still be held liable for damages, and you will be able to trace the reasoning from the well-known case of digging a well on a public road.

Guided Path
1
State the Principle
Read the opening statement: 'Contradiction does not prevent the validity of confession.' This is the core maxim. In Arabic: التناقض لا يمنع صحة الإقرار.
The principle is axiomatic in Hanafi law; it distinguishes between the statement itself and its subsequent contradiction.
2
Identify the Applied Case
The author applies it to witnesses who testify, the judge rules based on their testimony, and then they retract. Why is their retraction considered an iqrar? Because by retracting, they confess that they caused harm through false testimony.
The retraction is not just a void statement; it is an iqrar of liability.
3
Trace the Qiyas
The analogy: digging a well on a public road. Both cases involve indirect causation (tasbib) with transgression. The digger is liable even though the direct cause (falling into the well) is separate; similarly, the witnesses are liable even though the judge's ruling is the direct cause of loss.
The qiyas is khafi (subtle) because the connection is not immediately obvious.
4
Respond to the Objection
If someone objects that contradictory speech is void and thus cannot be the basis of liability, the Hanafi response is that contradiction does not affect the iqrar. The retraction is not the original testimony; it is a new iqrar.
The objection is anticipated and refuted directly by reasserting the principle.
5
Formulate the Ruling
The witnesses are liable for the property lost due to their testimony. The judge's ruling is not rescinded. The practical consequence: the witnesses must compensate the defendant.
This ruling ensures that plaintiffs are not left uncompensated due to witness retraction.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الرجوع عن الشهادات
(۷۲) التَّنَاقُضُ لَا يَمْنَعُ صِحَّةَ الْإِقْرَارِ .

ترجمہ: تناقض اقرار کی صحت کے لئے مانع نہیں ہے۔
تشریح: مذکور و اصول کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ اگر مقر کے کلام میں تناقض ہو، مثلاً پہلے ایک چیز کا اقرار کیا پھر اس سے رجوع کیا، تو اس تناقض سے اقرار کی صحت پر کوئی اثر نہیں پڑے گا بلکہ اقرار درست ہو گا۔ صاحب ہدایہ مذکورہ اصول ذکر کر کے یہ تلا ر ہے ہیں کہ اگر گواہوں نے مدعی علیہ کے خلاف گواہی دی اور قاضی نے ان کی شہادت پر مدعی علیہ کے خلاف فیصلہ کیا، پھر گواہوں نے اپنی گواہی سے رجوع کیا تو قاضی کا فیصلہ مسخ نہیں ہوگا، اور گواہوں پر اس مال کا مضمان آئے گا جو مال انہوں نے اپنی گواہی کی وجہ سے مدعی علیہ کا تلف کیا ہے، کیونکہ گواہوں کا اپنی گواہی سے رجوع کرنا اپنے حق میں سبب عمان کے وجوب کا اقرار ہے، نیز یہاں گواہ کے کلام میں اگر چہ تناقض ہے، لیکن تناقض اقرار کی صحت کے لئے مانع نہیں ہے، لہذ امذکورہ صورت میں بھی گواہوں کا تناقض ان کے اقرار کے لئے مانع نہ ہوگا اور ان پر ضمان لازم ہوگا۔

وَعَلَيْهِمْ ضَمَانُ مَا أَتْلَفُوهُ بِشَهَادَتِهِمْ لِإِقْرَارِهِمْ عَلَى أَنْفُسِهِمْ بِسَبَبِ الضَّمَانِ، فَقَضَاءُ الْقَاضِي وَإِنْ كَانَ عِلَّةَ لِلتَّلَفِ لَكِنَّهُ كَالْمَلْجَا مِنْ جِهَتِهِمْ، فَكَانَ التَّسْبِيبُ مِنْهُمْ تَعَدِّيَا فَيُضَافُ الْحُكْمُ إِلَيْهِمْ كَمَا فِى حَفْرِ الْبِثْرِ عَلَى قَارِعَةِ الطَّرِيقِ. فَإِنْ قِيلَ: كَلَامُهُمْ مُتَنَاقِضٌ وَذَلِكَ سَاقِطُ الْعِبْرَةِ فَعَلَامَ الضَّمَانُ؟ أَجَابَ بِقَوْلِهِ وَالسَّنَاقُضُ لَا يَمْنَعُ صِحَّةَ الْإِقْرَارِ. (العناية: كتاب الرجوع عن الشهادة، ج۷ ص ۴۷۹)
(وعليهم أى وعلى الشهود ضمان ما أتلفوه بشهادتهم لإقرارهم على أنفسهم بسبب الضمان فقضاه القاضي، وإن كان علة للتلف لكنه كالملجأ من جهتهم فكان السبب منهم تعديا، فيضاف الحكم إليهم كما في حفر البئر على قارعة الطريق والتناقض لا يمنع صحة الإقرار هذا جواب عما يقال كلامهم متناقض وذلك ساقط العبرة (البناية: كتاب الرجوع عن الشهود، ج ۹ ص ۲۰۰)
Book of Retraction from Testimonies. (72) Contradiction does not prevent the validity of confession. Translation: Contradiction is not a preventive for the validity of confession. Explanation: The meaning of the aforementioned principle is that if there is contradiction in the speech of the confessor, for example, he first confessed to something and then retracted it, then this contradiction will not affect the validity of the confession; rather, the confession will be valid. The author of al-Hidayah, after mentioning this principle, is explaining that if witnesses testified against the defendant and the judge decided against the defendant based on their testimony, then the witnesses retracted their testimony, the judge's decision will not be reversed, and the witnesses will be liable for the property they destroyed by their testimony, because their retraction of testimony is a confession upon themselves of the cause of liability. Moreover, although there is contradiction in the witnesses' statement, contradiction does not prevent the validity of confession. Therefore, in the mentioned case, the witnesses' contradiction will not prevent their confession, and they will be liable for damages. And upon them is the guarantee (daman) of what they destroyed by their testimony due to their confession upon themselves of the cause of liability. The judge's ruling, although it is the cause of the destruction, is like a resort from their side. So the causation (tasbib) from them was transgressive, so the ruling is attributed to them, as in the case of digging a well on the public road. If it is said: Their speech is contradictory and that is disregarded, so on what basis is there liability? He answered by saying: Contradiction does not prevent the validity of confession. (Al-'Inayah: Kitab al-Ruju' an al-Shahada, vol. 7, p. 479) And upon them, i.e., upon the witnesses, is the guarantee of what they destroyed by their testimony, due to their confession upon themselves of the cause of liability, so the judge's ruling, although it is the cause of destruction, is like a resort from their side, so the causation from them was transgressive, so the ruling is attributed to them, as in digging a well on the public road. And contradiction does not prevent the validity of confession. This is a response to the statement that their speech is contradictory and that is disregarded. (Al-Binayah: Kitab al-Ruju' an al-Shuhud, vol. 9, p. 200)
Source pages p. 115

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof from the Hanafi school regarding the effect of contradiction (tanaquḍ) on the validity of an iqrar (confession). The principle is stated at the beginning: 'Contradiction does not prevent the validity of confession' (التناقض لا يمنع صحة الإقرار). This means that if a person makes a confession and then contradicts himself (e.g., by retracting or making an inconsistent statement), the original confession remains valid and is not nullified by the contradiction. The author applies this principle to the case of witnesses who testify against a defendant, the judge rules based on their testimony, and then the witnesses retract. Their retraction is considered a confession that they caused harm, so they are liable for damages (daman). Their contradictory statements (first testimony, then retraction) do not invalidate the fact that they have confessed to causing loss. The proof is provided through qiyas (analogy): just as a person who digs a well on a public road is liable for harm caused because he created the danger, similarly, the witnesses, by giving testimony that led to a judgment, caused the loss, even though the direct cause is the judge's ruling. The judge's ruling is likened to a 'refuge' (malja) that is forced upon them; the true causation (tasbib) comes from the witnesses. The text also addresses an objection: if the witnesses' speech is contradictory and thus null, how can they be held liable? The answer is that contradiction does not prevent the validity of an iqrar (confession). Their retraction itself is an iqrar that they have done something wrong. This ruling is from the later part of al-Hidayah, Kitab al-Ruju' an al-Shahadat, and is supported by commentaries al-'Inayah and al-Binayah.

Key Terms
التَّنَاقُض (al-tanaquḍ): Contradiction in speech, such as making a statement and then retracting it or making a conflicting statement.
الضَّمَان (al-daman): Liability or guarantee to compensate for loss or damage caused.
التَّسْبِيب (al-tasbib): Indirect causation, where one creates a situation that leads to harm, even if not the direct cause.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, if witnesses testify and then retract after the judge has already given a ruling, what is the legal consequence?
A) The judge's ruling is reversed and the witnesses are not liable.
B) The judge's ruling stands and the witnesses are liable for damages.
C) The retraction is considered a new testimony that overrides the first.
D) The witnesses are penalized but not liable for the property.

Key Takeaway
Contradiction does not nullify an iqrar; a retraction can itself be a binding confession of liability.

Contradiction Does Not Invalidate Confession
States the principle that textual contradiction does not prevent validity of confession

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule that contradiction does not invalidate a confession, and apply it to the case of witnesses retracting their testimony.

Core Idea
A contradictory retraction of testimony is still a valid confession that obligates guarantee.

In this lesson, we examine a key principle in Hanafi law of testimony (shahādah): contradiction (tanāquḍ) within a person's statement does not automatically render it void. The passage from Al-Hidayah presents this rule in the context of witnesses who first testify and then retract after the judge's verdict. The retraction is considered a confession of liability for the loss caused by their testimony, and despite the contradiction, it remains valid. The ruling is supported by a qiyās (analogy) to digging a well on a public thoroughfare.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Ruling and Its Context
The passage states that witnesses who retract their testimony are liable for the loss they caused. The retraction itself is a confession of liability. Note that the judge's verdict is an intermediary cause, but the direct cause (tasbīb) is attributed to the witnesses because their initial testimony was transgressive.
The key is that the witnesses' act of testifying falsely was a transgression, so they are treated as direct causers.
2
Understand the Principle: Contradiction Does Not Invalidate Confession
An objection is raised: the witnesses' speech is contradictory (first they testify, then they retract), so it should be disregarded. The text answers with the principle: contradiction does not prevent the validity of a confession. The retraction is a confession of liability, and its validity is not harmed by the contradiction with the earlier testimony.
This principle is specific to confessions (iqrār). Contradiction in other types of statements may be treated differently.
3
Analyze the Proof: Analogy to Digging a Well
The text compares the witnesses' situation to someone who digs a well on a public road. If someone falls into it, the digger is liable because the act was transgressive. Similarly, the witnesses' false testimony caused the judge to issue a ruling, leading to loss. The judge's verdict is like the well – an intermediary – but the witnesses are the cause because their act was wrongful.
This is a qiyās: the 'illah (effective cause) is transgressive causation (ta'addī) leading to loss.
4
Apply the Rule to the Scenario
Given that the retraction is a valid confession, the witnesses must guarantee (ḍamān) the value of what was lost due to their testimony. The ruling is that the guarantee is wājib (obligatory) because they have confessed to causing the loss through transgression.
No distinction is made between the first testimony and the retraction; the retraction itself is the operative confession.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَعَلَيْهِمْ ضَمَانُ مَا أَتْلَفُوهُ بِشَهَادَتِهِمْ لِإِقْرَارِهِمْ عَلَى أَنْفُسِهِمْ بِسَبَبِ الضَّمَانِ، فَقَضَاءُ الْقَاضِي وَإِنْ كَانَ عِلَّةَ لِلتَّلَفِ لَكِنَّهُ كَالْمَلْجَا مِنْ جِهَتِهِمْ، فَكَانَ التَّسْبِيبُ مِنْهُمْ تَعَدِّيًا فَيُضَافُ الْحُكْمُ إِلَيْهِمْ كَمَا فِى حَفْرِ الْبِثْرِ عَلَى قَارِعَةِ الطَّرِيقِ. فَإِنْ قِيلَ: كَلَامُهُمْ مُتَنَاقِضٌ وَذَلِكَ سَاقِطُ الْعِبْرَةِ فَعَلَامَ الضَّمَانُ؟ أَجَابَ بِقَوْلِهِ وَالسَّنَاقُضُ لَا يَمْنَعُ صِحَّةَ الْإِقْرَارِ. (العناية: كتاب الرجوع عن الشهادة، ج۷ ص ٤٧٩) وعليهم أى وعلى الشهود ضمان ما أتلفوه بشهادتهم لإقرارهم على أنفسهم بسبب الضمان فقضاه القاضي، وإن كان علة للتلف لكنه كالملجأ من جهتهم فكان السبب منهم تعديا، فيضاف الحكم إليهم كما في حفر البئر على قارعة الطريق والتناقض لا يمنع صحة الإقرار هذا جواب عما يقال كلامهم متناقض وذلك ساقط العبرة (البناية: كتاب الرجوع عن الشهود، ج ٩ ص ٢٠٠)
And upon them is the guarantee of what they caused to be lost by their testimony, because of their confession against themselves concerning the cause of guarantee. So the judge's verdict, although it is the cause of the loss, is like a refuge from their side. Thus, the causation from them was transgressive, so the ruling is attributed to them, just as in digging a well on a public thoroughfare. If it is said: Their speech is contradictory, and that is disregarded, so why is the guarantee? He answered with his statement: And contradiction does not prevent the validity of confession. (Al-Inayah: Book of Retraction from Testimony, vol. 7, p. 479) And upon them, meaning upon the witnesses, is the guarantee of what they caused to be lost by their testimony, because of their confession against themselves concerning the cause of guarantee. The judge's verdict, although it is the cause of the loss, is like a refuge from their side. So the causation from them was transgressive, thus the ruling is attributed to them, just as in digging a well on a public thoroughfare. And contradiction does not prevent the validity of confession. This is an answer to what is said: their speech is contradictory and that is disregarded. (Al-Binayah: Book of Retraction from Testimony, vol. 9, p. 200)
Source pages p. 116

Commentary
This passage presents the principle that contradiction (tanāquḍ) does not invalidate a confession (iqrār). The context is witnesses who retract their testimony after the judge has already ruled based on it. The retraction is considered a confession of liability for the loss caused by their false testimony. The objection that their statement is contradictory (initial testimony then retraction) and thus should be disregarded is answered by this principle. The analogy of digging a well on a public road illustrates that causation from a transgressor makes them liable, even if an intermediary (like the judge's verdict) exists. The ruling is that the witnesses must guarantee (ḍamān) the value of what was lost due to their testimony, even though their retraction creates a contradiction.

Key Terms
التناقض (al-tanāquḍ): Contradiction in a person's statement, such as first affirming then denying.
الإقرار (al-iqrār): A confession or admission of a right or liability against oneself.
الضمان (al-ḍamān): Liability or guarantee to compensate for loss caused by one's action.
التسبيب (al-tasbīb): Indirect causation, where one's action sets in motion a chain leading to loss.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi principle discussed, what is the legal effect of a witness retracting their testimony after the judge's verdict?
A) The retraction nullifies the original testimony, and no liability arises.
B) The retraction is considered a valid confession of liability for the loss caused, despite the contradiction.
C) The retraction is only valid if made before the judge's verdict.
D) The retraction is invalid because it contradicts the first statement.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, a contradictory retraction of testimony is still a valid confession that obligates the witness to guarantee the loss caused by their original testimony.

Repentance Must Match the Crime: Retraction in Court
States the rule and provides two proofs for retraction in court.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule that retraction of false testimony must occur in the same court and explain its basis in faskh (annulment) and tawbah (repentance) proportionality.

Core Idea
A public crime requires public repentance: retraction of false testimony is valid only in the court where it was given.

This passage from Al-Hidayah establishes a key procedural rule for withdrawing false testimony. It combines two legal concepts: retraction as an annulment (faskh) of the original testimony, and as an act of repentance (tawbah) proportional to the crime. Understanding this rule is essential for anyone involved in Islamic judicial proceedings.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
The Hanafi position is that retraction of false testimony must be made in the same court (majlis al-ḥākim) where the testimony was originally given. This is a condition for validity.
The ruling is derived from two independent proofs.
2
Analyze the faskh analogy
Retraction is an annulment (faskh) of the testimony. Just as annulment of a sale requires the same conditions as the original sale (e.g., existence of the item, mutual consent), annulment of testimony requires the same forum.
Qiyas: asl = sale faskh, far = testimony retraction, illa = both are annulments.
3
Apply the tawbah principle
Repentance must be proportionate to the crime (al-tawbah ʿalā ḥasab al-jināyah). False testimony is a public crime in the courtroom, so repentance must be public in the same courtroom.
This principle is derived from Allah’s attribute of justice and the need for public vindication.
4
Note the cross-madhhab difference
Some schools may allow retraction elsewhere if properly recorded, but Hanafi insists on court presence to maintain public accountability and mirror the original act.
The Hanafi position is mufta bihi in the school.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الهداية كتاب الرجوع عن الشهاة، ح ٣ ص ١٨١ لأنَّهُ فَسْخٌ لِلشَّهَادَةِ فَيَخْتَصُّ بِمَا تَخْتَصُّ بِهِ الشَّهَادَةُ مِنْ مَجْلِسِ الْحَاكِمِ أَيِّ حَاكِمِ كَانَ كَالْفَسْحَ فِى بَابِ الْبَيْعِ حَيْثُ يُشْتَرَطُ لِصِحْتِهِ مَا يُشْتَرَطُ فِي الْبَيْعِ مِنْ قِيَامِ الْمَبِيعِ وَرِضًا الْمُتَبَايِعَيْنِ وَلأَنَّ الرُّجُوعَ عَنْ الشَّهَادَةِ تَوْبَةٌ عَمَّا أُرْتُكِبَ مِنْ قَوْلِ النُّورِ، وَالتَّوْبَةُ بِحَسَبِ الْجِنَايَةِ عَلَى فَإِذَا كَانَتْ الْجَرِيمَةُ بِحَضْرَةِ الْحَاكِمِ يَجِبُ أَنْ تَكُونَ تَوْبَتُهَا كَذَلِكَ، فَإِذَا كَانَ الرُّجُوعُ عِنْدَ غَيْرِهِ غَيْرَ صَحِيحٍ. تبيين الحقائق: كتاب الرجوع عن الشهادة، ج ٤ ص ٢٤٣ وَشَهَادَةُ النُّورِجِنَايَةً فِي مَجْلِسِ الْحُكْمِ فَالتَّوْبَةُ عَنْهَا تَتَقَيَّدُ بِهِ. (العناية : كتاب الرجوع عن الشهادة، ج ص ٤٨٠ ولأن الرجوع توبة) أى لأن الرجوع عن الشهادة توبة عن جناية الكذب
Al-Hidayah, Book of Retraction from Testimony, vol. 3, p. 181: Because it is an annulment (faskh) of testimony, so it is specific to what testimony is specific to, namely the court of the judge, any judge, just like annulment in the chapter of sale where for its validity what is required for sale is required: existence of the sold item and consent of the two parties. And because retraction from testimony is repentance (tawbah) from the falsehood committed, and repentance is according to the crime (al-tawbah 'alā hasab al-jināyah). So if the crime was in the presence of the judge, its repentance must also be so. Thus, if the retraction is before someone else, it is not valid. (Tabyīn al-Haqā'iq: Book of Retraction from Testimony, vol. 4, p. 243) And the testimony of falsehood is a crime in the courtroom, so repentance from it is restricted to it. (Al-Ināyah: Book of Retraction from Testimony, vol. 7, p. 480: And because retraction is repentance) Meaning because retraction from testimony is repentance from the crime of lying.
Source pages p. 117

Commentary
This passage explains why witnesses must retract their false testimony in the same court where they gave it. The retraction is an annulment (faskh) of the testimony, and just as testimony is specific to the courtroom, its annulment must also be there. An analogy is made to annulment in a sale contract, which requires the same conditions as the original sale. Further, the retraction is considered repentance (tawbah) for the crime of false testimony. Since the crime was committed in the judge's presence, repentance must also be public in that same place to be valid. This follows the principle that repentance must be proportional to the crime: a public crime requires public repentance.

Key Terms
التَّوْبَةُ عَلَى حَسَبِ الْجِنَايَةِ (al-tawbah 'alā hasab al-jināyah): Repentance must be proportionate to the crime; a public crime requires public repentance.
الرُّجُوعُ عَنِ الشَّهَادَةِ (al-rujū' 'an al-shahādah): Retraction or withdrawal of previously given testimony.
الفَسْخُ (al-faskh): Annulment or rescission of a legal act, here applied to testimony.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why must retraction of false testimony be made in the same court according to Hanafi law?
A) Because the judge needs to personally record the retraction.
B) Because retraction is both an annulment (faskh) and repentance (tawbah) that must mirror the original public act.
C) Because the witness must be scolded publicly.
D) Because only the court can authenticate the retraction.

Key Takeaway
Retraction of false testimony must be in the same court because it is both an annulment mirroring the original act and a repentance proportional to the public crime.

Repentance According to the Crime: Retraction Must Be in Court
Establishes principle that retraction of testimony must occur in judge's presence as repentance

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the principle that repentance matches the crime and apply it to derive the ruling that retraction of false testimony must occur in the judge's court.

Core Idea
Repentance must match the crime; open false testimony requires open retraction in court.

This lesson unpacks a core Hanafi legal principle: 'Repentance is according to the crime' (al-tawbah 'ala hasab al-jinayah). The author of Al-Hidayah uses this principle, along with qiyas (analogy) from the rescission of sale, to establish that witnesses who gave false testimony before a judge cannot validly retract it in private—they must do so in the same court. You will learn how the Hanafi school derives this rule and its practical implications.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is retraction (ruju') from testimony. The ruling is that it is wajib to perform this retraction before the judge; any retraction outside the court is invalid (ghayr sahih).
The ruling is not merely recommended—it is obligatory for legal validity.
2
Locate the dalil (evidence)
Two proofs are given: (1) Qiyas on rescission of sale (فسخ البيع)—just as rescission requires the same conditions as the original sale, annulling testimony requires the same forum as the original testimony. (2) The general principle that repentance corresponds to the crime—since false testimony was committed openly in court, repentance (retraction) must also be open in court.
The dalil is a combination of qiyas jali and a qa'ida kulliya.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah (how the dalil proves the ruling)
For the qiyas: the illa is 'annulment of a legal act'—both rescission and retraction dissolve a previous act, so they must share the same formal context. For the principle: the crime was committed in majlis al-hakim, so the tawbah must also take place there.
The court is the locus of both the crime and its remedy.
4
Note the ikhtilaf (scholarly difference)
The Hanafi position is that retraction must be before the judge. Some other schools may allow retraction elsewhere, but Hanafis hold this view as mufta bihi.
The Hanafi ruling is established in zahir al-riwayah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
اصول ہدایہ ثالث (۷۵) اَلتَّوْبَةُ عَلَى حَسَبِ الْجِنَايَةِ. ترجمہ: تو بہ بحسب جنایت ہوتی ہے۔ تشریح : مذکورہ اصول کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ جس قدر جرم ہو تو یہ بھی اسی جرم کے اعتبار سے ہوتی ہے، یعنی اگر جرم خفیہ ہے تو تو یہ بھی خفیہ اور اگر جرم اعلانیہ ہو تو تو یہ بھی اعلانیہ ہوگی۔ صاحب ہدایہ مذکورہ اصول ذکر کر کے یہ بتلا رہے ہیں کہ گواہوں کے لئے یہ جائز نہیں ہے کہ وہ قاضی کی مجلس سے علیحدہ ہو کر اپنی گواہی سے رجوع کریں بلکہ حاکم کی موجودگی میں اپنی گواہی سے رجوع کرنا ضروری ہے، کیونکہ گواہی سے رجوع کرنا گواہی کو مسخ کرنا ہے اور گواہی کا فتح خاص ہو گا اس مجلس کے ساتھ جس کے ساتھ شہادت خاص ہے اور شہادت مجلس قضاء کے ساتھ خاص ہے، لبد افتح شہادت بھی مجلس قضاء کے ساتھ خاص ہوگی۔ نیز گواہی سے رجوع کرنا تو بہ کرنا ہے اور تو بہ جرم کے اعتبار سے ہوتی ہے اور گواہوں نے چونکہ یہ جرم یعنی جھوٹی گواہی قاضی کی مجلس میں دی تھی لہذا تو یہ بھی مجلس قضاء میں علامیہ ہوگی ۔ الهداية كتاب الرجوع عن الشهاة، ح ۳ ص ۱۸۱ لأنَّهُ فَسْخٌ لِلشَّهَادَةِ فَيَخْتَصُّ بِمَا تَخْتَصُّ بِهِ الشَّهَادَةُ مِنْ مَجْلِسِ الْحَاكِمِ أَيِّ حَاكِمِ كَانَ كَالْفَسْحَ فِى بَابِ الْبَيْعِ حَيْثُ يُشْتَرَطُ لِصِحْتِهِ مَا يُشْتَرَطُ فِي الْبَيْعِ مِنْ قِيَامِ الْمَبِيعِ وَرِضًا الْمُتَبَايِعَيْنِ وَلأَنَّ الرُّجُوعَ عَنْ الشَّهَادَةِ تَوْبَةٌ عَمَّا أُرْتُكِبَ مِنْ قَوْلِ النُّورِ، وَالتَّوْبَةُ بِحَسَبِ الْجِنَايَةِ عَلَى فَإِذَا كَانَتْ الْجَرِيمَةُ بِحَضْرَةِ الْحَاكِمِ يَجِبُ أَنْ تَكُونَ تَوْبَتُهَا كَذَلِكَ، فَإِذَا كَانَ الرُّجُوعُ عِنْدَ غَيْرِهِ غَيْرَ صَحِيحٍ. تبيين الحقائق: كتاب الرجوع عن الشهادة، ج ۴ ص ۲۴۳ وَشَهَادَةُ النُّورِجِنَايَةً فِي مَجْلِسِ الْحُكْمِ فَالتَّوْبَةُ عَنْهَا تَتَقَيَّدُ بِهِ. (العناية : كتاب الرجوع عن الشهادة، ج ص ۴۸۰ ولأن الرجوع توبة) أى لأن الرجوع عن الشهادة توبة عن جناية الكذب
Usool e Hidayah Third (75) al-Tawbah 'ala hasab al-jinayah. Translation: Repentance is according to the crime. Explanation: The meaning of the aforementioned principle is that as much the crime is, the repentance is also according to that crime, i.e., if the crime is secret then repentance is also secret, and if the crime is open then repentance is also open. The author of Hidayah, after mentioning this principle, explains that it is not permissible for witnesses to retract their testimony away from the judge's court, rather it is necessary to retract in the presence of the ruler, because retracting testimony is annulling the testimony, and the annulment is specifically connected to the same court with which the testimony is specific, and testimony is specific to the court of judgment, therefore necessarily the testimony is also specific to the court of judgment. Also, retracting testimony is repentance, and repentance is according to the crime, and since the witnesses committed this crime i.e., false testimony in the judge's court, therefore this repentance will also be open in the court of judgment. Al-Hidayah Kitab al-Ruju' 'an al-Shahadah, vol. 3 p. 181: because it is annulment of testimony, so it is specific to what testimony is specific to from the court of the judge, any judge, like the annulment in the chapter of sale where for its validity are required what are required in sale from existence of the sold item and mutual consent of the contracting parties, and because retraction from testimony is repentance from what was committed of falsehood, and repentance is according to the crime, so when the crime was in the presence of the judge, it is obligatory that its repentance be likewise, so if the retraction is before other than him, it is not valid. Tabyin al-Haqa'iq: Kitab al-Ruju' 'an al-Shahadah, vol. 4 p. 243: And the testimony of falsehood is a crime in the court of judgment, so repentance from it is restricted to it. (Al-Inayah: Kitab al-Ruju' 'an al-Shahadah, vol. ? p. 480: And because retraction is repentance) i.e., because retraction from testimony is repentance from the crime of lying.
Source pages p. 117

Commentary
This passage presents a foundational legal principle (qa'ida) from the Hanafi school: 'Repentance is according to the crime.' The author uses this principle to derive a specific ruling in the chapter of retraction from testimony (رجوع عن الشهادة). The point is that witnesses who gave false testimony before a judge cannot validly retract their testimony in private or elsewhere; they must retract in the very same court where the false testimony was given. Why? Because retracting testimony is a form of repentance from the crime of lying in testimony, and repentance must correspond to the crime in terms of openness. If the false testimony was given openly in court, the repentance (retraction) must also be open in court. The author strengthens this by analogy (qiyas): just as rescinding a sale (فسخ البيع) requires the same conditions as the original sale (existence of the subject matter and mutual consent), so also annulling testimony (فسخ الشهادة) requires the same forum as the original testimony. The text cites Al-Hidayah, Tabyin al-Haqa'iq, and Al-Inayah to support this. The ruling is clear: retraction is invalid if done outside the judge's presence.

Key Terms
التوبة (al-tawbah): Repentance from sin; here specifically the act of retracting false testimony as a form of repentance.
الجناية (al-jinayah): The crime or offense; here specifically the crime of false testimony (شهادة الزور).
الرجوع عن الشهادة (al-ruju' 'an al-shahadah): Retraction of testimony; the act of a witness withdrawing their previously given statement.
مجلس الحكم (majlis al-hukm): The court or session of the judge (qadi) where legal proceedings take place.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the principle 'al-tawbah 'ala hasab al-jinayah', where must a witness retract their false testimony?
A) In any mosque
B) Before the same judge in whose court they testified
C) Immediately after leaving the court
D) At home in the presence of their family

Key Takeaway
Retraction of false testimony must be performed in the same court before the same judge to be legally valid, based on the principle that repentance matches the crime.

Proportional Validity of Witness Testimony After Retraction
Applies principle of proportional witness retraction

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule for witness retraction in property cases and apply it to determine the liability of retracting witnesses.

Core Idea
Only remaining witnesses count; the retractor loses their share and must compensate.

When a witness retracts after a judgment has been executed, the effect is not to void the entire testimony. Instead, the Hanafi school assesses the situation based on how many witnesses remain. This principle ensures that the truth is upheld proportionally and that retractors face financial liability for their reversal.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
The act is the retraction of a witness after judgment. The ruling: the retractor is liable for a share of the property proportional to the number of witnesses who retracted.
In Hanafi law, the retraction does not undo the entire judgment.
2
Locate the dalil
The dalil is the practice of the Companions and qiyas. The passage quotes al-Hidayah: 'Consideration is given to the remaining witnesses, not to the one who retracted.'
This is a juristic principle, not a direct Quranic or hadith text.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The right (haqq) is divisible by the number of witnesses. Each witness supports a portion of the claim. When one retracts, his portion is lost and he must compensate it.
The remaining witness's testimony continues to support half the right.
4
Note the practical consequence
If two witnesses testify and one retracts, the retractor pays half the property. If both retract, each pays half, and the judgment is effectively reversed.
The plaintiff does not have to return the property, as the remaining testimony still justifies half.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
اصول پر ایہ ثالث (۶) الْمُعْتَبَرُ فِى بَابِ الرُّجُوعِ بَقَاءُ مَنْ بَقِيَ لَا رُجُوعَ مَنْ رَجَعَ . ) ترجمہ : گواہی سے رجوع کے باب میں ماچھی گواہوں کا اعتبار ہوگا جنہوں نے رجوع کیا ان کا اعتبار نہیں ہوگا۔ تشریح : مذکورہ اصول کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ شہادت سے رجوع کے بعد دیکھا جائے گا کہ اگر تعداد پوری ہے تو پھر رجوع کرنے والوں پر ضمان نہیں آئے گا اور اگر ماضی کی تعداد پوری نہ ہو تو پھر رجوع کرنے والوں پر ضمان آئے گا۔ صاحب ہدایہ مذکورہ اصول ذکر کر کے یہ بتلا رہے ہیں کہ اگر دو گواہوں نے کسی شخص کے خلاف مال کے بابت گواہی دی اور قاضی نے مدعی کے حق میں فیصلہ کرتے ہوئے اس شخص سے مال لے کر مدعی کے حوالہ کر دیا ، پھر ان دو گواہوں میں سے ایک نے اپنی گواہی سے رجوع کیا تو وہ نصف مال کا ضامن ہوگا، کیونکہ مابقی ایک گواہ ہے اور مابقی کا اعتبار ہوتا ہے، لہذا جب ایک اپنی گواہی پر برقرار ہے تو جس نے رجوع کیا ہے اس پر نصف ضمان آئے گا، اور اپنی گواہی پر قائم رہنے والے کی گواہی چونکہ معتبر ہے اس لیے اس پر کوئی ضمان نہ ہوگا۔ والتوبة على حسب الجناية، فالسر بالسر، والإعلان بالإعلان فالشهادة كانت بالإعلان، والرجوع أيضا كذلك. (البناية: كتاب الرجوع عن الشهود، باب كيفية الرجوع عن الشهادة، ج ۹ ص ۲۰۱) الهداية: كتاب الرجوع عن الشهادات، ج ۳ ص ۱۸۲ وَالْعِبْرَةُ فِي الرُّجُوعِ بَقَاء من بَقِى من الشُّهُودَ لَا رُجُوع مِن رَجَعَ وَيبقى الحق يقدر بَقَاءِ الشُّهُود ويتلف بقدر مَا رَجَعَ إِذَا ثَبَت هَذَا الأَصْل تخرج عَلَيْهِ الْمَسَائِل إِذا شهد شَاهِدَانِ على رجل بِمَال وَقضى القَاضِي بذلك وَسلم المال إِلَى الْمُدَّعِي ثُمَّ رَجَعَ أَحدهما غرم نصف المَالِ لِأَنَّهُ بَقِي النِّصْفِ بِبَقَاءِ شَاهد واحد. (تحفة الفقهاء: كتاب الرجوع عن الشهادة، ج ۳ ص ۳۶۵)
Third principle on Usool (6) al-Mu'tabaru fi bab al-ruju'i baqa'u man baqiya la ruju'a man raja'a. Translation: In the chapter of retraction from testimony, consideration is given to the remaining witnesses; those who retracted are not considered. Explanation: The meaning of the aforementioned principle is that after retraction from testimony, it will be seen if the number (of remaining witnesses) is sufficient, then the retractors will not be liable, and if the number of remaining is not sufficient, then the retractors will be liable. The author of Hidayah, after mentioning this principle, explains that if two witnesses testified against a person concerning property, and the judge, ruling in favor of the plaintiff, took the property from that person and handed it over to the plaintiff, then one of these two witnesses retracted his testimony, then that witness will be liable for half the property, because the remaining [witness] is one, and consideration is given to the remaining. So when one remains on his testimony, the one who retracted will be liable for half, and since the testimony of the one who remains is valid, he will not be liable for anything. And repentance is according to the crime: the secret with the secret, and the open with the open. The testimony was open, and the retraction is also thus. (al-Binayah: Kitab al-Ruju' 'an al-Shuhud, Bab Kayfiyyat al-Ruju' 'an al-Shahadah, vol. 9 p. 201) al-Hidayah: Kitab al-Ruju' 'an al-Shahadat, vol. 3 p. 182: And consideration in retraction is given to the remaining of the witnesses, not to the one who retracted. And the right remains according to the remaining witnesses and is lost according to what is retracted. When this principle is established, the issues are derived from it. If two witnesses testified against a man concerning property and the judge ruled accordingly and paid the property to the plaintiff, then one of them retracted, he pays half the property because half remained by the stay of one witness. (Tuhfat al-Fuqaha': Kitab al-Ruju' 'an al-Shahadah, vol. 3 p. 365)
Source pages p. 118

Commentary
This passage introduces another key principle in the Hanafi law of testimony retraction: 'Consideration in retraction is given to the remaining witnesses, not to those who retracted.' The principle determines liability (ضمان) for the retracting witness. The classic case: two witnesses testify to a debt, judgment is given, property transferred. If one later retracts, he must compensate half the value because the remaining witness still supports the claim. The author connects this to the earlier principle of repentance matching the crime: since the testimony was public, the retraction is also public. The ruling is derived from Al-Hidayah and supported by Al-Binayah and Tuhfat al-Fuqaha'. The Hanafi position: the retraction only affects the share corresponding to the retracting witness; the remaining witness's testimony maintains half the right.

Key Terms
بقاء من بقي (baqa'u man baqiya): The remaining (witnesses) who have not retracted; their testimony continues to be valid.
ضمان (daman): Liability or guarantee; here the retracting witness must compensate the value of the lost testimony's share.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If two witnesses testify for a plaintiff, judgment is given, then one witness retracts. What is the liability of the retracting witness?
A) He pays the entire amount
B) He pays half the amount
C) No liability because retraction is allowed
D) He pays nothing if the remaining witness is credible

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, witness retraction only affects the share of the retracting witness; the judgment remains valid proportionally.

Guarantee Requires Equivalence: The Case of Retracting Witnesses in Marriage
Explaining the legal maxim that guarantee requires equivalence, applied to witnesses retracting testimony in marriage.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi maxim 'al-tadmeen yastad'ee al-mumathalah' to determine liability in witness retraction cases and distinguish between loss of tangible objects and benefits.

Core Idea
No guarantee without equivalence—benefits have no like, so witnesses are not liable for retracting marriage testimony.

The Hanafi law of guarantee (daman) is built on a core principle: liability requires equivalence between the lost item and the compensation. This principle, known as 'al-tadmeen yastad'ee al-mumathalah', is applied in Al-Hidayah to a specific case: witnesses who testify about a marriage and later retract their testimony. The key question is whether they must compensate the woman for the loss of the usufruct of her private part (manafi' al-bud'). Understanding this application helps you see how Hanafi jurists reason from a general maxim to a specific ruling, and why they treat benefits differently from tangible objects.

Guided Path
1
State the maxim
The maxim 'al-tadmeen yastad'ee al-mumathalah' means guarantee requires equivalence. This is a foundational rule in Hanafi daman.
The maxim is a qawida derived from istiqra' of Shariah.
2
Identify the case
Witnesses testify that a woman married with a proper dower, then retract. The woman loses the usufruct of her private part (the benefit of sexual relationship in marriage).
The loss is not the dower amount but the benefit itself.
3
Classify the lost item
The lost thing is a benefit (manfa'ah), not a tangible object ('ayn). In Hanafi fiqh, benefits do not have an exact equivalent (mithl) because they are not goods that can be measured or replaced.
Tangible objects have mithl; benefits like usufruct do not.
4
Apply the maxim
Since guarantee requires equivalence, and benefits lack an equivalent, the witnesses are not liable. The loss is irreplaceable in kind, so no compensation is due.
This holds whether the dower stated was equal to the proper dower or less.
5
Note the cross-madhhab dispute
Imam al-Shafi'i holds that witnesses are liable, likely considering benefits as having value. The difference stems from whether benefits can have an equivalent for guarantee.
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf; each school follows its own usul.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۷۷) اَلتَّضْمِينُ يَسْتَدْعِي الْمُمَاثَلَةَ .
ترجمہ: ضامن بنا نا مماثلت کا تقاضا کرتا ہے۔
۱۱۹
تشریح: مذکورہ اصول کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ ضمان کے لئے ضروری ہے کہ جس شے کا انسان ضامن بنایا جائے اس میں اور مضمون بہ میں مماثلت ہو، اگر وہ شے مضمون بہ کی مماثل نہ ہو تو ضمان ساقط ہو جاتا ہے۔ صاحب خدا یہ مذکورہ اصول ذکر کر کے یہ بتلارہے ہیں کہ اگر گواہوں نے کسی عورت کے خلاف گواہی دی کہ اس نے فلاں کے ساتھ مہر مثل پر نکاح کیا ہے، پھر بعد میں گواہوں نے اپنی گواہی سے رجوع کیا تو ان گواہوں پر ضمان نہیں آئے گا، کیونکہ گواہوں نے اپنی گواہی کے ذریعے صرف عورت کے منافع بضعہ کو تلف کیا ہے اور اس کا مثل نہیں ہے، کیونکہ ضمان مماثلت کا تقاضا کرتا ہے، اور مذکورہ صورت میں تلف شدہ منافع بضعہ اور گواہوں کی طرف سے بطورِ ضمان دیا جانے والا مال کے درمیان مماثلت نہیں ، لہذا یہاں بھی رجوع کرنے سے گواہوں پر ضمان نہیں ہوگا۔ عین اور منفعت یعنی منافع بضعہ کے درمیان کوئی مماثلت نہیں ہے۔
قوله وإن رجع أحدهما ضمن النصف والأصل أن المعتبر بقاء من بقى لا رجوع من رجع وقد بقى من يبقى بشهادته نصف الحق. (الجوهرة النيرة كتاب الرجوع عن الشهادة، ج ۲ ص ۲۳۷)
(وإن رجع أحدهما ضمن (النصف والأصل أن المعتبر في هذا بقاء من بقي، لا رجوع من رجع، وقد بقى من يتقى بشهادته نصف الحق. اللباب في شرح الكتاب: كتاب الرجوع عن الشهادة، ج ۳ ص ۷۲)
الهداية: كتاب الرجوع عن الشهادات ، ج ۳ ص
وَإِنْ شَهِدَ عَلَى امْرَأَةٍ بِالنِّكَاحِ ثُمَّ رَجَعَا فَلَا ضَمَانَ عَلَيْهِمَا، سَوَاءٌ كَانَتِ الشَّهَادَةُ بِمِقْدَارِ مَهْرٍ مِثْلِهَا أَوْ بِأَقَلَّ مِنْ ذَلِكَ، لِأَنَّ الْمُتَلَفَ هَاهُنَا مَنَافِعُ الْبُضْعِ وَمَنَافِعُ الْبُضْعِ
Translation: Guarantee requires similarity. Explanation: This principle means that for guarantee, it is necessary that the thing for which one is made a guarantor and the guaranteed thing have similarity; if the thing is not similar to the guaranteed thing, the guarantee becomes void. The author of Hidayah, by mentioning this principle, explains that if witnesses testify against a woman that she married someone with a proper dower (mahr mithl), then later retract, they are not liable, because through their testimony they only destroyed the woman's usufruct of her private part (manafi' al-bud'), and it has no equivalent, since guarantee requires similarity, and in this case there is no similarity between the destroyed usufruct and the wealth given as guarantee. So here too, retracting does not make them liable. There is no similarity between an object ('ayn) and a benefit (manfa'ah), i.e., the usufruct of the private part. The saying: 'If one of them retracts, he guarantees half, and the basis is that what is considered is the persistence of the one who remains, not the retraction of the one who retracts...' (Al-Jawharah al-Nayyirah, Bab al-Ruju' 'an al-Shahadah, vol. 2, p. 237) (Al-Lubab fi Sharh al-Kitab, Kitab al-Ruju' 'an al-Shahadah, vol. 3, p. 72) Al-Hidayah: Kitab al-Ruju' 'an al-Shahadat, vol. 3, p. And if they testify against a woman for marriage then retract, there is no guarantee upon them, whether the testimony was for the amount of her proper dower or less, because the lost thing here is the usufructs of the private part and the usufructs of the private part…
Source pages p. 119

Commentary
This passage presents a legal maxim (qawida) from the Hanafi school: 'Guarantee requires equivalence' (al-tadmeen yastad'ee al-mumathalah). The commentator explains that for a guarantee to be valid, the thing guaranteed must be similar in kind to what is lost. If there is no similarity, the guarantee falls. The specific application is from the chapter on retraction of testimony (Kitab al-Ruju' 'an al-Shahadah). When witnesses testify that a woman married with a proper dower and then retract, they are not liable for damages because the loss they caused is the usufruct of her private part (manafi' al-bud'), which is a benefit (manfa'ah), not a tangible object ('ayn). The Hanafi position is that there is no equivalent for benefits in terms of guarantee, so no compensation is due. The passage cites Al-Jawharah al-Nayyirah and Al-Lubab to support the sub-rule that if one witness retracts, he guarantees half, but the base principle remains that the retraction does not impose liability when the loss is a benefit. The Hidayah text reinforces that the witnesses are not liable regardless of the dower amount stated, because the thing lost is the usufructs of the private part, which have no exact equivalent.

Key Terms
التضمين (al-tadmeen): The act of making someone a guarantor (damin); guarantee, liability.
المماثلة (al-mumathalah): Equivalence, similarity in kind and value between the guaranteed thing and the loss.
منافع البضع (manafi' al-bud'): The usufruct of the private part, i.e., the benefit derived from sexual intercourse, which is a benefit (manfa'ah) not a tangible object.
ضمان (daman): Guarantee, liability to compensate for loss.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the principle 'al-tadmeen yastad'ee al-mumathalah', why do witnesses who testify about a marriage and retract not face liability?
A) Because retraction is allowed in marriage cases.
B) Because the loss caused is a benefit (manfa'ah), which has no equivalent (mumathalah).
C) Because the witnesses did not directly destroy the woman's property.
D) Because the testimony was about a marriage, not a financial transaction.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi law of guarantee hinges on equivalence; benefits without a like do not trigger liability, even when caused by wrongful retraction of testimony.

The Principle: Evidence is for Affirmation
States the principle that evidence is for proof, not negation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the principle that evidence is for affirmation to determine which party's witnesses are accepted in disputes over price or quantity in sales.

Core Idea
Evidence proves claims of increase, not absence—the affirmatory nature of bayyinah.

A fundamental rule in Islamic evidence law states that evidence (bayyinah) is designed to affirm (ithbat) the existence of a fact, not to disprove a claim. This principle resolves many practical disputes, especially when both parties in a sale present witnesses. This lesson unpacks the rule and its application through concrete examples from al-Hidayah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Principle
State the maxim 'al-bayyinatu li al-ithbat' and recognize it as a guiding rule for accepting evidence.
2
Apply to a Price Dispute
If buyer claims price is 1000 and seller claims 2000, both with witnesses, determine whose witnesses affirm an increase (seller's). Accept them.
The party claiming the higher amount is affirming a fact beyond the other's claim.
3
Apply to a Quantity Dispute
If seller claims 5 kg and buyer claims 10 kg, both with witnesses, accept the witnesses claiming the larger quantity (buyer's) because they affirm an increase.
The principle consistently favors the party whose evidence affirms more.
4
Understand the Procedural Rule
When a plaintiff has witnesses present, the defendant may be asked to provide a surety for three days to prevent absconding, showing how the principle is implemented in court procedure.
This is a related but distinct rule from al-Hidayah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الْبَيِّنَاتُ لِلإِثْبَاتِ .
ترجمہ: گواہ اثبات کے لئے ہوتے ہیں۔
تشریح: مذکورہ اصول کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ گواہ کسی شے کو ثابت کرنے کے لئے ہوتے ہیں نفی کے لئے نہیں ہوتے ، لہذا جس کے گواہ زیادتی کو ثابت کرنے والے ہوں گے وہی معتبر ہوں گے۔ صاحب ہدایہ مذکورہ اصول ذکر کر کے یہ بتا رہے ہیں کہ اگر بائع اور مشتری دونوں نے صحیح پائن کی مقدار میں اختلاف کیا، مثلا مشتری (۱۰۰۰) روپے شمن بتائے اور بائع (۲۰۰۰) بتلائے ، اسی طرح بائع (۵) کلو گندم مبیع ہونے کا دعویدار ہو اور مشتری (۱۰) کلو گندم مبیع ہونے کا دعویدار ہو اور دونوں نے اپنے اپنے گواہ پیش کر دئیے ہوں، تو جس کے گواہ زیادتی ثابت کرنے والے ہیں انہی کی گواہی قبول ہوگی، کیونکہ بینات کو اثبات کے لیے وضع کیا گیا ہے، اس لیے جس کا گواہ زیادتی کے لیے مثبت ہوگا وہی معتبر ہوگا، یعنی پہلی صورت میں بائع کے گواہ اور دوسری صورت میں مشتری کے گواہ معتبر ہوں گے اور چونکہ جو لِلْمُدَّعِي وَضَرَرُ الْمُدَّعَى عَلَيْهِ بِهِ يَسِيرٌ فَيُتَحَمَّلُ كَالْإِعْدَاءِ وَالْحَيْلُولَةُ بَيْنَهُ وَبَيْنَ أشغاله. (العناية: باب اليمين، ج۸ ص ۱۹۳)
وإذا قال المدعى لى بينة حاضرة في المصر (قيل لخصمه: أعطه كفيلا بنفسك ثلاثة أيام لئلا يغيب نفسه فيضيع حقه، والكفالة بالنفس جائزة عندنا وأخذ الكفيل لمجرد الدعوى استحسان عندنا لأن فيه نظرا للمدعى، وليس فيه كثير ضرر بالمدعى عليه. اللباب) في شرح الكتاب: كتاب الدعوى، ج ۴ ص ۳۷) الهداية كتاب الدعوى باب التحالف، ج ۳ ص ۲۱۷
Evidence (bayyinat) are for affirmation (ithbat). Translation: Witnesses are for affirmation. Explanation: The meaning of the mentioned principle is that witnesses are for proving something, not for negation. Therefore, whoever's witnesses prove an increase, they will be acceptable. The author of al-Hidayah, after mentioning this principle, is explaining that if the seller and buyer both differ in the amount of the correct price, e.g., the buyer says 1000 rupees as the price and the seller says 2000, similarly the seller claims 5 kg of wheat as the sold commodity and the buyer claims 10 kg as the sold commodity, and both present their witnesses, then whoever's witnesses prove the increase, their testimony will be accepted. Because evidence is established for affirmation, so whichever witness is positive for the increase will be reliable. Thus, in the first example, the seller's witnesses, and in the second, the buyer's witnesses will be accepted. And because the ruling is for the plaintiff and the harm to the defendant is slight, it is bearable, like transgression and prevention from his occupations. (Al-Inayah: Bab al-Yamin, vol. 8, p. 193) And if the plaintiff says, "I have witnesses present in the city," (he is told to his opponent: "Give him a surety for yourself for three days, lest he disappear and his right be lost." And kafalah bi al-nafs is permissible in our view, and taking a surety for mere claim is by istihsan in our view, because it contains consideration for the plaintiff and there is not much harm on the defendant. Al-Lubab in Sharh al-Kitab: Kitab al-Da'wa, vol. 4, p. 37) Al-Hidayah: Kitab al-Da'wa, Bab al-Tahaluf, vol. 3, p. 217
Source pages p. 132

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement establishing a fundamental principle of Islamic evidence law: evidence (bayyinat) are for affirmation (ithbat), not for negation. This means that witnesses are called upon to prove the existence of a fact, not to disprove a claim. The commentary illustrates this with examples from sales disputes: if the buyer and seller disagree on the price (1000 vs. 2000) or the quantity (5 kg vs. 10 kg), and both have witnesses, the witnesses of the party claiming the higher amount (affirming the increase) are accepted. This is because evidence is designed to affirm, and the party with the higher claim is the one asserting a positive fact. The text then quotes from al-Hidayah a related procedural rule: when the plaintiff claims that his witnesses are present, the defendant may be asked to provide a surety for himself for three days. This is permissible (kafalah bi al-nafs) and is justified by istihsan, as it protects the plaintiff's right without severe harm to the defendant.

Key Terms
بينة (bayyinah): Evidence, typically witness testimony, but can include other proofs in a broader sense.
إثبات (ithbat): Affirmation; establishing the existence of a fact or right.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In a dispute over the price of a commodity, the buyer says the price is 1000 and brings witnesses, while the seller says it is 2000 and brings witnesses. Whose witnesses will be accepted according to this principle?
A) The buyer's witnesses
B) The seller's witnesses
C) Both are accepted
D) Neither is accepted

Key Takeaway
Evidence (bayyinat) is only for proving what is claimed to exist, not for disproving a claim, and in disputes, the party whose evidence affirms a higher or greater fact prevails.

The Obligation to Act on Testimonies as Much as Possible
States the principle of obligatory action on testimonies with an example.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi principle regarding acting on two testimonies and apply it to a case where testimonies conflict with possession.

Core Idea
Testimonies must be given effect as much as possible, even against apparent possession.

This lesson introduces a fundamental rule in Islamic evidence law: when two valid testimonies are presented, the judge is obligated to act on them to the maximum extent possible. Even if the testimonies appear to contradict other evidence like possession, the judge must attempt to harmonize them. This principle ensures that witness testimony is not lightly disregarded.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
Read the opening Arabic phrase: it states that acting on the two testimonies is obligatory (wajib). Note the qualifier 'as much as possible' (mā amkan).
The ruling is wajib on the judge, not just recommended.
2
Understand the scope
The commentary applies the principle to a specific scenario: husband and wife dispute ownership of household items. Both testimonies are given, but the rule says items suitable for both (utensils, gold, etc.) belong to the man because possession is with him, unless the item is specific to the woman.
This illustrates how testimonies are reconciled with the possession rule.
3
Analyze the interaction
When testimonies conflict with apparent possession, the judge must try to give effect to both. If the item is suitable for both, the testimonies are interpreted in light of possession. If the item is specific to the woman, her testimony may prevail over the husband's possession.
The principle prioritizes testimonies but does not nullify possession entirely.
4
Apply to new cases
Consider a case where two witnesses testify that a car belongs to X, but X's brother is in possession. The judge should accept the testimonies unless the brother provides evidence of ownership or the testimonies are contradicted by stronger proof.
The principle is general and applies to all claims.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۹۳) يَجِبُ الْعَمَلُ بِالشَّهَادَتَيْنِ مَا أَمْكَنَ .) ترجمہ: شہادتوں پر حتی الامکان عمل کرنا واجب ہے۔ (وَمَا يَصْلُحُ لَهُمَا كَالْآنِيَةِ) وَالذَّهَبِ وَالْفِضَّةِ وَالْامْتِعَةِ وَالْعَقَارِ فَهُوَ لِلرَّجُلِ لَّانَّ الْمَرْأَةَ وَمَا فِي يَدِهَا فِي يَدِ الزَّوْجِ، وَالْقَوْلُ فِي الدَّعَاوَى لِصَاحِبِ الْيَدِ) بِخِلَافِ مَا يَخْتَصُّ بِهَا لِأَنَّهُ يُعَارِضُ ظَاهِرَ الزَّوْحِ بِالْيَدِ. (رد المحتار مع الدر المختار كتاب الدعوى باب التحالف، ج ۵ ص ۵۶۴) الهداية كتاب الدعوى، باب ما يدعيه الرجلان، ج ۳ ص ۲۲۵
(93) It is obligatory to act on the two testimonies as much as possible. Translation: Acting on testimonies is obligatory as much as possible. (And what is suitable for both of them, like utensils, gold, silver, goods, and real estate, it belongs to the man because the woman and what is in her hand are in the hand of the husband, and the word in claims is for the possessor) unlike what is specific to her because it contradicts the apparent ownership of the husband through possession. Commentary
This passage presents a fundamental rule in the law of evidence: when two testimonies (i.e., two witnesses) are available, the judge must act on them to the extent possible, even if it requires harmonizing apparent contradictions. The commentary then repeats the example from the previous lesson about husband-wife property disputes, showing how the principle of acting on testimonies interacts with the possession rule. The Arabic quotes here serve as a reminder that even when testimonies conflict with apparent possession, the testimonies should be given effect if possible, but the possession rule may prevail in certain cases.

Key Terms
شهادتین (shahadatayn): Two testimonies; the testimony of two witnesses.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, judges must give effect to two testimonies as much as possible, harmonizing them with possession rules.

Shahadat — Testimony
