Reconciling Conflicting Testimonies: The Ruling of Tansif
A Hanafi ruling on reconciling conflicting testimonies by dividing the property equally.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule for conflicting testimonies in a property dispute and explain why the property is divided equally.

Core Idea
When two valid testimonies conflict, divide the property equally to act on both.

This lesson explains a key Hanafi principle in judicial proceedings: if two plaintiffs present valid witnesses for the same property held by a third party, the judge does not reject either testimony. Instead, he splits the property equally. This ruling is based on the obligation to act on testimonies as far as possible, a principle derived from the need to honor legal proofs when truth is hidden.

Guided Path
1
Identify the legal scenario
Two plaintiffs each bring witnesses claiming ownership of a property in a third party's possession. The testimonies appear contradictory.
The property is not claimed by the possessor; it is held by someone else.
2
Recognize the principle
The matn states: 'It is obligatory to act on the two testimonies as much as possible.' This is a wajib obligation.
The principle prioritizes reconciling testimonies over rejecting them.
3
Understand the reasoning
Both testimonies can be valid: one witness saw a purchase (cause of ownership), the other saw possession (also a cause). Since ownership is hidden, both testimonies are plausible.
The judge does not assume one is lying; certainty of falsehood is not established.
4
Apply the solution
Since the property is divisible and both claimants are equal in their cause of entitlement, the solution is equal division (tansif).
This acts on both testimonies fully in a divided sense.
5
Note the epistemological point
The validity of a testimony does not depend on actual ownership; it depends on the witness's perception of a cause. Thus both testimonies are accepted.
This is a rational (aqli) proof based on the unseen nature of ownership.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب ما يدعيه الرجلان
(۹۳) يَجِبُ الْعَمَلُ بِالشَّهَادَتَيْنِ مَا أَمْكَنَ . )
ترجمہ: شہادتوں پر حتی الامکان عمل کرنا واجب ہے۔
اصول ہدایہ ثالث
۱۳۹
تشریح : مذکورہ اصول کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ جہاں تک ہو سکے جانبین کے گواہوں کی گواہی پر عمل کرنا واجب ہے، کیونکہ شاہد ان کی شہادت حجت ہے۔ صاحب ہدایہ مذکورہ اصول ذکر کر کے یہ بتلارہے ہیں کہ اگر دو آدمیوں نے کسی ایسی چیز کا دعوی کیا جو کسی تیسرے آدمی کے قبضہ میں ہے اور مدعی میں سے ہر ایک نے گواہ قائم کئے تو اس چیز کا ان کے درمیان نصف نصف کا فیصلہ کیا جائے گا، کیونکہ یہاں دو شہادتیں ہیں اور دونوں مقبول ہیں، کیونکہ دونوں نے ایسی گواہی دی ہے جو قبول کی جاسکتی ہے، مثلاً ایک گواہ نے خریداری دیکھ کر گواہی دی جو سبب ملک ہے اور دوسرے نے قبضہ کی بنیاد پر گواہی دی، اس حوالے سے دونوں گواہی صحیح ہیں، اور صحیح شہادتوں پر حتی الامکان عمل کرنا واجب ہوگا، لہذا مذکورہ صورت میں بھی حتی الامکان دونوں شہادتوں پر عمل کرنا واجب ہے اور اس کی بہترین صورت تنصیف کا فیصلہ ہے۔
وَلَا نُسَلِّمُ كَذِبَ أَحَدِهِمَا بِيَقِينِ لَّانَّ الْمُطْلَقَ لِلشَّهَادَةِ فِي حَقٌّ كُلِّ وَاحِدٍ مِنْهُمَا مُحْتَمَلُ الْوُجُودِ، فَإِنَّ صِحَّةَ أَدَاءِ الشَّهَادَةِ لَا تَعْتَمِدُ وُجُودَ الْمِلْكِ حَقِيقَةٌ لِأَنَّ ذَلِكَ غَيْبٌ لَا يَطَّلِعُ عَلَيْهِ الْعِبَادُ فَجَازَ أَنْ يَكُونَ أَحَدُهُمَا اعْتَمَدَ سَبَبَ الْمِلْكِ بِأَنْ رَآهُ يَشْتَرِى فَشَهِدَ عَلَى ذَلِكَ، وَالْآخَرُ اعْتَمَدَ الْيَدَ فَشَهِدَ عَلَى ذَلِكَ فَكَانَتْ الشَّهَادَتَانِ صَحِيحَتَيْنِ فَيَجِبُ الْعَمَلُ بِهِمَا مَا أَمْكَنَ، وَقَدْ أَمْكَنَ بِالنَّصْنِيفِ بَيْنَهُمَا لِكَوْنِ الْمَحَلِّ قَابِلًا وَتَسَاوِيهِمَا فِي سَبَبِ الاسْتِحْقَاقِ .
(العناية: كتاب الدعوى، باب ما يدعيه الرجلان، ج۸ ص ۲۴۶) وَلانَّ الْمُطْلَقَ لِلشَّهَادَةِ فِي حَقِّ كُلِّ وَاحِدٍ مِنْهُمَا يَحْتَمِلُ الْوُجُوهَ بِأَنْ يَعْتَمِدَ أَحَدُهُمَا سَبَبَ الْمِلْكِ وَالْآخَرُ الْيَدَ فَصَحْتِ الشَّهَادَتَانِ فَيَجِبُ الْعَمَلُ بِهِمَا مَا أَمْكَنَ وَقَدُ أَمْكَنَ بِالتَّنْصِيفِ إِذِ الْمَحَلُّ يَقْبَلُهُ وَإِنَّمَا يُنَصَّفُ لِاسْتِوَائِهِمَا فِي سَبَبِ الاسْتِحْقَاقِ .
(البحر الرائق: كتاب الدعوى، باب دعوى الرجلين، ج ص ۲۳۴)
Chapter of what two men claim. (93) It is obligatory to act on the two testimonies as much as possible. (Translation: It is obligatory to act on testimonies as much as possible.) Usool-e-Hidayah Third Volume 139. Explanation: The meaning of the mentioned principle is that it is obligatory to act on the testimony of witnesses from both sides as far as possible, because the testimony of witnesses is proof. The author of al-Hidayah, by mentioning this principle, is explaining that if two people claim something that is in the possession of a third person, and each of the plaintiffs brings witnesses, then the item will be adjudicated half and half between them, because here there are two testimonies and both are accepted, because both gave testimony that can be accepted. For example, one witness testified based on seeing a purchase, which is a cause of ownership, and the other testified based on possession. In this regard, both testimonies are valid, and it is obligatory to act on valid testimonies as much as possible. So in this case too, it is obligatory to act on both testimonies as much as possible, and the best form of that is the ruling of dividing equally. And we do not accept the lying of one of them with certainty, because the absolute [validity] of testimony for each of them is possible of existence. Indeed, the validity of delivering testimony does not depend on the actual existence of ownership, because that is unseen which people cannot know. So it is possible that one of them relied on a cause of ownership, such as seeing him buy, so he testified on that, and the other relied on possession, so he testified on that. Thus both testimonies are valid, and it is obligatory to act on them as much as possible, and it is possible by dividing equally between them because the place is divisible and they are equal in the cause of entitlement. (al-'Inayah: Kitab al-Da'wa, Bab Ma Yadde'ihi al-Rajulan, vol. 8, p. 246) And because the absolute [validity] of testimony for each of them can have various aspects, such that one relied on a cause of ownership and the other on possession, so both testimonies are valid, and it is obligatory to act on them as much as possible, and it is possible by dividing equally, since the place accepts it, and it is divided equally due to their equality in the cause of entitlement. (al-Bahr al-Raiq: Kitab al-Da'wa, Bab Da'wa al-Rajulayn, vol. ?, p. 234)
Source pages p. 138

Commentary
This passage presents a Hanafi ruling on conflicting testimonies in a property dispute. The principle is that it is wajib (obligatory) to act on both testimonies if possible. When two plaintiffs claim the same property owned by someone else, and each brings witnesses, the judge cannot reject one testimony outright. Instead, he divides the property equally between the two claimants. The reasoning is that both testimonies can be true: one witness may testify based on a purchase (cause of ownership) and the other based on possession (also a cause). Since ownership is hidden, we cannot definitively know which is false. Therefore, to reconcile both, the property is split. This is an application of istihsan (juristic preference) based on maslaha (public interest) of doing justice. The Arabic quotes from 'Inayah and Bahr al-Raiq emphasize that the validity of testimony does not depend on actual ownership, so both testimonies are valid and must be acted upon by giving half to each.

Key Terms
شھادت (shahādat): Testimony given by a witness in court.
تنصیف (tanṣīf): Dividing the property equally between the two claimants as a means to act on both testimonies.
سبب ملک (sabab al-milk): A cause of ownership, such as purchase (buying) as witnessed in the example.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
When two plaintiffs each present witnesses for the same property held by a third person, how does the Hanafi school rule?
A) The property is given to the one with stronger proof
B) Both testimonies are rejected due to contradiction
C) The property is divided equally between the two claimants
D) The property is given to the possessor

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi rule is to reconcile conflicting testimonies by dividing the disputed property equally when both testimonies are valid and the property is divisible.
